Why the Oath in Qasama is Taken by the Accused
Explains why oath in qasama cannot establish entitlement to blood-money

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rational argument for why the oath in qasama is taken from the defendant, not the plaintiff, and apply the principle that oaths are for defense, not entitlement.

Core Idea
The oath is for defense, not entitlement — so it cannot establish the guardian's right to blood-money.

This lesson presents the Hanafi rational argument (dalīl 'aqlī) for a key rule in qasama: the oath (yamin) is taken by the people of the neighborhood (the accused) to deny involvement, not by the guardian (the plaintiff) to claim blood-money. The passage uses a logical a fortiori (awlā) reasoning based on the function of oaths in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The ruling concerns the taking of the oath in qasama. The Hanafi position is that the oath is taken by the accused (people of the neighborhood) to deny involvement, not by the guardian to establish entitlement to blood-money or qisas.
2
State the key principle
The principle: 'al-yamin hujjat li al-daf' lā li al-istihqāq' — the oath is a proof for defense, not for entitlement.
This is a foundational legal maxim in Hanafi law regarding oaths.
3
Apply the principle to the guardian
The guardian's need is for entitlement (istihqāq) to blood-money, not for defense. Therefore, the oath cannot serve his purpose.
4
Use the a fortiori argument
Even property (māl mutabaddal) cannot be established by an oath; since the protected life (nafs muḥtarama) is greater in status, it follows a fortiori that an oath cannot establish entitlement to blood.
This is a qiyās al-awlā (a fortiori analogy).
5
Conclude the Hanafi rule
Therefore, in Hanafi qasama, the oath is only administered to the accused parties (people of the neighborhood), not to the guardian.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احناف کی عقلی دلیل
ولأن اليمين حجة للدفع دون الاستحقاق وحاجة الولى إلى الاستحقاق ولهذا لايستحق بيمينه المال المتبدل فأولى أن لا يستحق به النفس المحترمة ترجمہ اور اسلئے کہ یمین حجت ہے دفع مضرت کیلئے نہ کہ استحقاق کیلئے اور ولی کی حاجت استحقاق کی جانب ہے اور اسی وجہ سے مدقق کی یمین سے وہ مال مستحق نہیں ہوتا جو متبدل ہے (صرف کر دیا جاتا ہے ) پس بدرجہ اولی یہ بات ہوگی کہ یمین سے نفس محترم کا استحقاق نہ ہو سکے۔
تشریح یمین صرف اہل محلہ کا فریضہ ہوگا نہ کہ اولیاء کا اسلئے کہ ہمیں وہاں ہوتی ہے جس کا مقصد دفع ہو استحقاق نہ ہو اور یہاں مدعی کا مقصد دفع مضرت نہیں بلکہ استحقاق ہے پھر یہ بات بھی واضح ہے کہ نفس کا مقام مال سے بڑھا ہوا ہے اور یمین سے مال کا ثبوت نہیں ہوتا تو نفس محترم کا استحقاق بدرجہ اولی ثابت نہ ہوگا۔
And because the oath is a proof for defense, not for entitlement, and the guardian's need is for entitlement, therefore by his oath the property that is exchangeable is not established, so a fortiori the protected life is not established by it. Translation: And because the oath is a proof for repelling harm, not for entitlement, and the guardian's need is towards entitlement, and for this reason by the oath of the plaintiff [؟] that property which is exchangeable (spent) is not established, then a fortiori it will be that by oath the entitlement to the protected life cannot be established. Commentary: The oath will be only the duty of the people of the neighborhood, not of the guardians, because the oath is used where the purpose is defense, not entitlement, and here the plaintiff's purpose is not defense but entitlement. Also it is clear that the status of life is greater than property, and by oath property is not established, so entitlement to the protected life is a fortiori not established.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rational argument for why the oath (yamin) in qasama is taken from the people of the neighborhood, not from the guardian (wali). The key principle is that the oath is a proof (ḥujja) for defense (daf‘) against harm, not for establishing entitlement (istihqāq). The guardian seeks entitlement (to the blood-money or qisas), so his oath cannot serve that purpose. Furthermore, since an oath cannot even establish entitlement to property (māl mutabaddal), it follows a fortiori (awlā) that it cannot establish entitlement to a protected life (nafs muḥtarama). The commentary clarifies that the oath is only to confirm the defendant's claim of innocence; here the plaintiff wants to prove guilt, so the oath is not suited for that.

Key Terms
یمین (yamin): Oath sworn by the defendant (people of the neighborhood) to deny involvement in killing
حجة للدفع (hujjat li al-daf‘): Proof used for defense against a claim, not for establishing a right
استحقاق (istihqāq): Entitlement to a right, such as blood-money or qisas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rational argument, why can the guardian's oath not establish entitlement to blood-money?
A) Because the oath is only valid for the defendant, not the plaintiff.
B) Because the oath is a proof for defense, not for entitlement, and even property cannot be claimed by oath.
C) Because the guardian is not a resident of the neighborhood.
D) Because blood-money is a divinely prescribed punishment.

Key Takeaway
The oath in qasama is a defensive tool for the accused, not a means for the guardian to prove entitlement.

Guardian's Right to Select Fifty Men for Qasama Oath
Explains guardian's choice of fifty men for qasama oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the guardian selects the fifty men for qasama, explain the rationale based on the oath being the guardian's right, and distinguish between conditions for oath and testimony by applying the rule that a blind or ḥadd-punished person may still swear.

Core Idea
The guardian selects the fifty oath-takers; even a blind or ḥadd-punished person may swear because it is an oath, not testimony.

In qasama (compurgation for murder without witnesses), the guardian of the victim has the right to select fifty men from the neighborhood to swear that they did not kill nor know the killer. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind that right and clarifies why the oath is accepted even from individuals ordinarily barred from testimony, such as the blind or those punished for false accusation (qadhf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the core ruling: the guardian (walī) has the right to select (yatakhayyaruhum) the fifty men who will take the qasama oath.
This is based on the phrase 'يتخيرهم الولي' in the text.
2
Understand the rationale
The oath (yamīn) is the guardian's right; therefore, the guardian chooses those who will swear.
The benefit of the oath is that refusal (nukūl) resolves the case or that the righteous avoid false oaths.
3
Distinguish oath from testimony
Testimony (shahāda) has strict conditions (e.g., sight, integrity); an oath (yamīn) does not. Hence, a blind person or one punished for qadhf (whose testimony is rejected) can still swear.
The text explicitly says: 'لأنه يمين وليست بشهادة' (because it is an oath, not testimony).
4
Apply to edge cases
The guardian may even select a blind or ḥadd-punished person; the oath is valid and the case proceeds.
This is permissible despite such persons being ineligible as witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بشهادة وقوله "يتخيرهم الولى " إشارة إلى أن خيار تعيين الخمسين إلى الولى؛ لأن اليمين حقه والظاهر أنه يختار من يتهمه بالقتل أو صالحي أهل المحلة لما أن تحرزهم عن اليمين الكاذبة أبلغ التحرز فيظهر القاتل وفائدة اليمين النكول فإن كانوا لا يباشرون ويعلمون يفيد يمين الصالح على العلم بأبلغ مما يفيد يمين الطالح ولو اختاروا أعمى أو محدودا في قذف جائز لأنه يمين ولي ترجمہ اور قدوری کا قول "يتخيرهم الولی اشارہ ہے اس بات کی جانب کہ پچاس کی تعیین کا خیار ولی کو ہے اسلئے کہ یمین اس کا حق ہے اور ظاہر یہ ہے کہ وہ اسکو اختیار کر یگا جس کو وہ قتل کیساتھ متہم پائیگا یا محلہ کے نیک لوگوں کو اسلئے کہ ان کا ( صلحاء کا ) جھوٹی قسم سے بچنا کامل بیچنا ہو گا تو قاتل ظاہر ہو جائے گا اور یمین کا فائدہ انکار کرنا ہے ( تو مطلوب ہی حاصل ہو جائیگا ) پس اگر اہل محلہ نے قتل نہ کیا ہو اور وہ قاتل کو جانتے ہوں تو جاننے پر صالح کی بیمین اس سے زیادہ فائدہ دے گی جو بد کار کی بیمین فائدہ دے گی اور اگر اولیاء نے نابينا يا محدود فى القذف کو اختیار کیا ہو تو جائز ہے اس لئے کہ یمین ہے اور شہادت نہیں ہے۔۔ تشریح اہل محلہ میں سے پچاس آدمیوں کو منتخب کرنے کا حق ولی کو ہوگا کیونکہ یمین اولیا ء ہی کا حق ہے تو یہ اختیار بھی اسی کو ملے گا کیونکہ وہ ایسے افراد کومنتخب کرے گا جن کو وہ اپنے گمان میں متہم بالقتل جانتا ہے تو اس سے قاتل کا ظہور جلدی ہوگا اور یمین کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ اگر انھوں نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو مسئلہ ہی حل ہو جائے گا یا ولی محلہ کے نیک لوگوں کو منتخب کریگا کیونکہ ان کے بارے میں یہ خیال غالب ہے کہ یہ جھوٹ نہیں بولیں گے بلکہ سچ بولیں گے اور اس سے جلدی قاتل کا ظہور ہوگا پھر اگر ان لوگوں نے قتل نہ کیا ہو لیکن قاتل کو جانتے ہوں تو قاتل جاننے کے بارے میں نیک لوگوں کی شہادت سے جو مجرم کے اندر پختگی پیدا ہوگی وہ بدکاروں کی شہادت سے حاصل نہ ہو سکے گی۔ اور اگر اولیاء نے جن لوگوں کو اختیار کیا ہے ان میں سے کوئی اندھایا محدود فی القذف ہو تو بھنی جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ یمین ہے شہادت نہیں ہے۔
With testimony and his statement: 'The guardian selects them' is an indication that the choice of appointing the fifty is for the guardian; because the oath is his right. And it is apparent that he will choose the one he suspects of the killing or the righteous people of the neighborhood, because their avoidance of false oath is more complete, so the killer will appear. The benefit of the oath is refusal (nukūl). If they did not directly kill but they know, the oath of the righteous regarding knowledge benefits more than the oath of the wicked. And if they chose a blind person or one who received hadd for qadhf, it is permissible because it is an oath, not testimony. And if the guardians chose a blind person or one who received hadd for qadhf, it is permissible because it is an oath, not testimony. Commentary: The guardian has the right to select fifty men from the neighborhood because the oath is his right. He will choose those he suspects or the righteous. If they refuse to swear, the case is resolved. Even if the selected person is blind or has been punished for false accusation, it is valid because it is an oath, not testimony.

Commentary
This passage explains the guardian's right to select the fifty men from the neighborhood who will take the oath in qasama. The guardian chooses based on his suspicion of the killer or selects righteous people because they are more cautious about false oaths. The purpose of the oath is to make the killer appear or to elicit a refusal (nukūl), which settles the case. Even if the selected person is blind or has been punished for false accusation (ḥadd al-qadhf), the oath is valid because it is an oath, not testimony (shahāda). The commentary elaborates that the guardian's choice is his right, and he will naturally pick those most likely to know the truth.

Key Terms
یتخیرهم الولی (yatakhayyaruhum al-walī): The guardian has the right to select the fifty men from the neighborhood for the qasama oath
محدود فی القذف (mamdūd fī al-qadhf): A person who has received the prescribed punishment for false accusation of adultery
یمین (yamin): Oath sworn by the selected men to deny knowledge or involvement in killing

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because such persons are more truthful.
B) Because the qasama oath is a form of testimony, and they are eligible witnesses.
C) Because the qasama oath is an oath, not testimony, and therefore the strict conditions of testimony do not apply.
D) Because the guardian has no other option.

Key Takeaway
The guardian selects the fifty men for qasama, and even those disqualified from testimony (blind or ḥadd-punished) may swear because it is an oath, not testimony.

Dispute on Diyah Obligation After Qasama Oath
Disagreement between Hanafis and Shafi'is on diyah obligation after qasama oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on diyah after qasama and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using textual and rational evidence.

Core Idea
The qasama oath drops qisas but diyah remains obligatory on the neighborhood in Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson examines the disagreement between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i on the effect of the qasama oath. While both schools agree that the oath prevents qisas, they differ on whether diyah (blood-money) remains obligatory. The Hanafi position, supported by prophetic practice and the actions of Umar (ra), holds that diyah is due from the neighborhood. Imam al-Shafi'i, relying on a different hadith and a general principle of oaths, argues for complete exoneration.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
When the fifty men from the neighborhood swear the qasama oath, judgment is given for diyah against the neighborhood. The guardian is not required to swear.
This is the position of the Hanafi school as stated by al-Quduri.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proofs
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that no liability remains after the oath. His evidence: (1) the hadith 'tabri'ukum al-yahud' (the Jews are cleared by their oaths), and (2) the rational principle that oaths in shari'ah exonerate the defendant, not impose liability.
The Shafi'i argument relies on both textual and rational proofs.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response interprets 'tabri'ukum' restrictively: it means exemption from qisas and imprisonment only, not from diyah. Furthermore, the Prophet (peace be upon him) combined qasama and diyah in the hadith of Sahl ibn Abi Hathma and that of Ziyad ibn Abi Maryam. Umar (ra) also combined them in a case of the tribe of Wadi'a.
The Hanafis use multiple narrations to show that the oath does not eliminate financial liability.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi law, the victim's heirs receive diyah from the neighborhood; under Shafi'i law, they receive nothing after the oath.
This difference has significant implications for justice and compensation.
5
Conclude with the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon because it is supported by multiple authentic narrations and the practice of the early caliphs. The Shafi'i evidence is interpreted in a way that does not contradict these stronger proofs.
The tarjih is based on the preponderance of evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسامت کے سلسلے میں امام ابوحنیفہ کا دعوی اور امام شافعی کی دلیل نقلی و عقلی
قال فإذا حلفوا قضى على أهل المحلة بالدية ولا يستحلف الولى وقال الشافعى لا تجب الدية لقوله عليه السلام في حديث عبد الله بن سهل رضى الله عنه تبرئكم اليهود بأيمانها ولأن اليمين عهدت فى الشرع . للمدعى عليه لاملزما كما في سائر الدعاوى
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا پس جب کہ انہوں نے قسم کھالی تو اہل محلہ پر دیت کا فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا اور ولی سے حلف نہیں لیا جائے گا اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ دیت واجب نہ ہوگی عبداللہ بن سہل کی حدیث میں نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ یہود تم سے بری ہو جائیں گے اپنی قسموں کی وجہ سے اور اس لئے کہ یمین شریعت میں معہود ہے اس حال میں کہ وہ مدعی علیہ کو بری کرنے والی ہے نہ کہ لازم کرنے والی جیسے تمام دعاوی میں۔ تشریح جب اہل محلہ میں سے پچاس آدمیوں نے قسم کھالی تو ان سے قصاص ساقط ہو کر ان پر دیت واجب ہو جائے گی یہ ہمارا مذہب ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک اب اہلِ محلہ پر کوئی مضمان واجب نہیں رہا نہ قصاص اور نہ دیت اس بارے میں امام شافعی نے دو دلیلیں بیان کی ہیں : -1 حدیث مذکورہ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب یہود قسم کھا لیں گے تو وہ اب تم سے بری ہو جائیں گے اور ان پر عمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ دوسری ان کی دلیل عقلی ہے، فرماتے ہیں کہ شریعت میں جہاں یمین مشروع ہے اس کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ مدنی علیہ مدعی کے حق سے بری ہو جائے نہ یہ کہ مدعی کا حق مدعی علیہ کے حلف کے باوجود مدعی علیہ پر لازم ہو جائے ، تمام دعاوی میں یہی حال ہے لہذا قسامت میں بھی یوں ہی ہوگا۔
امام اعظم کی دلیل اور امام شافعی کے مستدلات میں سے پہلی دلیل کا جواب
ولنا أن النبي عليه السلام جمع بين الدية والقسامة فى حديث سهل وفي حديث زياد بن أبى مريم وكذا جمع عمر رضى الله عنه بينهما على وادعة وقوله عليه السلام تبرئكم اليهود محمول على الإبراء عن القصاص والحبس
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے سہل کی حدیث میں دیت اور قسامت کے درمیان جمع کیا اور زیاد بن ابو مریم کی حدیث میں اور ایسے ہی حضرت عمر نے دیت اور قسامت کے درمیان جمع کیا قبیلہ وادعہ پر اور نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان تبرئكم اليهود قصاص اور گرفتاری سے بری کرنے پر محمول ہے۔ تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے کہ حلف کے بعد اہل محلہ پر دیت کیوں واجب ہے، تو اولا سہل کے واقعہ کا حوالہ دیا جس میں قسامت اور دیت کو جمع کیا گیا ہے اس حدیث کے راوی سہل بن ابی حشمہ ہیں اور ایسے ہی زیاد بن ابی مریم کی حدیث میں دونوں کو جمع کیا گیا ہے اور اسی طرح قبیلہ کہد ان کی ایک شاخ وادعہ میں یہ واقعہ پیش آیا تو فاروق اعظم نے بھی قسامت اور دیت کو جمع فرمایا تھا۔ یہ یہاں تک تو ہمارے دلائل میں آگے امام شافعی کے مستدلات کا جواب ہے ان کی دلیل اوّل کا یہ جواب دیا گیا ہے کہ حدیث
Regarding the claim of Imam Abu Hanifa and the textual and rational evidence of Imam Shafi'i in the matter of qasama: He (Quduri) said: When they have sworn, judgment is given against the people of the neighborhood for the diya, and the guardian is not made to swear. Imam Shafi'i said: The diya is not obligatory because of his statement (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Abdullah ibn Sahl (may Allah be pleased with him): 'The Jews are cleared by their oaths,' and because the oath is established in the Shari'ah as absolving the defendant, not as imposing, as in all other claims. ... Our evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) combined between diya and qasama in the hadith of Sahl and in the hadith of Ziyad ibn Abi Maryam, and similarly Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) combined between them for the tribe of Wadi'a. And his statement (peace be upon him) 'tabri'ukum al-yahud' is interpreted as exemption from qisas and imprisonment.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage presents the disagreement (ikhtilāf) between the Ḥanafī school and Imām al-Shāfi‘ī regarding the consequence of the qasāma oath. According to the Ḥanafīs, when the fifty men from the neighborhood swear that they did not kill and do not know the killer, the diya (blood-money) becomes obligatory upon the people of the neighborhood. The guardian is not required to swear. Imām al-Shāfi‘ī holds that no liability remains — neither qisās nor diya — based on the ḥadīth of ‘Abdullāh ibn Sahl: 'The Jews are cleared of responsibility by their oaths,' and on the general principle that oaths exonerate the defendant. The Ḥanafī response cites other narrations (from Sahl ibn Abī Ḥathma and Ziyād ibn Abī Maryam) and the practice of ‘Umar (raḍiyallāhu ‘anh) where diya and qasāma were combined. The ḥadīth 'tabri'ukum' is interpreted as exemption from qisās and imprisonment, not from diya.

Key Terms
دیت (diya): Blood-money paid to the heirs of the victim in cases of homicide where qisas is not applicable
یمین (yamin): Oath taken by fifty men from the neighborhood in qasama to deny involvement
تبرئكم اليهود (tabri'ukum al-yahud): Hadith phrase: 'The Jews are cleared by their oaths' – interpreted by Hanafis as exemption from qisas and imprisonment only

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi response to Imam al-Shafi'i's use of the hadith 'tabri'ukum al-yahud'?
A) They accept it fully and agree no diya is due.
B) They argue the hadith is weak.
C) They interpret it as exemption only from qisas and imprisonment, not from diya.
D) They say it applies only to Jews.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the qasama oath drops qisas but does not prevent the obligation of diyah on the neighborhood.

Completing Fifty Oaths in Qasamah with Repetition
Provides procedure for repeating oaths to reach fifty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that oaths must be repeated on available individuals to reach fifty in qasamah, and explain the evidence from the practice of Caliph Umar.

Core Idea
When oath-takers are fewer than fifty, repetition is wajib to fulfill the Sunnah requirement.

This lesson examines the Hanafi procedure for qasamah when the local community has fewer than fifty adult men. The key question is how to fulfill the requirement of fifty oaths. The Hanafi school permits repetition of oaths on the same individuals, based on the practice of Caliph Umar and other early authorities.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and condition
Identify that when the number of eligible men from the locality is less than fifty, the judge repeats the oaths on those present until the count of fifty is reached.
2
Examine the evidence from Umar
Analyze the narration that Caliph Umar had only forty-nine men and repeated the oath on one of them to complete fifty, then he ordered payment of diyah.
3
Understand the legal reasoning
Recognize that fifty oaths are wajib by the Sunnah, so completing them is obligatory as much as possible; one does not need to identify a specific benefit beyond the Sunnah's authority.
4
Apply the principle of necessity
Explain that repetition is only allowed out of necessity to complete the number; if the full fifty are available, repetition is not permitted.
5
Contrast with the case of complete number
Note that if the guardian wants to repeat oaths when fifty men are present, he has no right, as the necessity for repetition is absent.

Source Text

تشریح ماقبل میں کہا گیا ہے کہ اہل محلہ میں سے پچاس شخصوں سے قسم لیجائے گی تو اگر اتفاق سے پچاس کی تعداد پوری نہ ہو سکے تو افراد موجودہ سے مکر رقم لیجائے تا کہ پچاس کی تعداد پوری ہو سکے حضرت عمر اور قاضی شریح اور حضرت ابراہیم حنفی سے ایسے منقول ہے۔ اور چونکہ پچاس کا عدد حدیث سے ثابت ہے تو بقدر امکان اسکا اتمام واجب ہے اور اس کی صورت یہاں یہی ہے جو مذکور ہوئی ہے۔ سوال اس تکرار سے کیا فائدہ ہے ؟ جواب اس چکر میں پڑنا غلط ہے بس یہاں ثبوت کے لئے اتنی بات کافی ہے کہ یہ سنت سے ثابت ہے اور اگر کچھ فائدہ نہ معلوم ہوتو یہ فائدہ کچھ ہے ہی کہ اس میں خون کے معاملے کو بہت بھاری اور عظیم معاملہ سمجھا جاتا ہے۔ اگر پچاس کا عدد پورا ہے اس کے باوجود ولی چاہتا ہے کہ ان میں سے کسی ایک سے قسم مکرر لیجائے تو ولی کو اس کا حق نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ یمین میں تکرار بر بناء ضرورت تھا اور اصول مسلم ہے کہ "الضرورة تتقدر بقدر الضرورۃ" اور یہاں کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
He said: And if the people of the locality are not complete, the oaths are repeated upon them until fifty are completed, because it is narrated that when Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) gave judgment in qasamah, forty-nine men came to him, so he repeated the oath upon one of them until fifty were completed, then he gave judgment with the diyah. And from Shuraih and al-Nakha'i (may Allah be pleased with them) similar is narrated. And because fifty are obligatory by the Sunnah, so completing them is obligatory as much as possible, and one is not required to look into the benefit because it is established by the Sunnah. Then in it there is a consideration of the gravity of blood. So if the number is complete, and the guardian wants to repeat upon one of them, that is not allowed for him, because resorting to repetition is due to the necessity of completion. Translation: Quduri said: And if the number of the people of the locality is not complete, the oaths are repeated upon them until fifty are completed, because it is narrated that when Umar (RA) gave judgment in qasamah, forty-nine men came to him, so he repeated the oath upon one of them until fifty were completed, then he gave judgment with the diyah. And from Shuraih and al-Nakha'i (RA) similar is narrated. And because fifty are wajib by hadith, so their completion is wajib as much as possible, and one is not asked to know the benefit because it is established by the Sunnah. Then in it there is viewing the matter of blood as great. So if the number is complete, and the guardian intends to repeat the oath upon any one of them, he does not have that right, because resorting to repetition is due to the necessity of completion. Explanation: In the previous discussion, it was said that fifty men from the locality will take oaths. So if by chance the number of fifty cannot be completed, the oaths are repeated upon the available individuals so that the number of fifty may be completed. This is narrated from Umar, Qadi Shuraih, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. And since the number of fifty is established by hadith, its completion is wajib to the extent possible, and this is the method mentioned. Question: What benefit is there in this repetition? Answer: It is wrong to delve into this; it is sufficient that it is established by the Sunnah. And if no benefit is known, then there is this benefit: that the matter of blood is considered very grave and great. If the number of fifty is complete, and despite that the guardian wants to take a repeated oath from one of them, then the guardian does not have the right, because repetition in oaths was based on necessity, and the accepted principle is 'Necessity is measured according to its extent,' and here there is no necessity.

Commentary
This passage provides the method for completing the fifty oaths required in qasamah when the local community has fewer than fifty men. The author states that the oaths are repeated on the available individuals until fifty is reached. This is based on the practice of Caliph Umar, who repeated the oath on one of forty-nine men to complete the number. Similarly, the judges Shuraih and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i followed this. The reason is that fifty oaths are required by the Sunnah, so it is obligatory to complete them as much as possible. One does not need to understand the wisdom behind the number; it is sufficient that it is from the Sunnah, and it emphasizes the gravity of bloodshed. If the number of available oath-takers is fifty or more, the guardian may not repeat the oath on any of them, because repetition is only allowed out of necessity.

Key Terms
قسامة (qasamah): Procedure involving oaths from the locality when a murder victim is found.
يمين (yamin): Oath
تكرار (takrar): Repetition of oath on the same person to complete the required number.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because it is required by the Sunnah to complete fifty
C) To give more chances to the accused
D) To follow the practice of Shuraih

Key Takeaway
Repetition of oaths in qasamah is a wajib concession to fulfill the Sunnah requirement of fifty oaths when the community is small.

General Principle on Repetition of Qasamah and Diyah
States a general principle to avoid repetition of qasamah/diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general principle for avoiding repetition of qasamah and diyah when body parts are found at different times, and apply the same principle to janazah prayer.

Core Idea
Qasamah and diyah are not repeated for the same murder; obligation attaches only to the part that would not have been separately obligated.

This passage from Al-Hidayah introduces a subtle but important rule: when parts of a murdered body are discovered at different times, the community's liability for qasamah and diyah is triggered only once. To determine which part triggers the obligation, a general principle is applied, and the same logic governs janazah prayer over partial remains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Understand that if qasamah and diyah were obligated on every discovered part, they would be repeated, which is not allowed.
2
State the Principle
The author gives a principle: look at the body part you have now, and consider if another part found later would make qasamah/diyah obligatory. If yes, the current part does not; if no, the current part does.
This ensures only one obligation.
3
Apply the Principle
You must assess each part in sequence relative to the next possible discovery.
The principle avoids repetition.
4
Extend to Janazah Prayer
The same rule applies: janazah prayer is not repeated over parts of the same body.
The underlying illah (cause) is non-repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور دوسری وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ اگر اقل کا اعتبار کر کے قسامت اور دیت واجب کر دی جائے تو پھر اکثر بدن کے ملنے سے قسامت اور دیت واجب ہوگی تو قسامت اور دیت کا تکرار لازم آئے گا حالانکہ قسامت اور دیت میں تکرار نہیں ہے اس کے متعلق مصنف نے ایک قاعدہ کلیہ بیان فرمایا ہے کہ یوں دیکھ لو کہ اب جو حصہ آپ کو ملا ہے اگر بعد میں اور حصہ بھی مل جائے تو اس دوسرے پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہوگی یا نہیں اگر دوسرے میں قسامت و دیت ہو تو پہلے میں واجب نہ ہوگی اور اگر دوسرے میں واجب نہ ہوتی ہو پہلے میں واجب ہوگی اور اس قاعدہ کی بھی یہی وجہ ہے کہ قسامت اور دیت میں تکرار لازم نہ آئے اور نماز جنازہ کا بھی یہی حکم ہے یعنی اگر بدن کا کچھ حصہ ملا ہے تو دوسرے کو دیکھو کہ اگر وہ مل جائے تو اس پر نماز جنازہ ہوگی یا نہیں اگر ہو تو اول حصہ پر نہ ہوگی اور اگر دوسرے پر نہ ہو تو اول حصہ پر نماز جنازہ ہوگی ۔ اس لئے کہ نماز جنازہ بھی مکرر نہیں ہوتی ، فلیتا مل۔ ( محمد یوسف )
And the second reason is also that if qasamah and diyah are made obligatory by considering the smaller part, then when the greater part of the body is found, qasamah and diyah would become obligatory, leading to repetition of qasamah and diyah, while there is no repetition in qasamah and diyah. Regarding this, the author stated a general principle: look, the part that you have now, if another part is also found later, will qasamah and diyah be obligatory on that second part or not? If there is qasamah and diyah in the second, then it is not obligatory on the first; and if it is not obligatory in the second, then it is obligatory on the first. The reason for this principle is to avoid repetition of qasamah and diyah. The same ruling applies to janazah prayer: if some part of the body is found, look at the second part: if it is found, will janazah prayer be performed over it? If yes, then it is not performed over the first part; and if not on the second, then it is performed over the first part. Because janazah prayer is also not repeated. May Allah grant success. (Muhammad Yusuf)
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage explains a general legal maxim (qa'idah kulliyyah) regarding the repetition of qasamah (oath-taking for retribution) and diyah (blood money) when parts of a murdered body are found at different times. The author of Al-Hidayah states that to avoid repetition (takrar), one should look at the second body part that might be found later. If that second part, were it found alone, would make qasamah and diyah obligatory on the locality, then the first part does not make them obligatory. Conversely, if the second part would not make them obligatory, then the first part does. This principle ensures that qasamah and diyah are not imposed more than once for the same murder. The same rule applies to janazah prayer over body parts: if a second part would be prayed over, the first is not prayed over, and vice versa.

Key Terms
قسامت (qasamah): Oath-taking procedure for retribution in murder cases where the killer is unknown, involving the locality's oath and payment of diyah.
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid to the heirs of the victim as compensation, here imposed on the locality.
قاعدہ کلیہ (qa'idah kulliyyah): A general principle or maxim that governs specific cases, used here to determine the timing of obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qasamah and diyah are obligatory on the first part.
B) Qasamah and diyah are not obligatory on the first part.
C) Both parts equally share the obligation.
D) The first part is prayed over but no diyah.

Key Takeaway
Qasamah, diyah, and janazah prayer are single obligations that cannot be repeated; a general principle determines which discovered body part triggers the obligation.

Finding a Fetus: When Qasamah and Diyah Apply
States the ruling on qasamah and diyah when a fetus or premature baby is found among people

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions required for qasamah and diyah to be obligatory on the locality when a fetus or premature baby is found, and identify when they do not apply.

Core Idea
A fully-formed fetus with marks of violence triggers qasamah and diyah; an incomplete one does not.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on a tragic scenario: finding a dead fetus or premature baby among the people of a locality. The key is distinguishing when the community bears responsibility (qasamah and diyah) versus when they are absolved. The text from Al-Hidayah sets out two critical criteria: the presence of marks of violence and the completeness of the baby's physical formation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Legal Context
Recognize that the act is the discovery of a dead fetus or premature baby (saqt) among the people of a specific locality (mahallah). The legal question is whether the locality is liable for qasamah (sworn oath) and diyah (blood money).
Qasamah is a collective oath taken to establish liability for murder in cases where a body is found with signs of violence but no known perpetrator.
2
Determine the First Condition: Marks of Violence
Check if there are marks of beating (athar al-darb) on the body. If no marks are present, the ruling is that nothing is due on the locality, by analogy to an adult found dead without marks.
The text states: 'if there is no mark of beating, there is nothing upon the people of the locality because it does not surpass the adult in status.'
3
Determine the Second Condition: Completeness of Formation
If marks are present, then evaluate the baby's physical formation. A fully-formed baby (tam al-khalq) with all limbs complete triggers liability because the apparent fact (zahir) is that it was born alive and then killed. An incomplete baby (naqis al-khalq) does not trigger liability because the presumption is it was stillborn.
The distinction is based on customary experience: a fully-formed baby is likely to have been born alive; an incomplete one is likely to have been stillborn.
4
Apply the Ruling to the Combination of Factors
Combine the two criteria: (1) No marks → no liability regardless of formation. (2) Marks present + fully formed → qasamah and diyah wajib. (3) Marks present + incomplete → no liability.
This is the complete ruling from the text.
5
Understand the Underlying Reasoning
The analogy to an adult (for no marks) and the presumption of live birth (for fully formed) form the ratio legis. The ruling reflects Hanafi reliance on customary presumptions (zahir) to determine legal consequences.
Other schools may use different criteria for viability, such as crying or movement, but Hanafis rely on physical completeness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو وجد فيهم جنين أو سقط ليس به أثر الضرب فلاشيء على أهل المحلة؛ لأنه لا يفوق الكبير حالا وإن كان به أثر الضرب وهو تام الخلق وجبت القسامة والدية عليهم؛ لأن الظاهر أن تام الخلق ينفصل حيا وإن كان ناقص الخلق فلاشيء عليهم؛ لأنه ينفصل ميتا لا حيا

ترجمہ اور اگر اہل محلہ کے درمیان جنین پایا جائے یا نا تمام گرا ہوا بچہ جس پر ضرب کا اثر نہ ہوتو اہل محلہ پر کوئی چیز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ جنین حالت میں بڑے آدمی سے نہیں بڑھے گا اور اگر اس پر ضرب کا اثر ہو اور وہ تام الخلق ہو تو اہل محلہ پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہے اس لئے کہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ نام اخلاق زندہ جدا ہوتا ہے اور اگر وہ ناقص الخلق ہو تو ان پر کوئی چیز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ مردہ جدا ہوتا ہے نہ کہ زندہ

تشریح اور اگر محلہ والوں کے درمیان وہ بچہ ملا جو بھی جنین تھا مگر اب پیدا ہو گیا ہے اور محلہ میں پڑا ہے یا بچہ نا تمام ہے لیکن اس پر زخم الضرب کا کوئی اثر نہیں تو اہل محلہ پر کچھ بھی واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اگر بڑا آدمی بھی مردہ پایا جاتا اور اس پر کوئی اثر نہ ہوتا تب بھی اہل محلہ پر دبیت واجب نہیں تھی لہذا اب بھی واجب نہ ہوگی اور اگر اس پر ضرب کا اثر ہو اور اعضاء و اس کے سب بن چکے ہوں یعنی وہ تام الخلق ہو تو اب اہل محلہ پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہوگی اس لئے کہ یہاں ظاہر یہی ہے کہ وہ اپنی ماں سے زندہ پیدا ہوا ہے اور اس کو کسی نے مارا ہے، اور اگر وہ ناقص الخلق ہو تو ان پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ یہاں ظاہر یہ ہے کہ وہ ماں کے پیٹ سے مردہ پیدا ہوا ہے نہ کہ زندہ۔
And if a fetus or a premature baby is found among them without any mark of beating, there is nothing upon the people of the locality because it does not surpass the adult in status. But if there is a mark of beating and it is fully formed, the qasamah and diyah become obligatory upon them because the apparent fact is that the fully formed one separates alive. And if it is imperfectly formed, there is nothing upon them because it separates dead, not alive.

Translation: And if among the people of the locality a fetus is found, or a prematurely dropped child on which there is no effect of beating, then there is nothing upon the people of the locality because a fetus in its state does not surpass an adult. And if there is an effect of beating and it is fully formed (tam al-khalq), then qasamah and diyah are obligatory upon the people of the locality because the apparent fact is that a fully formed child separates alive. And if it is imperfectly formed (naqis al-khalq), then there is nothing upon them because it separates dead, not alive.

Explanation: And if among the people of the locality a child is found who was also a fetus but has now been born and lies in the locality, or the child is imperfect but there is no effect of the beating wound, then nothing is obligatory on the people of the locality because if an adult was also found dead without any effect, even then the diyah was not obligatory on the people of the locality, so now also it will not be obligatory. And if there is an effect of beating and all its limbs are fully formed, i.e., it is fully formed, then qasamah and diyah become obligatory on the people of the locality because the apparent fact is that it was born alive from its mother and someone killed it. And if it is imperfectly formed, then nothing is obligatory on them because the apparent fact is that it was born dead from its mother's womb, not alive.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling from the matn of Al-Hidayah regarding the finding of a fetus or a prematurely delivered baby among the people of a locality. The ruling distinguishes based on two criteria: the presence of marks of violence and the completeness of the baby's physical formation. If there are no marks of violence, no qasamah or diyah is due, similar to an adult found dead without marks. If there are marks and the baby is fully formed (tam al-khalq, meaning all limbs are complete), then qasamah and diyah are obligatory on the locality because the external evidence (zahir) indicates that such a baby was born alive and then killed. However, if the baby is not fully formed (naqis al-khalq), even with marks, nothing is due because the presumption is that it was stillborn. This shows the Hanafi reliance on customary presumption based on physical completeness to determine whether life existed at birth.

Key Terms
تام الخلق (tam al-khalq): A baby whose physical form is complete with all limbs fully developed, presumed to have been born alive.
ناقص الخلق (naqis al-khalq): A baby with incomplete physical formation, presumed to be stillborn and thus not a legal person for qasamah/diyah.
أثر الضرب (athar al-darb): Marks or evidence of beating or violence on the body.
قسامة (qasamah): A collective swearing of oaths by the people of a locality to deny responsibility for a murder, or to establish liability.
دية (diyah): Blood money payable for homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is qasamah and diyah obligatory on the locality for a found fetus?
A) Whenever a fetus is found dead with any mark.
B) Only if the fetus is fully formed and has marks of violence.
C) Only if the fetus is not fully formed.
D) Whenever the fetus is found, regardless of marks or formation.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on finding a fetus distinguishes between fully formed (tam al-khalq) and incomplete (naqis al-khalq) because the former is presumed live-born, making marks of violence evidence of homicide triggering collective liability.

Liability for Death on a Controlled Animal
States the ruling on liability for diyah when a dead body is found on a controlled animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah when a dead body is found on an animal under a person's control, and apply the qiyas analogy to determine liability in multi-person scenarios.

Core Idea
Blood money falls on the controller's clan, not the locality—control creates custody.

This passage from Al-Quduri, expanded in Al-Hidayah, addresses a specific scenario: a dead body found on a beast of burden while someone is driving, leading, or riding it. The ruling shifts liability from the locality to the person controlling the animal, by analogy to finding the body in one's house. We will examine the reasoning and its application when multiple persons share control.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling and its exceptions
Read the passage to extract the main rule: diyah is on the 'aqilah of the controller, not the locality. Note that this applies whether the person is driving (sa'iq), leading (qa'id), or riding (rakib).
The ruling is categorical: no distinction between modes of control.
2
Understand the ratio legis (illah) – custody under hand
The reasoning given is 'because he is under his hand' (li-annahu fi yadihi). This indicates control and custody, analogous to possession of a house. The illah is the exclusive control over the space where the body is found.
This illah is key for extending the ruling to other scenarios.
3
Apply the analogy (qiyas) explicitly
The text compares the animal under control to a house: just as a body found in a house makes the occupant liable, so too a body found on a controlled animal makes the controller liable. Trace the asl (house), far' (animal under control), illah (being under his hand), and hukm (diyah on 'aqilah).
This is a clear example of Hanafi qiyas using custody as the operative cause.
4
Analyze the collective scenario
If multiple persons control the animal together (e.g., one driving, one leading, one riding), the diyah is on all their 'aqilahs jointly. The illah of collective custody applies, akin to a shared house.
Joint liability is proportional? The text implies equal, but further details may come from other sources.
5
Consider cross-madhhab differences
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may assign liability to the locality (ahl al-mahalla) in some cases. The Hanafi position rests on the primacy of individual custody over collective locality responsibility.
This ikhtilaf is not elaborated here but noted for context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإذا وجد القتيل على دابة يسوقها رجل فالدية على عاقلته دون أهل المحلة؛ لأنه في يده فصار كما إذا كان في داره وكذا إذا كان قائدها أو راكبها فإن اجتمعوا فعليهم؛ لأن القتيل فى أيديهم فصار كما إذا وجد في دارهم

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جبکہ مقتول کسی چوپائے پر پایا جائے جس کو کوئی شخص ہانکتا ہو تو دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر ہوگی نہ کہ اہل محلہ پر اس لئے کہ مقتول اس کے ہاتھ میں ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اس کے گھر میں ہو اور ایسے ہی حکم ہے جب کہ وہ چوپائے کا قائد یا اس کا راکب ہو پس اگر یہ سب جمع ہو جائیں تو دیت ان سب پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ مقتول ان کے ہاتھ میں ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے جب کہ مقتول ان کے گھر میں پایا جائے۔

تشریح ایک چوپائے کو کوئی شخص لئے جاتا ہے اور اس پر کوئی مقتول ہے تو اس کی دیت اس پر واجب ہوگی جیسے اگر مقتول اس کے گھر میں ملا تو یہی حکم ہوتا، پھر وہ شخص پیچھے سے ہانکے یا آگے سے کھینچے یا اس پر سوار ہو سب برابر ہے اور اگر تین شخص ہوں ایک سائق اور ایک قائد اور ایک راکب تو ان سب پر دیت واجب ہوگی ۔ جیسے اگر ان کے گھر میں مقتول ملا تو ان سب پر دیت واجب ہوتی ایسے ہی یہاں بھی واجب ہوگی۔
He said: And if the slain person is found on an animal that a man is driving, then the blood money is upon his 'aqilah (family/clan), and not upon the people of the locality, because he is under his hand, so it becomes as if he were in his house. Similarly, if he is leading it or riding it, and if they are all together, then it is upon them, because the slain person is under their hands, so it becomes as if he were found in their house.

Translation: Al-Quduri said: And when a slain person is found on a mount which a person is driving, then the blood money is upon his 'aqilah, not upon the people of the locality, because the slain person is in his hand, so it becomes as if he were in his house. The same ruling applies when he is the leader or rider of the mount. Then if they all are gathered, then the blood money is upon all of them, because the slain person is in their hands, so it becomes as if the slain is found in their house.

Explanation: A person is taking an animal, and there is a slain person on it, then the diyah is obligatory on him, just as if the slain person was found in his house, this ruling would apply. Then whether that person drives from behind, or leads from the front, or rides upon it, all are equal. And if there are three persons: one driver (sa'iq), one leader (qa'id), and one rider (rakib), then diyah is obligatory on all of them, just as if the slain person was found in their house, diyah would be obligatory on all of them, similarly here it is obligatory.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage addresses the liability for diyah when a dead body is found on an animal that is under human control. The ruling from Al-Quduri states that the diyah is on the 'aqilah (the group responsible for paying blood money) of the person controlling the animal, not on the locality. The reasoning is that the deceased is under the hand (fi yadihi) of that person, analogous to being found in his house. The 'aqilah pays because it is a case where the responsibility arises from control and presumptive negligence. The ruling applies equally whether the person is driving the animal from behind (sa'iq), leading it from the front (qa'id), or riding it (rakib). If multiple persons are involved, all of them share the liability because the slain person is under the collective control of all, akin to being found in a house owned jointly.

Key Terms
عاقلہ ('aqilah): The group of male agnatic relatives (or tribe) who are responsible for paying diyah on behalf of the perpetrator, here the person controlling the animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a dead body is found on an animal that a man is leading from the front, who is liable for the diyah?
A) The people of the locality.
B) The 'aqilah of the man leading the animal.
C) The owner of the animal.
D) No one, since it is an accident.

Key Takeaway
The diyah for a body found on a controlled animal is on the 'aqilah of the person in control, not the locality, by qiyas to finding the body in one's house.

Diyah Liability for a Body Found on an Animal Between Two Villages
Ruling on diyah liability with proof and a condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah liability when a dead body is found on an animal between two villages, identify the textual proof, and explain the qualification regarding voice reach.

Core Idea
The nearer village is liable for diyah, but only if the victim's cry could have been heard and they failed to help.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi criminal law: an animal passes between two villages carrying a dead body, with no known killer. Imam Muhammad rules that the nearer village bears the diyah (blood money). We will explore the textual evidence from the Prophet's and Umar's practices, and the critical qualification added by some jurists: that the village must be close enough for the victim's voice to reach them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the ruling from Imam Muhammad: when an animal carrying a dead body passes between two villages, the diyah is on the nearer village.
The ruling is based on the claim that the nearer village could have provided help but failed (taqsir).
2
Analyse the Primary Proof
Look at the hadith: the Prophet ﷺ ordered measurement when a body was found between two villages. This indicates that distance is the criterion for liability.
The measurement determines which village is nearer.
3
Analyse the Secondary Proof
Examine the practice of Umar (رضي الله عنه) in the case of Wadi'a and Arhab. He measured and imposed qasamah (oaths) on the nearer village.
This confirms the principle and provides a precedent.
4
Understand the Qualification
Some jurists qualify the ruling: the nearer village is only liable if the distance is such that the victim's voice could reach them (i.e., they could have heard his call for help).
If the village is too far, there is no negligence, so no diyah.
5
Grasp the Rationale
The underlying rationale is that diyah is imposed due to the villagers' failure to protect and help. The voice-reach condition ensures that only those who could have realistically helped are held accountable.
This balances justice with practicality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإن مرت دابة بين قريتين وعليها قتيل فهو على أقربهما لما روى أن النبي عليه السلام أتي بقتيل وجد بين قريتين فأمر أن يذرع وعن عمر رضى الله عنه أنه لما كتب إليه فى القتيل الذي وجد بين وادعة وأرحب كتب بأن يقيس بين قريتين فوجد القتيل إلى وادعة أقرب فقضى عليهم بالقسامة قيل هذا محمول على ما إذا كان بحيث يبلغ أهله الصوت لأنه إذا كان بهذه الصفة يلحقه الغوث فتمكنه النصرة وقد قصروا

ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا اور اگر کوئی چوپایہ دو گاؤں کے درمیان گذرے اور اس پر مقتول ہو تو دیت ان دونوں میں سے اقرب پر ہوگی اس روایت کی وجہ سے جو مروی ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام کے پاس ایک مقتول لایا گیا جو دو گاؤں کے درمیان ملا تھا پس آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پیمائش کا حکم دیا اور عمر سے منقول ہے جبکہ ان کی جانب اس مقتول کے بارے میں لکھا گیا جو وادعہ اور ارحب کے درمیان ملا تھا تو انہوں نے لکھا کہ دونوں کے درمیان پیمائش کی جائے مقتول کو وادعہ کے زیادہ قریب پایا گیا تو انہی پر قسامت کا فیصلہ کیا گیا کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ (ان میں سے اقرب پر دیت کا فیصلہ ) اس حالت پر محمول ہے جبکہ مقتول ایسے مقام پر ہو کہ اہل اقرب کو آواز پہنچ سکے اس لئے کہ وہ جب اس صفت پر ہو گا تو اس کو بد دلاحق ہو سکتی ہے تو ان کو مدد کر نا ممکن تھا حالانکہ انہوں نے کوتاہی کی ہے۔

تشریح ایک چوپایہ خود جارہا ہے جس کا کوئی سائق وغیرہ نہیں ہے اور اس پر ایک مقبول ہے تو اس کا کیسا حکم ہوگا تو فرمایا کہ چوپایہ جہاں کو گذر رہا ہے جو گاؤں اس جگہ سے قریب ہے اس گاؤں والے دیت کے ذمہ دار ہونگے اس پر بعض فقہاء نے کہا ہے کہ وہ گاؤں اتنے فاصلہ پر ہونا چاہئے کہ اگر وہاں سے مقتول ان کو آواز دیتا تو ان کو آواز پہنچ سکتی تھی ورنہ اگر زیادہ دور ہوگا تو پھر اس گاؤں والوں پر دیت نہ ہوگی کیونکہ دیت اس لئے واجب ہوتی ہے کہ یہ حفاظت و نصرت کر سکتے تھے لیکن انہوں نے کوتاہی کی ہے اور جب زیادہ دور ہوگا تو وہاں کوئی کوتا ہی ان کی جانب سے نہیں ہے بہر حال متن میں جو فر مایا گیا ہے کہ دونوں گاؤں میں سے جو قریب ہوگا اس کے باشندوں پر دیت واجب ہوگی اس پر مصنف نے دو دلیل بیان فرمائی ہیں:
He said: And if an animal passes between two villages and on it is a slain person, then the diyah is upon the nearer of the two, due to what is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ was brought a slain person found between two villages, so he ordered that it be measured. And from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that when he was written to regarding the slain person found between Wadi'a and Arhab, he wrote that measurement should be taken between the two villages, and the slain person was found nearer to Wadi'a, so he passed judgment of qasamah against them. It is said that this is interpreted upon the condition that the voice could reach its people, because if it is in such a condition, help can reach him, and it was possible for them to give support, yet they fell short.

Translation: Imam Muhammad said: And if an animal passes between two villages and on it is a slain person, then the diyah is upon the nearer of the two, due to the narration that the Prophet ﷺ was brought a slain person found between two villages, so he ordered measurement. And it is narrated from Umar that when he was written to regarding the slain person found between Wadi'a and Arhab, he wrote that measurement should be made between the two villages, and the slain person was found nearer to Wadi'a, so he decided qasamah against them. It is said that this ruling is interpreted upon the condition that the slain person is in a place where the voice of the residents of the nearer village could reach him, because when he is in such a condition, help could reach him, and it was possible for them to give support, yet they fell short.

Explanation: An animal is moving on its own, without any driver, and on it is a slain person. What is the ruling? He said: The animal is passing through, and whichever village is nearer to that place, the people of that village are responsible for the diyah. Some jurists have said that the distance should be such that if the slain person called out to them, his voice could reach them. Otherwise, if it is too far, then the diyah will not be on those villagers, because diyah is imposed on them due to their ability to protect and help, but they were negligent. When it is too far, there is no negligence on their part. In any case, in the matn it is stated that the nearer village is liable for diyah, and the author has provided two proofs:
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where an animal without a handler passes between two villages with a dead body on it. The ruling from Imam Muhammad states that the diyah is on the nearer village. The proof is from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, who ordered measurement when a body was found between two villages, and from the practice of Umar, who decided against the nearer village. However, some jurists qualify this: the liability only applies if the distance is such that the victim's voice could reach the villagers, enabling them to render aid. The underlying rationale is that the villagers are held accountable because they could have provided help but failed (taqsir). If the village is too far for the voice to carry, there is no negligence, and thus no diyah. This ruling highlights the Hanafi principle that liability in qasamah/diyah is based on presumed ability to protect and negligence in failing to do so.

Key Terms
أقرب (aqrab): The nearer of the two villages in terms of distance to where the dead body is found.
يذرع (yudhri'): To measure the distance between the body and the villages, using arm spans or cubits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The body must be found on a camel, not a donkey.
B) The village must have more than 100 people.
C) The distance must be such that the victim's voice could reach the village.
D) The animal must have been ridden recently.

Key Takeaway
Diyah liability on a village for a body found on a passing animal depends on proximity and the possibility of the victim's cry for help reaching them, due to their negligence.

Ruling on Diyah for a Corpse Found on an Animal Between Two Villages
Ruling on diyah when corpse on animal passes between two villages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah when a corpse is found on an animal between two villages, identify the two proofs cited, and apply the condition of proximity.

Core Idea
Proximity determines liability: diyah is on the nearest village able to render aid.

This passage from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani addresses an unusual scenario: a slain person found on an unattended animal passing between two villages. The ruling imposes blood money (diyah) on the closer village. The reasoning hinges on the villagers' ability to help—their negligence is the basis for liability. Two proofs anchor this: the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered measurement in a similar case, and Caliph 'Umar applied the same method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal act being ruled upon: the situation of a corpse on an animal between two villages. The ruling is that the blood money (diyah) is wajib on the closer village.
The ruling is part of the chapter on jinayat (homicide) and blood money.
2
Locate the dalīl
Two proofs are cited: (1) a prophetic action (Sunnah) where the Prophet ordered measurement when a slain person was found between two villages; (2) the practice of Caliph 'Umar in a similar case between Wadi'a and Arhab.
These are dalīl naqlī (textual proofs). The second is a qawl al-ṣaḥābī, which Hanafis consider a strong proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The command to measure distance indicates that proximity is the criterion for liability. The 'illah (effective cause) is the ability to render aid: if the village is close enough that the victim's voice could be heard, aid was possible, so negligence triggers diyah.
Some jurists restrict the ruling to a distance where the voice carries; otherwise, no negligence.
4
Note the ikhtilāf
The ruling is mukhtalaf fīh: the Shāfi'ī school may have a different approach (e.g., requiring qasamah or a fixed distance). The Hanafīs rely on proximity and the ability to assist.
The thamarah al-khilāf (practical difference) is in which village is held liable.
5
Evaluate the tarjīḥ
This is the muftā bihī position from the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah. The reliance on proximity is supported by the Prophet's and 'Umar's actions, which are strong proofs in Hanafī uṣūl.
No known intra-Hanafī disagreement; all three imams (Abū Ḥanīfah, Abū Yūsuf, Muḥammad) agree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإن مرت دابة بين قريتين وعليها قتيل فهو على أقربهما لما روى أن النبي عليه السلام أتي بقتيل وجد بين قريتين فأمر أن يذرع وعن عمر رضى الله عنه أنه لما كتب إليه فى القتيل الذي وجد بين وادعة وأرحب كتب بأن يقيس بين قريتين فوجد القتيل إلى وادعة أقرب فقضى عليهم بالقسامة قيل هذا محمول على ما إذا كان بحيث يبلغ أهله الصوت لأنه إذا كان بهذه الصفة يلحقه الغوث فتمكنه النصرة وقد قصروا
ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا اور اگر کوئی چوپایہ دو گاؤں کے درمیان گذرے اور اس پر مقتول ہو تو دبیت ان دونوں میں سے اقرب پر ہوگی اس روایت کی وجہ سے جو مروی ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام کے پاس ایک مقتول لایا گیا جو دو گاؤں کے درمیان ملا تھا پس آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پیمائش کا حکم دیا اور عمر سے منقول ہے جبکہ ان کی جانب اس مقتول کے بارے میں لکھا گیا جو وادعہ اور ارحب کے درمیان ملا تھا تو انہوں نے لکھا کہ دونوں کے درمیان پیمائش کی جائے مقتول کو وادعہ کے زیادہ قریب پایا گیا تو انہی پر قسامت کا فیصلہ کیا گیا کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ (ان میں سے اقرب پر دیت کا فیصلہ ) اس حالت پر محمول ہے جبکہ مقتول ایسے مقام پر ہو کہ اہل اقرب کو آواز پہنچ سکے اس لئے کہ وہ جب اس صفت پر ہو گا تو اس کو بد دلاحق ہو سکتی ہے تو ان کو مدد کر نا ممکن تھا حالانکہ انہوں نے کوتاہی کی ہے۔
تشریح ایک چوپایہ خود جارہا ہے جس کا کوئی سائق وغیرہ نہیں ہے اور اس پر ایک مقبول ہے تو اس کا کیسا حکم ہوگا تو فرمایا کہ چوپایہ جہاں کو گذر رہا ہے جو گاؤں اس جگہ سے قریب ہے اس گاؤں والے دیت کے ذمہ دار ہونگے اس پر بعض فقہاء نے کہا ہے کہ وہ گاؤں اتنے فاصلہ پر ہونا چاہئے کہ اگر وہاں سے مقتول ان کو آواز دیتا تو ان کو آواز پہنچ سکتی تھی ورنہ اگر زیادہ دور ہوگا تو پھر اس گاؤں والوں پر دیت نہ ہوگی کیونکہ دیت اس لئے واجب ہوتی ہے کہ یہ حفاظت و نصرت کر سکتے تھے لیکن انہوں نے کوتاہی کی ہے اور جب زیادہ دور ہوگا تو وہاں کوئی کوتا ہی ان کی جانب سے نہیں ہے بہر حال متن میں جو فر مایا گیا ہے کہ دونوں گاؤں میں سے جو قریب ہوگا اس کے باشندوں پر دیت واجب ہوگی اس پر مصنف نے دو دلیل بیان فرمائی ہیں:
(٭ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے سامنے یہ واقعہ پیش آیا تو آپ نے پیمائش کا حکم فرمایا تھا تا کہ یہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ کون سی بستی قریب ہے تا کہ اس آ پر دیت واجب کی جاسکے۔
(۲ حضرت عمر کے دور میں وادعہ اور ارجب کے درمیان ایک مقتول ملا تو وہاں کے عامل نے یہ واقعہ امیر المؤمنین کو لکھا تو آپ نے پیمائش کا حکم فرمایا بعد پیمائش معلوم ہوا کہ وادعہ زیادہ قریب ہے تو اس کے باشندوں پر دیست واجب کر دی گئی ۔
Imam Muhammad said: And if an animal passes between two villages and on it is a slain person, then it is upon the closer of the two, due to what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was brought a slain person found between two villages, so he ordered that the distance be measured. And from 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that when he was written to concerning the slain person found between Wadi'a and Arhab, he wrote that the distance be measured between the two villages; they found the slain person closer to Wadi'a, so he decreed the qasamah upon them. It is said that this ruling is applied when the slain person is such that the people of the closer village could hear his voice, because if he is in that condition, he could be rescued and they could help him, but they failed. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: And if an animal passes between two villages and on it is a slain person, then the blood money is upon the closer of the two, due to this narration. Commentary: An animal is going by itself without any driver, and upon it is a slain person; what is the ruling? He said: the village nearer to where the animal is passing will be responsible for the blood money. Some jurists said that the village should be at such a distance that if the slain person called out to them, they could hear him; otherwise, if it is farther, then the blood money is not on that village because the blood money is obligatory when they could have protected and helped but failed. The author cited two proofs: (1) The Prophet was presented with this incident and ordered measurement. (2) In 'Umar's time, a slain person was found between Wadi'a and Arhab; the governor wrote to him; he ordered measurement; it was found closer to Wadi'a, so he imposed the blood money on them.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding a corpse found on an unattended animal passing between two villages. The blood money is imposed on the closer village, as established by the precedent of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who ordered measurement when a similar case occurred, and by the practice of Caliph 'Umar in the case between Wadi'a and Arhab. Some jurists restrict the ruling to cases where the village is close enough that the victim's voice could reach them, implying that the obligation arises from the villagers' ability to provide aid and their negligence. The passage includes the Arabic text from the Hidayah (or related works) and an Urdu commentary. The proofs are from the Sunnah (prophetic action) and the practice of a Companion (Caliph 'Umar), which is considered a strong proof in Hanafi usul. The ruling is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah and is relied upon for fatwa.

Key Terms
قسامة (qasamah): An oath taken in cases of suspected homicide when there is no clear evidence; often used in the context of liability for blood money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What two proofs are cited for the ruling that the blood money is on the closer village when a corpse is found on an animal between them?
A) A hadith of the Prophet and an action of Abu Bakr
B) A hadith of the Prophet and an action of 'Umar
C) A hadith of the Prophet and a ruling of Ali
D) Consensus of the Companions and a hadith

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a slain person is found on an unattended animal between two villages, the blood money is wajib on the closer village, provided the distance was such that aid could have been rendered.

Qasamah Liability: Owners vs. Residents
Intra-Hanafi dispute on inclusion of residents in qasamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether residents are included in qasamah, explain the proof of each side, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to a practical scenario.

Core Idea
Only owners, not mere residents, are liable for qasamah in a locality.

When a corpse is found in a locality, who is responsible for the qasamah? The Hanafi school holds owners primarily liable. But what about tenants or residents who do not own property? Abu Yusuf argued they share liability, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani limited it to owners. This lesson unpacks their reasoning, focusing on the concept of 'wilayat al-tadbir' and the precedent of Khaibar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the exact issue: when a corpse is found in a locality, are residents (non-owners) jointly liable with owners in oaths (qasamah)?
Qasamah here refers to the collective oath taken by the locality to deny involvement; if they refuse, they pay blood money.
2
State Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's position
Clearly state that they exclude residents. Only owners face the qasamah.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and his proof
Abu Yusuf includes all residents. His proof is the Khaibar precedent and the principle that wilayat al-tadbir is acquired by residence, not just ownership.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf
The response distinguishes Khaibar: the Jews were owners (they retained land in exchange for kharaj), not mere residents. Mere residency does not confer sufficient authority.
This rebuttal relies on a factual distinction.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
In a modern scenario with both owners and tenants, only owners are bound. Tenants are not required to participate in the qasamah.
The difference in practice is whether tenants face financial liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولاتدخل السكان في القسامة مع الملاك عند أبي حنيفة وهو قول محمد وقال أبويوسف هو عليهم جميعا لأن ولاية التدبير كما تكون بالملك تكون بالسكنى الاترى أنه عليه السلام جعل القسامة والدية على اليهود وإن كانوا سكانا بخيبر ولهما أن المالك هو المختص بنصرة البقعة دون السكان؛ لأن سكنى الملاك ألزم وقرارهم أدوم فكانت ولاية التدبير إليهم فيتحقق التقصير منهم وأما أهل خيبر فالنبي عليه السلام أقـــرهــم عــلــى أمــلاكـ أملاكهم كأن يأخذ لى وجه الخراج
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور قسامت میں، سکان داخل نہ ہوں گے مالکان کے ساتھ ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اور ہی محمد کا قول ہے اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ قسامت ان سب پر ہوگی اس لئے کر تد بیر کی ولایت جیسے ملک کے ذریعہ ہوتی ہے ایسے سکنی کے ذریعہ ہوتی ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے یہود پر قسامت اور دیت کو واجب کیا تھا اگر چہ وہ خیبر میں سکان تھے ( مالک نہ تھے ) اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بقعہ کی نصرت کے ساتھ مالک بھی مخصوص ہے نہ کہ رہنے والے اس لئے کیا کا نجی سکتی ہے اور ان کا بھمبر نازیادہ دائمی ہے۔ تو تدبیر کی ولایت انہی کو ہوگی تو ان کی جانب سے تقصیر متحقق ہوگی اور بہر حال اہل خیر تو نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کو ان کی املاک پر برقرار رکھا تھا اور ان سے ( جو کچھ لیتے تھے ) وہ خراج کے طریقہ پر لیتے تھے۔
Al-Quduri said: And the residents (sukkan) will not enter into the qasamah with the owners (mullak) according to Abu Hanifa, and that is the statement of Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said that it is upon all of them, because the authority of management, just as it is through ownership, is also through residence. Do you not see that the Prophet (peace be upon him) imposed the qasamah and diyah upon the Jews even though they were residents in Khaibar (not owners)? And the proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the owner is specifically responsible for the protection of the place (buq'ah) and not the residents, because the residence of the owners is more permanent and their stay is more lasting, so the authority of management is theirs, and thus negligence is realized from them. As for the people of Khaibar, the Prophet (peace be upon him) confirmed them upon their properties, as if taking from them in the manner of kharaj.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa (and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Abu Yusuf regarding whether residents (sukkan) who are not owners are included with the owners in qasamah when a corpse is found in a locality. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad exclude the residents, because the authority to manage and protect the area belongs to the owners due to their permanent residence and stake. Abu Yusuf argues that residents also have a degree of control, analogizing to the Jews of Khaibar who were residents (not owners) but were held liable for qasamah by the Prophet. The response (from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the Khaibar case is different: the Jews were actually owners of their properties (they held them as tenants or with rights), and the payment was in the form of kharaj (land tax), not because they were mere residents. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: only owners are liable for qasamah, not mere residents. This dispute is recorded in the later works (like Hidayah and its commentaries) and is significant in determining the scope of communal liability.

Key Terms
سکان (sukkan): Residents or tenants who live in a place without owning it.
ملاک (mullak): Owners of properties (land or houses).
ولایت تدبیر (wilayat al-tadbir): Authority or control to manage and protect a locality, giving rise to responsibility for negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, who is liable for qasamah when a corpse is found in a locality?
A) All residents including owners
B) Only the owners
C) Only the tenants
D) The entire locality equally

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi position is that only property owners, not mere residents, are liable for qasamah.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Residents vs Owners in Qasama
Intra-Hanafi dispute about including residents in qasama with owners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether non-owner residents are included in qasama, explain the proofs of both sides, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Only owners are liable in qasama; residents are not included because protection is tied to permanent ownership.

When a slain person is found in a locality, Islamic law requires the inhabitants to swear oaths (qasama) to deny involvement and avoid diyah liability. But who exactly is required to swear? In this passage, we encounter an internal Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani restrict qasama to property owners, while Abu Yusuf argues that residents (tenants) are also included. The resolution of this dispute hinges on the concept of 'authority of administration' (wilāyat al-tadbīr) and the interpretation of a Prophetic precedent concerning the Jews of Khaybar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine what the passage is disputing: when a slain person is found, who among the inhabitants (owners vs. residents) must participate in qasama?
Residents (sukkān) are those living without ownership, e.g., tenants.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that only owners (mullāk) are subject to qasama; residents are not. Abu Yusuf holds that both owners and residents are included.
The disagreement is within the Hanafi school itself.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf’s proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the Prophet ﷺ imposed qasama on the Jews of Khaybar even though they were residents, not owners. This shows that residence alone can establish authority of administration.
The Jews of Khaybar were treated as residents because they did not originally own the land.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond that the Jews of Khaybar were actually owners—the Prophet confirmed them on their properties, and the payments they made were in the nature of kharaj (land tax), not rent. Thus, the precedent does not apply to non-owner residents.
The key distinction is whether the Jews were owners or mere residents.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: only owners are liable for qasama. Residents are not included.
This is the fatwa that is generally given in the Hanafi school.

كانوا سكانا بخيبر ولهما أن المالك هو المختص بنصرة البقعة دون السكان؛ لأن سكنى الملاك ألزم وقرارهم أدوم فكانت ولاية التدبير إليهم فيتحقق التقصير منهم وأما أهل خيبر فالنبي عليه السلام أقـــرهــم عــلــى جانب سے تقصیر متحقق ہوگی اور بہر حال اہل خیبر تو نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کو ان کی املاک پر برقرار رکھا تھا اور ان سے (جو کچھ لیتے تھے) وہ خراج کے طریقہ پر لیتے تھے۔ تشریح: کسی محلہ کے باشندے کچھ تو وہ ہیں جو یہاں کے اصلی باشندے ہیں اور یہاں کی زمینوں کے مالک ہیں اور کچھ وہ ہیں جو بغیر ملکیت کے کرایہ وغیرہ پر یہاں رہتے ہیں تو قسامت کن پر ہوگی تو حضرات طرفین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ قسامت فقط مالکان پر ماخوذ ہوں گے۔ اور رہا مسئلہ خیبر کے یہود کا تو وہ مالک تھے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اُن کو ان کی املاک و جائداد پر برقرار رکھا تھا اور ان سے جو کچھ وصول فرماتے تھے وہ خراج کے طریقہ پر لیا کرتے تھے۔
He said: And the residents do not enter into the qasama with the owners according to Abu Hanifa, and this is the saying of Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: It is upon all of them because the authority of administration, just as it is established through ownership, is established through residence. Do you not see that the Prophet ﷺ made the qasama and diyah obligatory upon the Jews even though they were residents of Khaybar (not owners)? And for the two of them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): The owner is specifically entitled to the protection of the locality, not the residents, because the residence of the owners is more binding and their stay is more permanent, so the authority of administration belongs to them, and thus the negligence is realized from them. As for the people of Khaybar, the Prophet ﷺ confirmed them upon their properties, taking from them in the manner of kharaj. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And in qasama, the residents will not enter along with the owners according to Abu Hanifa, and this is the saying of Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: Qasama will be upon all of them because the authority of administration, like it is through ownership, is through residence. Don't you see that the Prophet ﷺ made qasama and diyah wajib upon the Jews even though they were residents of Khaybar (not owners). And the proof of the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the owner is specifically entitled to the protection of the locality, not the residents, because the residence of the owners is more lasting and their stay is more permanent. So the authority of administration will be for them, and negligence will be realized from them. And as for the people of Khaybar, the Prophet ﷺ confirmed them upon their properties and what he took from them was in the manner of kharaj. Elaboration: The inhabitants of a locality are of two types: some are original inhabitants and owners of the lands, and some live there without ownership on rent etc. So upon whom will qasama be? The two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that qasama is only upon the owners, not upon the residents. Abu Yusuf says that qasama is upon both because qasama and diyah relate to administration, and in this matter all are equal. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf was: the Prophet ﷺ made qasama and diyah wajib upon the Jews even though they were not owners of Khaybar but were residents without ownership, indicating that qasama and diyah are also upon non-owners. The proof of the two parties is that for the protection of the locality, only the owners are designated, not the residents, because the residents' stay and settlement is not permanent unlike the owners. Hence the authority of administration is on the owners, and protection is necessary upon them, so negligence is from them, and they will be held accountable. As for the issue of the Jews of Khaybar, they were owners, and the Prophet ﷺ confirmed them on their properties and took from them in the manner of kharaj.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether residents (sukkan) who are not owners of property are included in the qasama along with the owners when a slain person is found in a locality. The two positions are presented: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that only the owners (mālik) are subject to qasama and diyah, not the residents. Their reasoning is that the authority of administration (wilāyat al-tadbīr) belongs to owners because their residence is more permanent and their connection to the locality is stronger. On the other hand, Abu Yusuf argues that both owners and residents are included because the authority of administration can also be established through residence, as evidenced by the case of the Jews of Khaybar who were residents but not original owners, yet the Prophet ﷺ imposed qasama and diyah on them. The Hanafi rebuttal is that the Jews of Khaybar were actually owners; the Prophet had confirmed them on their properties and took kharaj from them, so their case is not a precedent for including non-owner residents. The commentary explains the practical scenario: residents are those who rent houses without ownership, and the dispute is whether they share responsibility. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, i.e., only owners are subject to qasama.

Key Terms
السكان (al-sukkān): Residents who live in a locality without owning the property, e.g., tenants.
الملاك (al-mullāk): Property owners in the locality.
ولاية التدبير (wilāyat al-tadbīr): The authority of administration and management over the locality, implying responsibility for protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, who is subject to qasama when a slain person is found in a locality?
A) Only the owners of property
B) Only the residents
C) Both owners and residents
D) The entire community

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, only property owners are liable for qasama; non-owner residents are not included because the authority of administration (wilāyat al-tadbīr) is tied to ownership.

Original Settlers vs Buyers in Qasama
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qasama liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on qasama between ahl al-khittah and buyers, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Qasama falls only on original settlers, not on subsequent buyers — ownership alone does not create liability.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a dispute within the Hanafi school about who bears the burden of qasama in a locality: the original settlers granted land by the Imam, or also those who later buy property. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad restrict qasama to the original settlers, while Abu Yusuf extends it to all owners. Understanding this dispute reveals how the school weighs historical connection (aṣīl) over mere ownership.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: qasama is only upon the ahl al-khittah (original settlers), not upon buyers.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Abu Yusuf disagrees and holds that all owners, both original settlers and buyers, are equally liable for qasama.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the authority of protection (wilāyat al-ḥifẓ) is based on ownership, and all owners are equal in that.
Thus, all are liable if they abandon protection.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond that the original settler is the one customarily responsible for protection (ta'āruf), and he is the original (aṣīl) while the buyer is a newcomer (dakhīl). Authority of administration belongs to the aṣīl.
Also, Abu Hanifa based this on his observation in Kufa.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if only ahl al-khittah are liable, buyers and their aqilah are exempt from qasama and diyah; if all owners are liable, they share the burden.

And it is said that Abu Hanifa based this on what he observed in Kufa.
