The second party are those who have bought property and taken up residence. Both parties are equal owners. In such a case, upon which party is qasama? Imam Abu Yusuf said that qasama and diyah are upon both parties because both are owners and both have the authority of protection, so due to abandonment of protection, both parties have committed negligence and crime, so both will be held accountable. Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage presents another intra-Hanafi dispute within the context of qasama. The question is whether qasama applies to original settlers (ahl al-khittah) — those who were granted land by the Imam at the time of conquest — or also to subsequent buyers (mushtarun) who purchase property and reside in the same locality. The matn states that qasama is on the ahl al-khittah, not on the buyers, which is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf disagrees, asserting that all owners, whether original settlers or buyers, share equal responsibility because the authority of protection (wilāyat al-ḥifẓ) is based on ownership, and in ownership they are equal. The reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is that the original settler (ṣāḥib al-khiṭṭah) is the one specially connected to the protection of the locality by custom, and because he is the original (aṣīl) while the buyer is a newcomer (dakhīl), the authority of administration belongs to the original. There is also a report that Abu Hanifa based this ruling on his observation of the situation in Kufa. The commentary explains the two categories and emphasizes that both are owners, yet the school differentiates based on the historical connection. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, i.e., qasama is only on the ahl al-khittah.

Key Terms
أهل الخطة (ahl al-khiṭṭah): Original settlers who were granted land by the Imam at the time of conquest.
المشترين (al-mushtarūn): Those who buy property in the locality after the original settlement.
الأصيل (al-aṣīl): The original, established person (here the original settler).
الدخيل (al-dakhīl): A newcomer or latecomer who does not have the same level of authority as the original.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Upon all property owners
B) Upon the original settlers (ahl al-khittah) only
C) Upon the buyers only
D) Upon the residents regardless of ownership

Key Takeaway
Qasama liability falls only on the original settlers (ahl al-khittah), not on subsequent buyers, due to their customary authority and status as aṣīl.

Qasamah on a Ship: Possession vs. Ownership
Ruling on liability for a murdered person found on a ship with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qasamah for a murdered person found on a ship and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding liability in fixed versus movable property.

Core Idea
On a ship, all present are liable for qasamah because possession governs; on a house, only owners are liable because ownership governs.

Imagine a dead body is found on a ship with many people, but no one knows who killed them. Islamic law holds the community responsible to deter secret killing. This lesson examines the classical Hanafi ruling on such a case and the nuanced disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) about whose liability extends from ships to fixed dwellings like houses.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed Hanafi position on a ship
Identify the ruling: when a murdered person is found on a ship, qasamah (and diyah if no oath) is obligatory upon all present – passengers, crew, and owners. This is the unanimous view of the three Hanafi imams.
The consensus is based on the ship being movable and in the collective possession of those on board.
2
Identify the point of dispute between Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn
The disagreement is about fixed property (a house or locality). Abu Yusuf extends the same rule: residents and owners are equally liable. The Sahibayn restrict liability to owners only.
The ship ruling is not disputed; the dispute concerns the application of the same principle to immovable property.
3
Follow the reasoning (qiyas) of each side
Abu Yusuf analogizes both ship and house to collective possession. The Sahibayn distinguish based on movability: a ship is like an animal (possession governs), a house is fixed (ownership governs).
The qiyas is khafi (subtle) because it involves the underlying criterion of yad vs. milk.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
In a fixed locality, according to Abu Yusuf, residents must swear oaths and may pay diyah along with owners. According to the Sahibayn, only owners are obligated. This affects who bears the financial burden.
The fatwa practice may follow the Sahibayn's more restrictive view to avoid burdening those without ownership.
5
Note the tarjih and the mufta bihi on ships
On ships, there is no dispute – all three agree. On houses, the text does not explicitly choose, but the Sahibayn's distinction is defended. The mufta bihi for ships is unanimously 'all present are liable.'
Later Hanafi fatwa works may adopt the Sahibayn's view for fixed property. The key is understanding the basis: yad for movable, milk for immovable.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ: قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر مقتول کشتی میں پایا جائے تو قسامت ان لوگوں پر واجب ہے جو کشتی میں ہیں یعنی سوار اور ملاح اس لئے کہ کشتی ان کے قبضہ میں ہے اور لفظ "من فيها" مالکان کشتی کو شامل ہے یہاں تک کہ قسامت واجب ہے ان مالکان کشتی پر جو کشتی میں ہیں اور سکان پر اور ایسے ہی ان لوگوں پر جو کشتی کو کھینچتے ہیں اس میں مالک اور غیر مالک برابر اور ایسے ہی بیل گاڑی اور یہ (سکان و ملاک کا برابر ہونا) ابو یوسف کی روایت کے مطابق تو ظاہر ہے اور طرفین کے لئے وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ کشتی منتقل ہوتی ہے اور متحول ہوتی ہے تو اس میں قبضہ معتبر ہوگا نہ کہ ملکیت جیسے چوپائے میں بخلاف محلہ اور گھر کے اس لئے کہ یہ منتقل نہیں ہوتے۔
تشریح: اگر مقتول کشتی کے اندر ہو تو جو لوگ کشتی کے اندر ہیں انہی پر قسامت و دیت واجب ہے خواہ سوار ہوں خواہ مالک اور خواہ ملاح لوگ ہوں سب ضامن ہوں گے اور بیل گاڑی کا بھی یہی حال ہے لہذا بسوں کا بھی یہی حال ہوگا۔
سوال: طرفین تو کل کے سبق میں یہ فرما رہے تھے کہ فقط مالکان دار پر قسامت ہے نہ کہ سکان پر البتہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک سکان و ملاک برابر ہیں اور یہ حکم اجماعی کیسے ہو گیا؟
جواب: امام ابو یوسف کے قول کی وجہ تو ظاہر ہے کیونکہ وہ اپنے سابق اصول پر ہیں البتہ طرفین پر اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے تو انہوں نے اس کا یہ جواب دیا ہے کہ گھر اور محلہ منتقل نہیں کیا جاتا اور کشتی محول ہوتی ہے اور منتقل ہوتی ہے تو چوپائے کے مثل اسی پر ملکیت کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا بلکہ قبضہ کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے اور قبضہ کشتی پر ان سب کا ہے خواہ سوار ہوں یا مالک یا ملاح۔
He said: And if a murdered person is found on a ship, then the qasamah is upon those who are on it from the passengers and the sailors, because it is in their hands, and the wording includes its owners, so that it is obligatory upon the owners who are on it and upon the residents, and likewise upon those who pull it, whether owner or non-owner equally, and likewise the cart. This is apparent according to what is narrated from Abu Yusuf, and the distinction for the two (Sahibayn) is that the ship is moved and transferred, so possession is considered in it, not ownership, like an animal, contrary to the locality and house because they are not moved.
Translation: Quduri said: And if a murdered person is found on a ship, then qasamah is obligatory upon the people who are on the ship, i.e., passengers and crew, because the ship is in their possession, and the wording 'those on it' includes the owners of the ship, to the extent that qasamah is obligatory upon the owners of the ship who are on it and upon the residents, and similarly upon those who pull the ship, whether owner or non-owner equally, and similarly the cart. And this (equality of residents and owners) is apparent according to the narration of Abu Yusuf, and for the two (Sahibayn) the reason for distinction is that the ship is movable and transferable, so possession is considered in it, not ownership, like in an animal, contrary to the locality and house because they are not movable.
Explanation: If a murdered person is found inside a ship, then those who are inside the ship are liable for qasamah and diyah, whether they are passengers, owners, or crew, all will be guarantors, and the same applies to an ox-cart, and thus also to buses.
Question: In the previous lesson, the two (Sahibayn) said that only the owners of the house are liable for qasamah, not the residents, but according to Imam Abu Yusuf, residents and owners are equal. How is this ruling agreed upon?
Answer: The basis of Imam Abu Yusuf's statement is apparent because he follows his earlier principle. However, an objection arises against the two (Sahibayn), and they gave this response: A house and locality are not movable, whereas a ship is transferable and movable, so like an animal, ownership is not considered but rather possession is considered, and possession of the ship belongs to all of them, whether passengers, owners, or crew.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of qasamah (oaths) and diyah (blood money) when a murdered person is found on a ship. The matn states that qasamah is upon all who are on the ship: passengers, crew, and owners. The reason given is that the ship is in their possession. The commentary clarifies that this is the view of Imam Abu Yusuf. A distinction is made by the Sahibayn (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) between a ship and a fixed locality/house. In a fixed locality, only owners are liable because ownership is the basis of responsibility, but on a ship, because it is movable, effective possession (yad) is the basis, and all present share possession. Therefore, even according to the Sahibayn, on a ship all are liable, and there is no dispute on this point. The dispute is on fixed property: Abu Yusuf holds that residents and owners are equal, while the Sahibayn say only owners are liable. The explanation also extends the ruling to ox-carts and modern vehicles like buses, analogizing them to ships due to mobility.

Key Terms
قسامت (qasāmah): Compurgatory oath or collective liability when a murdered person is found in a locality, requiring swearing that no one among them killed him; failing which they pay diyah.
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid to the heirs of a murder victim when the killer is unknown or if qasamah is not performed.
قبضہ (qabḍah): Effective possession or control over an object, including both physical custody and legal authority.
ید (yad): Hand or possession; a legal term meaning effective control over an object.
ملکیت (milkiyyah): Ownership; the legal right of possession and disposition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) agree with Abu Yusuf that all persons on a ship are liable for qasamah when a dead body is found?
A) Because they all own shares of the ship.
B) Because the ship is movable, so possession (yad) is the basis of liability.
C) Because all are equally guilty of the murder.
D) Because the ship is considered a public place like a market.

Key Takeaway
On movable property (ship, cart, bus), all present share liability for qasamah because possession governs; on immovable property (house, locality), ownership governs and only owners are liable according to the Sahibayn.

Qasamah for a Dead Body in a Locality Mosque
Ruling statement: qasamah upon locality residents for body in their mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for qasamah when a dead body is found in a locality mosque and explain the rationale based on management responsibility.

Core Idea
A locality mosque's residents bear qasamah because its management and protection are their exclusive duty.

The location of a discovered body determines liability for qasamah. This lesson examines the specific case of a locality mosque (masjid al-mahallah), where the residents' duty to manage the mosque makes them liable if a murder occurs there without a known killer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is finding a murdered body in a locality mosque. The ruling: qasamah (and diyah) is upon the people of that locality.
Qasamah is a collective oath and payment of blood money when the killer is unknown.
2
Identify the liable party
The liable party is 'ahl al-mahallah' – the residents of the locality, not the general public or the mosque's imam.
The mahallah is a defined neighbourhood with its own mosque.
3
Analyse the rationale (illa)
The reason given: 'because its management is entrusted to them.' The residents have the duty to protect and manage the mosque, so they bear liability for crimes within it.
This connects duty (wajib) with liability (daman).
4
Distinguish from other mosques
Contrast with a congregational mosque (masjid al-jami') which is public. There, qasamah would fall on the general Muslim community or the ruler, not a specific locality.
This ruling is specific to local mosques with defined responsible residents.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if a body is found in a locality mosque, the residents collectively perform qasamah or pay diyah. This ensures the victim's family receives compensation.
The residents must swear fifty oaths to deny knowledge of the killer; if they cannot, they pay diyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإن وجد في مسجد محلة فالقسامة على أهلها لأن التدبير فيه إليهم
ترجمہ: قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر مقتول محلہ کی مسجد میں پایا گیا تو قسامت اہل محلہ پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ مسجد کے بارے میں تدبیر انہی کی طرف محول ہے۔

He said: And if a murdered person is found in the mosque of a locality, then the qasamah is upon its people because the management of it is entrusted to them.
Translation: Quduri said: And if a murdered person is found in the mosque of a locality, then qasamah is upon the people of the locality because the management of the mosque is referred to them.
Explanation: The protection etc. of the locality mosque is the duty of the people of the locality, therefore if a murdered person is found in the locality mosque, qasamah and diyah are obligatory upon the people of the locality.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This brief passage states the ruling for a dead body found in a locality mosque (masjid al-mahalla). The matn declares that qasamah is upon the people of that locality (ahl al-mahalla). The reasoning given is that the management (tadbir) and responsibility for the mosque belong to them. The commentary adds that the protection of the mosque is their duty, so they are liable. This is a pure ruling statement without any discussion of proofs or disputes. It stands as a distinct case from the congregational mosque (masjid al-jami') which is public.

Key Terms
محلہ (mahallah): A locality or neighbourhood; a distinct part of a town or city with its own mosque and community.
قسامت (qasamah): A collective oath taken by the residents of a locality to deny knowledge of a murder, and the subsequent payment of blood money if they cannot swear.
دیت (diyah): Blood money; financial compensation paid to the victim's heirs in cases of homicide where the killer is unknown or the death is accidental.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the mosque is privately owned by them.
B) Because they are responsible for the management and protection of the mosque.
C) Because they are the only ones who use the mosque.
D) Because the mosque is built on their land.

Key Takeaway
The residents of a locality are liable for qasamah and diyah if a murdered body is found in their local mosque, because its management is their responsibility.

Qasamah for Dead Bodies in Public Places
Ruling that no qasamah is required for dead bodies found in public places; diyah from Bait al-Mal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qasamah and diyah when a dead body is found in a public place, and explain the underlying principle of public ownership.

Core Idea
No qasamah for public places – the community's treasury pays diyah.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Islamic criminal law: a murdered person found in a location that belongs to the general public, such as the main congregational mosque, a public road, or a bridge. Unlike private areas where liability is assigned to residents, here no specific individual or group is responsible. The Hanafi ruling is clear: qasamah (the oath procedure) is not required, and the blood money (diyah) is paid from the public treasury (Bait al-Mal). This reflects the principle that what belongs to all is maintained by all.

Guided Path
1
Identify the location's nature
Determine whether the place where the body is found is fully public (owned by all Muslims) or private. Public examples: masjid al-jami', shari' a'zam, jisr (bridge).
A locality mosque is not fully public; it is associated with the local residents.
2
Assess liability for qasamah
If the place is fully public, there is no specific group to hold liable, so qasamah (oaths) is not applicable. The Prophet ﷺ exempted such places.
Qasamah is a pre-trial procedure to establish liability.
3
Determine the diyah payment
Since no one is directly responsible, the diyah falls on Bait al-Mal, the collective treasury of all Muslims.
Bait al-Mal is funded by public revenues; paying from it fulfills the community's duty.
4
Connect to the principle of public ownership
The ruling is based on the fact that these places are 'li al-ammah' – for the general public – and Bait al-Mal is also public property. Therefore, diyah is paid from common wealth.
This avoids injustice to any individual or small group.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن وجد في المسجد الجامع أو الشارع الأعظم فلا قسامة فيه والدية على بيت المال لأنه للعامة لا يختص به واحد منهم وكذا الجسور للعامة ومال بيت المال مال عامة المسلمين
ترجمہ: اور اگر مقتول جامع مسجد یا عام راستہ پر پایا جائے تو اس میں قسامت نہیں ہے اور دیت بیت المال پر ہے اس لئے کہ یہ (ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک) عام لوگوں کے لئے ہے لوگوں میں سے کوئی ان کے ساتھ مخصوص نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی ہیں عام لوگوں کے لئے پل۔ اور بیت المال کا مال عامتہ المسلمین کا ہے۔
تشریح: اگر جامع مسجد میں یا عام سڑک پر مقتول ہے تو اس صورت میں قسامت نہیں ہے اور دیت بیت المال سے ادا کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ کوئی تنہا شخص جامع مسجد یا عام سڑک یا پل کے ساتھ مخصوص نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ چیزیں عامۃ المسلمین کی ہیں اور بیت المال کا مال بھی عامۃ المسلمین کا ہے تو ان کے مال سے دیت ادا کر دی جائے گی۔
And if a murdered person is found in the congregational mosque or the main thoroughfare, then there is no qasamah in it, and the diyah is upon the treasury (Bait al-Mal) because it is for the general public, not specific to any one of them; likewise the bridges are for the general public, and the property of Bait al-Mal is the property of the general body of Muslims.
Translation: And if a murdered person is found in the congregational mosque or public road, then there is no qasamah in it, and diyah is upon Bait al-Mal because each of these is for the general public; no one is specifically associated with them; likewise bridges are for the general public, and the wealth of Bait al-Mal belongs to the general body of Muslims.
Explanation: If a murdered person is found in the congregational mosque or on a public road, then qasamah is not required, and diyah will be paid from Bait al-Mal. Because no single person is specifically associated with the congregational mosque, public road, or bridge; rather these things belong to the general Muslim public, and the wealth of Bait al-Mal also belongs to the general Muslim public, so diyah will be paid from their wealth.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage deals with dead bodies found in places that are universally accessible: the congregational mosque (masjid al-jami'), the main public street (al-shari' al-a'zam), and public bridges. Since no individual or specific group has exclusive control or management over these places, qasamah (the obligatory oath) is not imposed. Instead, the blood money (diyah) is borne by the Bait al-Mal (public treasury), because it is the collective wealth of all Muslims. The underlying principle is that liability falls upon those responsible for the place; when responsibility is shared by the entire community, the community's treasury pays.

Key Terms
جامع مسجد (masjid al-jāmi‘): The main Friday mosque where the entire community gathers, as opposed to a locality mosque.
بیت المال (bayt al-māl): The public treasury of the Islamic state, funded by revenues like zakat, booty, and khums.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the heirs of a murder victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a dead body is found in the main congregational mosque of a city, who pays the diyah?
A) The imam of the mosque.
B) The residents of the locality around the mosque.
C) The public treasury (Bait al-Mal).
D) The government officials.

Key Takeaway
Qasamah is not required for bodies found in fully public places; diyah falls on the collective treasury.

Liability for a Dead Body in a Market: Owned vs Public
Ruling on liability for a murdered person found in a market, with distinction between owned and public market

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on liability for a murder victim found in a privately owned market and apply the correct rule for public markets.

Core Idea
Liability for a body in a market depends on ownership: owners or residents pay; if public, Bait al-Mal pays.

This lesson addresses a specific fiqh scenario: a murdered person is found in a market, and the killer is unknown. The ruling for qasamah and diyah (blood money) depends on whether the market is privately owned or public. Within the Hanafi school, there is a key dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn on who bears liability for an owned market. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the rules of liability in different settings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A murdered person is found in a market with no known killer. The issue is who must pay diyah.
This is subject to the rules of qasamah.
2
Classify the market type
Determine whether the market is privately owned (mamluk) or public (like a market built on public streets).
The ruling depends on this classification.
3
Recall the two Hanafi views for owned market
For an owned market, Abu Yusuf holds residents are liable; the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold owners are liable.
The dispute is based on the underlying illa: possession vs ownership.
4
Apply the rule for public market
If the market is not owned, liability falls on Bait al-Mal because the place belongs to the general congregation of Muslims.
This is analogous to a public road or mosque.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو وجد في السوق ان كان مملوكا فعند أبي يوسف تجب على السكان وعندهما على المالك وان لم يكن مملوكا كالشوارع العامة التي بنيت فيها فعلى بيت المال لانه لجماعة المسلمين
ترجمہ: اور اگر مقتول بازار میں پایا جائے تو اگر وہ بازار مملوک ہو تو ابو یوسف کے نزدیک سکان پر دیت واجب ہے اور طرفین کے نزدیک مالک پر اور اگر مملوک نہ ہو جیسے وہ عام راستے جن پر بازار بنائے جائیں تو دیت بیت المال پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ یہ بازار جماعت مسلمین کے لئے ہے۔
تشریح: اگر مقتول بازار میں ملے تو بازار کو دیکھا جائے کہ مملوک ہے یا غیر مملوک اگر لوگوں کا مملوک ہو تو طرفین کے نزدیک مالکان سوق پر دیت واجب ہوگی اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ان لوگوں پر دیت واجب ہوگی جو بازار میں رہتے ہیں اور اگر مملوک نہیں جیسے عام راستوں پر بازار لگایا جائے تو اب دیت بیت المال پر واجب ہوگی اس لئے کہ یہ بازار جماعت مسلمین کا ہے اور بیت المال کا مال بھی انہی کا ہے تو بیت المال سے دیت ادا کی جائے گی۔
And if a murdered person is found in the market, then if it is owned (privately owned), according to Abu Yusuf it is obligatory upon the residents, and according to the two (Sahibayn) upon the owner. And if it is not owned, like the public streets upon which markets are built, then it is upon Bait al-Mal because it is for the congregation of Muslims.
Translation: And if a murdered person is found in the market, then if that market is owned, then according to Abu Yusuf diyah is obligatory upon the residents, and according to the two (Sahibayn) upon the owner. And if it is not owned, like the public streets upon which markets are built, then diyah will be upon Bait al-Mal because this market is for the congregation of Muslims.
Explanation: If a murdered person is found in the market, look at the market: is it owned or not? If it is owned by people, then according to the two (Sahibayn) diyah is obligatory upon the owners of the market, and according to Imam Abu Yusuf it is obligatory upon the people who reside in the market. And if it is not owned, like a market set up on public roads, then diyah will be obligatory upon Bait al-Mal because this market belongs to the congregation of Muslims, and the wealth of Bait al-Mal is also theirs, so diyah will be paid from Bait al-Mal.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for a dead body found in a market (suq). The ruling depends on whether the market is privately owned (mamluk) or public (like a market built on public streets). For an owned market, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the residents (sukkan) of the market are liable, while the two (Sahibayn: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that the owners (malik) are liable. This parallels the earlier distinction on fixed property: Abu Yusuf relies on possession, the Sahibayn on ownership. For a public market that is not owned, the liability falls on Bait al-Mal, because the place is for the general public, analogous to the congregational mosque and public street.

Key Terms
سوق (sūq): Marketplace; a physical location where commerce takes place, either privately owned or public.
بيت المال (Bait al-Mal): Public treasury; the financial institution of the Islamic state responsible for managing public funds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a dead body is found in a public market (ghayr mamluk), who is liable according to the Hanafi school?
A) The shopkeepers
B) The owners
C) Bait al-Mal
D) No one

Key Takeaway
Liability for a murdered person found in a market hinges on whether the market is privately owned (triggering a dispute between owners and residents) or public (triggering Bait al-Mal liability).

Qasamah for a Body in Prison: Abu Yusuf vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qasamah for a body found in prison

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn on liability for a dead body found in prison and explain the legal basis (nasrah) for the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Prisoners are too powerless to support each other—so Bait al-Mal bears the diyah, not them.

In this lesson, we examine an important intra-Hanafi dispute: when a murdered person is found inside a prison, who is liable for the diyah? Imam Abu Yusuf holds the inmates liable, while Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad argue the state pays. The key is the concept of nasrah (mutual support) and the prisoners' status as maqhur (overpowered). Understanding this dispute clarifies a major principle in qasamah law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
What exactly is the legal issue? A dead body is found in a prison; the killer is unknown. The question is: who must pay diyah and perform qasamah?
The default rule in Hanafi law is that residents of a place where a body is found are liable, but here an exception is claimed.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and his proof
Abu Yusuf holds that the inmates are liable because they are residents (sukkan) and have internal management (wilayat al-tadbir), making it apparent that the killing occurred among them.
He draws an analogy to residents of a house.
3
Explain the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that prisoners are overpowered (maqhur) and cannot support each other (la yatanasurūn), so the basis of qasamah—mutual support—is absent. Additionally, the prison is built for public benefit, so losses fall on the public treasury.
They emphasize the powerlessness of prisoners as the decisive factor.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical difference: according to Abu Yusuf, inmates must take oaths and pay diyah; according to the Sahibayn, no oaths and diyah from Bait al-Mal. The text presents the Sahibayn's view as the primary ruling, and it is the mufta bihi position.
This demonstrates how a single condition—powerlessness—can override the default rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو وجد في السجن فالدية على بيت المال وعلى قول أبي يوسف الدية والقسامة على أهل السجن لأنهم سكان وولاية التدبير إليهم والظاهر أن القتل حصل منهم وهما يقولان إن أهل السجن مقهورون فلا يتناصرون فلا يتعلق بهم ما يجب لأجل النصرة ولأنه بنى لاستيفاء حقوق المسلمين فإذا كان غنمه يعود إليهم فغرمه يرجع عليهم قالوا وهذه فريعة المالك والساكن وهى مختلف فيها بين أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف
ترجمہ: اور اگر مقتول قید خانے میں پایا جائے تو دیت بیت المال پر واجب ہوگی اور ابو یوسف کے قول کے مطابق دیت اور قسامت اہل قید خانہ پر ہے اس لئے کہ وہ سکان ہیں اور ولایت تدبیر ان کی طرف ہے اور ظاہر یہ ہے کہ قتل انہی میں سے ہوا ہے اور وہ دونوں (امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد) فرماتے ہیں کہ قید خانہ والے زبردست اور مجبور ہوتے ہیں لہذا وہ ایک دوسرے کی مدد نہیں کر سکتے تو وہ چیز جو نصرت کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتی ہے وہ ان پر واجب نہیں ہوگی اور اس لئے کہ قید خانہ مسلمانوں کے حقوق وصول کرنے کے لئے بنایا گیا ہے جب اس کا نفع انہی مسلمانوں کو پہنچتا ہے تو اس کا نقصان بھی ان پر واپس آتا ہے۔ انہوں نے کہا یہ فریعہ مالک و ساکن ہے اور اس میں ابود حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے درمیان اختلاف ہے۔
And if a murdered person is found in the prison, then the diyah is upon Bait al-Mal, and according to the saying of Abu Yusuf, the diyah and qasamah are upon the people of the prison because they are the residents and authority of management is entrusted to them, and it is apparent that the killing occurred from among them. And the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say that the people of the prison are overpowered and forced, so they cannot support each other, so what is obligatory due to mutual support is not obligatory upon them; and because the prison was built for the extraction of rights of Muslims, so if its benefit returns to them, its loss also reverts to them. They said: This is the branch (far'iah) of owner and resident, and there is a difference of opinion between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf concerning it.
Translation: And if a murdered person is found in the prison, then diyah is obligatory upon Bait al-Mal, and according to the saying of Abu Yusuf, the diyah and qasamah are upon the people of the prison because they are the residents and authority of management is entrusted to them, and it is apparent that the killing occurred from among them. And the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say that the people of the prison are overpowered (maqhur) and forced, so they cannot support each other, therefore that which is obligatory because of mutual support (nasrah) is not obligatory upon them; and because the prison was built for the purpose of exacting the rights of Muslims, so if its benefit accrues to them, its loss also reverts to them. They said: This is the branch of owner and resident, and there is a difference of opinion between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf concerning it.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage deals with a dead body found in a prison (sijn). The general ruling is that diyah is on Bait al-Mal, but Imam Abu Yusuf dissents, holding that both diyah and qasamah are on the inmates (ahl al-sijn) because they are the residents and have internal management (wilayat al-tadbir), and it is likely that the killing occurred among them. The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that prisoners are overpowered (maqhur), meaning they have no power to protect themselves or each other, so they cannot be held liable for failing to provide mutual support (nasrah), which is the basis of qasamah. Additionally, the prison is built for the public good of Muslims to exact justice, so the public treasury should bear losses. The commentary notes that this is a specific application (fari'ah) of the more general dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the liability of owners vs residents in fixed places.

Key Terms
مقهورون (maqhūrūn): Overpowered or coerced; prisoners who are under the control of authorities and cannot defend themselves or assist each other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do Abu Hanifa and Muhammad exempt prisoners from qasamah?
A) Prisoners are not residents of the prison.
B) Prisoners are overpowered and cannot support each other.
C) The prison is owned by the government.
D) There is no qasamah for prisons in general.

Key Takeaway
When a dead body is found in prison, the mufta bihi Hanafi ruling is that diyah is paid by Bait al-Mal, not the inmates, because prisoners are maqhur and cannot offer mutual support.

Testimony of Suspect Witnesses in Qasama: Ruling and Oath Wording Dispute
Ruling on testimony and oath wording difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony of suspect witnesses in qasama and distinguish between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's positions on the subsequent oath wording.

Core Idea
A suspect cannot testify to clear himself—the testimony is rejected, but the subsequent oath is tailored to preserve disclosed knowledge.

In qasama cases, when the guardian accuses a specific person, the entire neighborhood is under collective suspicion (khuṣūmat). If two neighbors testify against the accused, their testimony is rejected because they are themselves parties. However, a subtle difference arises between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the wording of the qasama oath for these witnesses. This lesson unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The guardian claims murder against a specific person from the neighborhood. Two people from that same neighborhood testify against the accused.
The witnesses are part of the collective suspect group.
2
Understand the basis for rejection
The testimony is rejected because the witnesses are themselves suspects (mutahhamūn). The collective hostility (khuṣūmat) against the entire neighborhood means each neighbor is a potential defendant.
A witness cannot remove suspicion from themselves by testifying against another.
3
Note the unanimous ruling
Both Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf agree that the testimony is not accepted.
The disagreement is only about the oath after rejection.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The difference concerns the wording of the qasama oath that these witnesses will later take along with the rest of the neighborhood.
Abu Yusuf: only swear 'we did not kill'. Abu Hanifa: swear the full standard oath including 'we do not know a killer'.
5
Compare the two positions
Abu Yusuf argues that since the witnesses have already disclosed knowledge of the killer by testifying, they cannot swear they do not know. Abu Hanifa maintains the full oath unchanged.
The reasoning hinges on consistency with prior testimony.

اور اگر ولی نے اہل محلہ میں سے کسی ایک معین شخص پرقتل کا دعوی کیا پس اہل محلہ میں سے دو شخصوں نے اس پر گواہی دی تو گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی اس لئے کہ خصومت کل کیسا تھ قائم ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور شاہد خصومت کو اپنے نفس سے ختم کرتا ہے تو وہ تم ہو گا اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ گواہوں سے یہ صاف لیا جائے گا ، اللہ ما قتلناہ ، اور اس پر اضافہ نہیں کئے جائیں گے اس لئے کہ یہ تو وہ خبر دے چکے ہیں کہ وہ قاتل کو پہچانتے ہیں۔ تشریح اہل محلہ میں سے کسی ایک معین شخص پر ولی مقتول نے قتل کا دعوی کیا جس پر اہل محلہ کے دو شخصوں نے اس پر قتل کی گواہی دی تو چونکہ یہ دونوں متہم ہیں اس لئے کہ ان کی شہادت کا مقصد اپنے کو خصم ہونے سے بچانا ہے حالانکہ تمام اہل محلہ خصم ہیں اس وجہ سے ان کی شہادت قبول نہیں کی جائے گی اس پر امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ ان کی گواہی قبول نہیں ہوگی جیسے مذکور ہو مگر ان کی اس گواہی سے یہ تو معلوم ہو گیا کہ یہ دونوں شاہد قاتل کو جانتے ہیں اس وجہ سے جب یہ دونوں گواہ اہل محلہ کے ساتھ قسامت کی قسم کھائیں گے تو ان دونوں کو فقط ان الفاظ سے قسم دی جائے گی کہ خدا کی قسم ہم نے اس مقتول کو قتل نہیں کیا یعنی دوسرے اہل محلہ کی طرح ان کو اپنی قسم میں یوں کہنے کی ضرورت نہیں ، بالله ما قتلناه ولاعرفنا له، قاتلا ، یعنی اس آخرى . جملہ کے اضافہ کی ضرورت نہیں رہی کیونکہ یہ دونوں پہلے ہی یہ گواہی دے چکے ہیں کہ اس کا قاتل فلاں ہے، اس لئے پہلے جملہ پر اکتفاء کیا جائے گا۔
And if the guardian claimed murder against a specific person from the people of the neighborhood, and two people from the neighborhood testified against him, then the testimony will not be accepted, because the hostility of all [the neighborhood] is established as we have explained in detail, and the witness removes the hostility from himself, so he becomes [free]. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that the witnesses will be asked to swear: 'By Allah, we did not kill him,' and no addition will be made because they have already informed that they know the killer. Commentary: If the guardian of the murdered person claims murder against a specific person from the neighborhood, and two people from the neighborhood testify to the murder, since both are suspects — because the purpose of their testimony is to save themselves from being the accused, while all the people of the neighborhood are suspects — their testimony is not accepted. Imam Abu Yusuf said: their testimony is not accepted as mentioned, but from this testimony it is known that these two witnesses know the killer. Therefore, when these two witnesses take the oath of qasama with the people of the neighborhood, they will be made to swear only with these words: 'By Allah, we did not kill this murdered person.' That is, unlike the other people of the neighborhood, they do not need to say in their oath: 'By Allah, we did not kill him, and we do not know a killer for him.' The addition of the last phrase is not needed because they have already testified that so-and-so is the killer. So the first phrase will suffice.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the testimony and oath of witnesses in a qasama case. The passage states the ruling that if the guardian accuses a specific person of murder, and two witnesses from the same neighborhood testify, their testimony is rejected because they themselves are suspects (they are part of the collective accused group). The reasoning is that a witness cannot remove the accusation from himself by testifying against another when he is also under suspicion. Imam Abu Yusuf agrees that the testimony is not accepted, but he adds a nuance about the oath: when these two witnesses later take the qasama oath along with the rest of the neighborhood, they should only swear that they did not kill the victim, and not add the phrase 'and we do not know a killer' — because they have already stated they know the killer by testifying. This clarifies the application of the oath for witnesses who have previously declared knowledge.

Key Terms
قسامت (qasāmah): A collective oath taken by the people of a neighborhood or tribe to deny responsibility for a murder when the killer is unknown.
خصومت (khuṣūmat): The legal opposition or hostility between parties; here, the collective suspicion against the entire neighborhood.
متہم (mutahham): A suspect; one who is under accusation or suspicion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the testimony of two witnesses from the same neighborhood not accepted when the guardian accuses a specific person of murder?
A) Because they are not trustworthy
B) Because they are themselves suspects in the case
C) Because they are minors
D) Because they are relatives of the accused

Key Takeaway
In qasama, a witness who is a suspect cannot testify; and among the Hanafi imams, the subsequent oath wording varies to avoid contradicting prior testimony.

Qasama and Diya for a Bedridden Victim Moved Home: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qasama for a moved wounded person who dies after bedrest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on qasama when a wounded person is moved and dies after being bedridden, and apply the key condition of 'sahib al-firash' to determine liability.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, a wound that causes death is like killing; for Abu Yusuf, qasama is only for murder, not wounding.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf over qasama (collective oath) and diya (blood money) when a victim is wounded in a locality, moved home, and eventually dies from the injury. The crucial factor is whether the victim remained bedridden (sahib al-firash) until death, which Abu Hanifa requires to link death to the wound, while Abu Yusuf insists that qasama applies only to homicide, not to mere wounding. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify conditions that trigger liability in Hanafi criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
Read the passage and note the sequence: Zaid is wounded in a tribe/neighborhood, then moved to his home, remains bedridden (sahib al-firash), and dies from the wound. This is the core case.
The movement away from the wound location is key to the dispute.
2
State the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
Abu Hanifa holds that qasama and diya are wajib on the locality. Abu Yusuf holds they are not wajib at all. Write down each position in one sentence.
This is a difference within the Hanafi school; both imams agree on other points.
3
Analyze the proofs (dalil) for each position
Abu Hanifa argues that the wound becomes the cause (sabab) of death, so it is treated like killing – analogous to a known murderer facing qisas. Abu Yusuf argues that qasama and diya are only for murder, not wounding, and moving the victim introduces uncertainty.
Pay attention to the role of causation and doubt (shakk).
4
Identify the key condition: sahib al-firash
Both imams agree that if the victim does NOT remain bedridden, qasama and diya are not due by consensus. The dispute hinges on the presence of continuous bedrest. Abu Hanifa sees bedrest as sufficient to attribute death definitively to the wound; Abu Yusuf sees it as insufficient because the death occurred elsewhere.
This condition is unique to Abu Hanifa's reasoning and illustrates the use of istihsan.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In practice, if a mufti follows Abu Hanifa, the locality must pay diya unless they successfully take qasama. If following Abu Yusuf, no liability arises. This affects real-world cases of unknown assailants.
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is not given here; later Hanafi works generally favour Abu Hanifa's view under certain conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القسامة
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹ تشریح زید کوکسی قبیلہ یا محلہ میں زخمی کر دیا گیا پھر اس کو اٹھا کر اس کے گھر منتقل کر دیا گیا اور وہ برا بر صاحب فراش رہا یہاں تک کہ اس زخم سے مر گیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس قبیلہ یا محلہ والوں پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک قسامت ودیت کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ ویوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس محلہ میں اس کو فقط زخمی کیا گیا تھا اور قسامت ودیت قتل میں واجب ہوتی ہے نہ کہ غیر قتل میں ، تو جیسے صاحب فراش نہ رہنے کی صورت میں اگر وہ مر جائے تو بالاتفاق قسامت و دبیت نہیں ہے تو اسی طرح یہاں بھی قسامت و دیت واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب زخم موت کا سبب بن جاتا ہے تو زخم کو تل ہی کا درجہ دیا جاتا ہے یہی تو وجہ ہے کہ اگر قاتل معین ومعلوم ہو تو ایسی صورت میں اس پر قصاص واجب ہوتا ہے لہذا یہاں قسامت و دیت واجب ہوگی تو اگر وہ برابر صاحب فراش کر مر گیا تو موت اسی زخم کی جانب مضاف ہو گی اور اگر وہ صاحب فراش نہیں رہا تو اب اس میں احتمالات پیدا ہو گئے ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ اس زخم کی وجہ سے مرا ہو اور ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ اس زخم کی وجہ سے نہ مرا ہو تو شک پیدا ہو گیا لہذا شک کی وجہ سے قسامت اور دبیت واجب نہ ہوگی ۔
Chapter of Qasama. Explanation: Zaid was wounded in a tribe or neighborhood, then he was lifted and transferred to his home, and he remained bedridden until he died from that wound. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, qasama and diya are wajib upon the people of that tribe or neighborhood. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, qasama and diya are not wajib at all. His proof is that in this neighborhood he was only wounded, and qasama and diya are wajib in murder, not in non-murder. So, just as when he does not remain bedridden and dies, by consensus qasama and diya are not due, similarly here qasama and diya will not be wajib. Proof of Imam Abu Hanifa: when the wound becomes the cause of death, the wound is given the status of death itself. This is why if the murderer is known and specified, qisas is wajib upon him. Therefore here qasama and diya will be wajib. So if he remained bedridden continuously and died, death is attributed to that wound. And if he did not remain bedridden, then possibilities arise: maybe he died due to the wound and maybe not. So doubt occurs; due to doubt, qasama and diya are not wajib.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding qasama (collective oath) and diya (blood money) when a person is wounded in a specific locality, then moved to his home, remains bedridden, and subsequently dies from the wound. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the people of that locality are liable for qasama and diya because the wound was the direct cause of death and the victim remained bedridden (sahib al-firash), connecting the death to the initial injury. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that qasama and diya are only for homicide, not for wounding alone; since the death occurred elsewhere and the connection is uncertain, no liability arises unless the victim remained in the same place until death. The key condition is whether the victim remained bedridden ('ala firashihi). Both imams agree that if the victim did not remain bedridden, no liability. Abu Hanifa emphasizes that when the wound is the effective cause (sabab) of death, it is treated like actual killing, analogous to a known murderer facing qisas. Abu Yusuf maintains strict adherence to the requirement that the death be clearly linked to the locality. The passage is an example of istihsan (juristic preference) versus strict qiyas.

Key Terms
قسامة (qasama): Collective oath taken by the locality to deny involvement in a homicide, plus payment of diya.
دیت (diya): Blood money paid as compensation for killing or injury.
صاحب فراش (sahib al-firash): A bedridden person confined to bed due to injury; staying in bed continuously.
عاقلہ (aqila): The agnate relatives of a person who collectively pay diya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key condition that Imam Abu Hanifa requires for qasama and diya to be wajib when a wounded person is moved home?
A) The victim must die within 24 hours of the wound.
B) The victim must remain bedridden (sahib al-firash) until death.
C) The wound must be inflicted in a public place.
D) The killer must be unknown.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi qasama law, the condition of continuous bedrest (sahib al-firash) determines whether a wound that leads to death is linked to the location, triggering liability for the community.

Liability of the Carrier of a Wounded Person
Intra-Hanafi dispute on carrier liability for death of wounded person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the analogy of yad to mahalla to determine the carrier's liability for diya, and distinguish between Abu Hanifa's qiyas and Abu Yusuf's position.

Core Idea
A carrier's possession of a wounded person may make him liable for diya, just as a locality is liable — but Abu Yusuf rejects this analogy.

Carrying a critically wounded person seems like a good deed, but what if the person dies afterwards? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: Abu Hanifa's qiyas holds the carrier liable because his control over the victim is like a locality's custody, while Abu Yusuf exempts him. This lesson unpacks the analogy and its limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two positions
Read the passage and note: a wounded person with life remaining is carried to his home, dies after 1-2 days. Abu Yusuf says no liability; Abu Hanifa's qiyas says liable.
The dispute is about whether the carrier becomes a damin.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's qiyas: yad equals mahalla
Abu Hanifa analogizes the carrier's hand (possession) to the locality (mahalla). Just as a locality where a wounded person is found becomes liable for diya (via qasama), so does the carrier's possession create liability.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) because the illa is the custodial control over the victim.
3
Recall the earlier case of tribe/neighborhood
The passage references a prior discussion: if a wounded person is found in a domicile or tribe, the inhabitants are liable. Abu Hanifa extends that principle to anyone who has yad over the victim.
The earlier case likely involves qasama (oath-taking) which establishes liability on a locality.
4
Evaluate Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf rejects the analogy. His objection is not fully restated here, but from context he likely argued that the carrier's action is transient and uncertain, unlike a fixed locality. The carrier may have acted out of goodwill, and the death might not be caused by the move.
The uncertainty (shubha) in causation may break the analogy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa's qiyas, the carrier must pay diya; under Abu Yusuf, no diya. The ruling affects who bears the financial burden of the death.
The mufta bihi is not specified in the text; both views exist in the school.

ولو أن رجلا معه جرح به رمق حمله إنسان إلى أهله فمكث يوما أو يومين ثم مات لم يضمن الذي حمله إلى أهله في قول أبي يوسف وفى قياس قول أبي حنيفة يضمن؛ لأن يده بمنزلة المحلة فوجوده جريحا في يده کوجوده فيها وقد ذكرنا وجهى القولين فيما قبله من مسألة القبيلة ترجمہ اور اگر کوئی شخص زخمی ہو جس میں جان باقی ہو اس کو کسی انسان نے اٹھا کر اس کے گھر پہنچا دیا پس وہ پھرا ایک دن یا دو دن پھر وہ مر گیا تو ابو یوسف کے قول کے مطابق اس کو اس کے گھر تک اٹھانے والا ضائن نہ ہوگا اور ابو حنیفہ کے قول کے قیاس کے مطابق ضامن ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس کا قبضہ محلہ کے درجہ میں ہے تو مقتول کا زخمی ہونے کی حالت میں اس کے قبضہ میں پایا جانا مقتول کے زخمی ہونے کی حالت میں محلہ میں پائے جانے کی مثل ہے اور ہم دونوں قوالوں کی وجہ ذکر کر چکے ماقبل میں یعنی قبیلہ والے مسئلہ میں۔ تشریح ایک شخص زخمی ہے جس میں کچھ جان باقی ہے اس کو کوئی اٹھا کر اس کے گھر لے گیا اور اسی حال میں وہ ایک دو دن کے بعد مر گیا تو امام ابو یوسف کا قول یہ ہے کہ اٹھانے والا اس کا ضامن نہ ہوگا اور ابو حنیفہ کا قیاس یہ کہتا ہے کہ وہ ضامن ہوگا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل اس پر امام ابوحنیفہ یہ دلیل بیان کرتے ہیں کہ اس زخمی کا اٹھانے والے کے قبضہ میں موت ایسا ہے جیسے محلہ میں ہوتا اور ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اگر محلہ میں زخمی پایا جائے اور اس کو اٹھا کر گھر لایا جائے تو اہل محلہ ضامن ہوتے میں اسی طرح یہاں اٹھانے والا ضامن ہو گا اور امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل بھی وہیں گزر چکی ہے۔
And if a man has a wound with life remaining, a person carries him to his family, then he stays a day or two, then dies: the one who carried him to his family is not liable according to Abu Yusuf, and according to the qiyas of Abu Hanifa he is liable, because his hand is like the locality, so his finding the wounded person in his hand is like finding him in it. And we have mentioned the aspects of the two opinions previously in the question of the tribe. Translation: And if a person is wounded with some life remaining, a human being carries him to his home, then he stays one or two days, then he dies, then according to Abu Yusuf's statement the carrier to his home is not liable, and according to the qiyas of Abu Hanifa's statement he is liable, because his possession is like the locality, so the murdered person being found wounded in his possession is like being found wounded in the locality. And we have mentioned the reasons for both statements previously in the tribe question. Explanation: A person is wounded with some life remaining; someone carries him to his home and in that state he dies after one or two days. Imam Abu Yusuf's statement is that the carrier is not liable, and Abu Hanifa's qiyas says he is liable. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: this wounded person's death in the carrier's possession is like being in the locality, and it has passed previously that according to Imam Sahib, if a wounded person is found in a locality and is brought home, the people of the locality are liable; similarly here the carrier is liable. And Imam Abu Yusuf's proof has also passed there.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: a wounded person with some life remaining is carried by someone to his home, then dies after a day or two. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the carrier is not liable (does not guarantee diya). According to a qiyas based on Imam Abu Hanifa's view, the carrier is liable because his possession (yad) is analogous to the locality (mahalla). Just as the locality becomes liable if a wounded person is found there and dies, similarly the carrier's control over the victim makes him responsible. However, Imam Abu Yusuf distinguishes, likely because the carrier's act of moving may introduce uncertainty. The commentary references the earlier discussion of the tribe/neighborhood, indicating the same reasoning applies.

Key Terms
ضامن (damin): The person liable for compensation (diya) for the death.
ید (yad): Possession, control; used analogously to locality.
محلہ (mahalla): Locality or neighborhood; an area that can be liable for qasama.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The carrier caused the wound.
B) The carrier's possession is like the locality.
C) The carrier admitted guilt.
D) The carrier was the victim's relative.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the possession (yad) of a carrier of a wounded person can create liability for diya by analogy to the locality, but Abu Yusuf's view exempts the carrier due to the uncertainty of causation.

Blood Money for a Person Found Killed in His Own House: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diya liability when a murder victim is discovered in his own house.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding diya when a murdered person is found in his own house, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar) based on the timing of liability (zuhur al-qatl vs. time of wounding).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa ties diya to the time of discovery; Sahibayn tie it to the time of wounding.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether blood money (diya) is due when a person is found murdered in his own house. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the diya is payable on the 'aqila of the victim's heirs, while Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar hold that no diya is due because the victim's ownership of the house at the time of wounding makes it as if he killed himself. The key difference lies in the timing of the obligation: zuhur al-qatl (manifestation of murder) versus the moment of wounding.

Guided Path
1
State the Issue
Identify the legal question: Is diya due when a murdered person is found in his own house?
The source assumes the murder is discovered with no known killer.
2
Identify the Two Positions
State Abu Hanifa's position (diya on the 'aqila of the heirs) and the Sahibayn's position (no diya; blood is wasted).
The Sahibayn include Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Zufar.
3
Compare the Underlying Principles
Understand the difference: Sahibayn focus on possession at the time of wounding; Abu Hanifa focuses on the manifestation of murder (zuhur al-qatl).
This is a difference in usul regarding when liability attaches.
4
Analyze the Mukatib Exception
Note that Abu Hanifa makes an exception for a mukatib (slave under contract of manumission) because his house remains his property at the time of discovery, so it is as if he killed himself.
This exception confirms the rule: liability depends on who owns the house at zuhur.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the heirs receive diya; under Sahibayn, they receive nothing. This affects the 'aqila's obligation.
The mufta bihi is not specified in this text, but Abu Hanifa's reasoning is elaborated.

قسامت وقت جرح میں واجب نہیں بلکہ قسامت جب واجب ہے جبکہ قتل کا ظہور ہو جائے اور ظہور کاذب ہوا ہے اور اب حال یہ ہے کہ اس گھرکا مالک مقتول نہیں رہا بلکہ اس کے ورثہ ہو گئے لہذا دیت گھر والوں کے عاقلہ پر واجب ہو گی اور ورثہ کومل جائے گی، یعنی گھر والوں کو ۔ اور رہی اس کی دلیل کہ قتل کے ظہور کے وقت قسامت واجب ہوتی ہے تو وہ یہ ہے کہ ظہور قتل سے پہلے عاقلہ میں سے جو مر گیا تو اس کے ترکہ میں سے دیت ادا نہیں کی جائے گی ، تو اگر قسامت ودیت کا وجوب قبل ظہور ہوتا تو اس کے ترکہ میں سے دیت ادا ہونی چاہئے تھی ، البتہ اگر مکاتب کا اپنا ذاتی مکان تھا جس میں وہ مقتول پایا گیا تو اس کا خون بدر ہے ، اس لئے کہ جب اس کا قتل ظاہر ہوا تو یہ مکان تب بھی اس مکاتب کی ملک ہے اس لیے کہ مکاتب کی موت سے عقد کتابت باطل نہیں ہوتا جبکہ وہ بدل کتابت کے برابر مال چھوڑ کر مرے تو جب یہ مکان ظہور قتل کے وقت بھی اسی کی ملک قرار دیا گیا تو کسی پر منمان واجب نہ ہوگا بلکہ اس خون بدر ہوگا کیونکہ ایسا سمجھا جائے گا گویا کہ اس نے خود اسے کو قتل کیا ہے۔
And if a man is found killed in his own house, his diya is on his 'aqila for his heirs according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar said: there is nothing in it, because the house was in his possession at the time the wound was found, so it is as if he killed himself, so it is wasted. Translation: And if a man is found killed in his own house, his diya is on his 'aqila for his heirs according to Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar said: there is nothing in it, because when the wound was found, the house is in his possession, so it will be considered as if he killed himself, so it is wasted. Explanation: If a person is found killed in his own house, according to Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar, his blood is wasted and nothing is wajib on anyone, because when he was wounded, the owner of the house was this person himself, so no one else is liable. And Imam Abu Hanifa says: his heirs will receive his diya, and the 'aqila of the deceased will bear it. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is coming. Proof of the Great Imam: and for him is that qasama is only wajib based on the manifestation of murder (zuhur al-qatl), and for this reason, the person who dies before that manifestation does not enter into the diya. And at the time of manifestation of murder, the house belongs to the heirs, so diya is wajib on their 'aqila, unlike a mukatib if he is found killed in his own house, because at the time of manifestation of his murder, the house remains under the ruling of his ownership, so it becomes as if he killed himself, so his blood is wasted. Translation: And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that qasama is wajib based on the manifestation of murder, and for this reason the person who dies before the manifestation of murder will not be included in the diya. And at the time of manifestation of murder, the house belongs to the heirs, so diya is wajib on the 'aqila of the heirs. Unlike a mukatib if he is found killed in his own house, because at the time his murder becomes apparent, the house remains under the ruling of his ownership, so it becomes as if he killed himself, so his blood is wasted. Explanation: This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa. The summary: qasama is not wajib at the time of wounding; rather, qasama is wajib when the murder becomes manifest. And the manifestation has occurred. And now the situation is that the owner of this house is not the deceased but his heirs, so diya is wajib on the 'aqila of the house owners (i.e., the heirs) and the heirs will receive it. As for his proof that qasama is wajib at the time of manifestation of murder: that is because if someone from the 'aqila dies before manifestation, diya is not paid from his estate. If the obligation of qasama and diya were before manifestation, then diya would have to be paid from his estate. However, if a mukatib had his own personal house and was found killed in it, his blood is wasted, because when his murder became apparent, the house was still the property of this mukatib. This is because the death of a mukatib does not invalidate the contract of kitabah if he leaves behind property equal to the kitabah price. So when this house at the time of manifestation of murder is considered his property, no liability falls on anyone; rather, his blood is wasted, because it is understood that he killed himself.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling when a person is found murdered (cadaver) inside his own house. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the diya (blood money) is due on his 'aqila (agnatic relatives) and given to his heirs. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar hold that no blood money is due; the blood is wasted (hadar). Their reasoning: since the house was under his possession at the time of the wounding, it is as if he killed himself, so no liability. Abu Hanifa's argument: qasama and diya are based on the apparent occurrence of murder (zuhur al-qatl). At the time of discovery, the house belongs to the heirs (since the victim died), so diya falls on their 'aqila. An exception is a mukatib (slave under contract of manumission): if found killed in his own house, his blood is wasted because the house remains his property at the time of discovery (since the kitabah contract keeps him as owner until full payment), so it is as if he killed himself.

Key Terms
مکاتَب (mukatib): A slave who has made a contract (kitabah) with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
ہدر (hadar): Wasted, no blood money due; the blood is considered forfeit.
ظہور قتل (zuhur al-qatl): The manifestation or discovery of the murder, as opposed to the time of wounding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the exception to Abu Hanifa's ruling on diya for a person found killed in his own house?
A) If the victim is a mukatib.
B) If the victim is a minor.
C) If the victim is a woman.
D) If the house is rented.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's position that diya is due at the time of discovery (zuhur al-qatl) is distinguished from the Sahibayn's position focusing on the time of wounding, with an exception for a mukatib whose blood is wasted.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Diyah Liability Between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diyah liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the basis of the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding diyah liability and apply the principle of al-zahir to analogous scenarios.

Core Idea
When two men are alone and one is found dead, the norm (al-zahir) that people do not kill themselves determines liability.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the surviving man must pay diyah when his companion is found killed. Imam Muhammad argues that the possibility of suicide creates doubt and negates liability, while Imam Abu Yusuf relies on the apparent norm (al-zahir) that a person does not kill himself, making the survivor liable. The lesson explores their reasoning and the later juristic discussion on which view is mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and each imam's ruling
Read the source text carefully. Note the scenario: two men in a house, no third person, one found slaughtered. Identify the rulings of Abu Yusuf (diyah wajib) and Muhammad (no diyah).
This is a pure intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Follow Imam Muhammad's proof
Muhammad argues that it is possible (ihtimal) the deceased killed himself and possible the other killed him. Since both possibilities exist, certainty is lacking, and the survivor cannot be held liable due to doubt.
The key term is 'ihtimal' (possibility) leading to 'shakk' (doubt).
3
Analyse Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf relies on al-zahir: the apparent norm is that people do not commit suicide. Therefore, the conjecture (tawahhum) of suicide is dropped, and the default is murder by the other person.
The phrase 'al-zahir anna al-insan la yaqtulu nafsah' is the core of his argument.
4
Note the analogy to qasama
Abu Yusuf draws an analogy to a body found in a neighborhood (qaṭīl fī maḥalla): there, the community is liable because the norm is murder. Here too, the norm applies, so the survivor is liable.
This qiyas strengthens Abu Yusuf's position.
5
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: if Muhammad's view is followed, no diyah is paid; if Abu Yusuf's, the survivor pays full diyah. The commentary notes that later scholars differed on which is mufta bihi.
This dispute remains unresolved in the text, reflecting the richness of Hanafi jurisprudence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أن رجلين كانا في بيت وليس معهما ثالث فوجد أحدهما مذبوحا قال أبو يوسف يضمن الآخر الدية وقال محمد لا يضمنه لأنه يحتمل أنه قتل نفسه ويحتمل أنه قتله الآخر فلا يضمنه بالشك ولأبي يوسف أن الظاهر أن الإنسان لا يقتل نفسه فكان التوهم ساقطا كما إذا وجد قتيل في محلة.
If two men were in a house with no third with them, and one of them is found slaughtered, Abu Yusuf said: The other guarantees the diyah. Muhammad said: He does not guarantee it, because it is possible that he killed himself, and it is possible that the other killed him, so he does not guarantee it due to doubt. And Abu Yusuf's proof is that the apparent situation is that a person does not kill himself, so the conjecture is dropped, just as when a killed person is found in a neighborhood.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding a case where two men are alone in a house and one is found murdered. Imam Muhammad argues that since it is possible the deceased committed suicide, the surviving companion cannot be held liable for diyah due to uncertainty. Imam Abu Yusuf relies on the general norm (al-zahir) that people do not kill themselves; suicide is rare. Therefore, the possibility of suicide is rejected (sāqit), and the surviving companion is liable. Abu Yusuf draws an analogy to a case where a body is found in a neighborhood: the residents bear collective responsibility because the default is homicide. The commentary notes that later scholars differed on which view is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
قسامة (qasāma): In this context, qasāma refers to the procedure of oaths taken by the accused or the community to deny responsibility for a murder found in their area. The dispute here is about diyah, not qasāma.
دية (diya): Blood money, a financial compensation for homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, why is the surviving man liable for diyah when the other is found killed in their shared house?
A) Because the deceased was known to be wealthy
B) Because the apparent norm (al-zahir) is that people do not kill themselves
C) Because the surviving man confessed
D) Because the deceased was a guest

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the norm (al-zahir) that people do not kill themselves shifts the burden of proof to the survivor, but this principle is contested within the school, reflecting the balance between certainty and probability.

Who Bears Qasama When a Woman Owns a Village?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qasama when a woman owns a village.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on qasama when a woman owns a village, and identify the later tarjih.

Core Idea
The suspicion of murder falls on the owner, not the defender — qasama follows tuhma, not nusrah.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about qasama when a woman owns a village and a body is found there. The two views turn on whether the basis of qasama is suspicion (tuhma) or capacity for defense (nusrah). Understanding this distinction clarifies the Hanafi approach to collective responsibility.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold: the woman takes qasama (oaths) and diyah is on her 'aqila.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Abu Yusuf places both qasama and diyah on the 'aqila because women are not among ahl al-nusrah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Abu Yusuf's dalil: qasama is only required from those capable of defense; a woman is like a child.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue qasama aims to remove suspicion; the woman is the suspect, so she must swear.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If woman takes qasama, she swears 50 oaths alone; if 'aqila, they collectively swear. Diyah always on 'aqila, but later scholars add woman to diyah.
The practical difference in procedure and financial responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو وجد قتيل في قرية لامرأة فعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد القسامة عليها تكرر عليها الأيمان والدية على عاقلتها أقرب القبائل إليها في النسب وقال أبو يوسف القسامة على العاقلة أيضا لأن القسامة إنما تجب على من كان من أهل النصرة والمرأة ليست من أهلها فشبهت الصبي.
If a killed person is found in a village belonging to a woman, then according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the qasama is upon her, oaths are repeated upon her, and the diyah is upon her 'aqila (the closest tribe in lineage). Abu Yusuf said: The qasama is also upon the 'aqila, because qasama is only obligatory upon one who is among the people of support (ahl al-nusrah), and a woman is not among them, so she resembles a child.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a woman who owns an entire village where a body is found. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad rule that the burden of qasama falls on the woman herself because the suspicion of murder (tuhma) rests on her as owner. However, the diyah is paid by her 'aqila (paternal relatives). Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees: he places the entire burden of qasama on the 'aqila as well, arguing that qasama is only required from those capable of offering defense (ahl al-nusrah). Women, like children, are not considered capable, so they cannot be subject to qasama. The commentary also includes a later opinion (mutakhkhirin) that the woman may join the 'aqila in contributing to diyah because she is considered a killer (qatila) in this context.

Key Terms
عاقلة (ʿāqila): The paternal relatives of a person who are collectively responsible for paying diyah in cases of accidental or semi-intentional homicide.
نصرة (nusrah): Support, defense; the capacity and responsibility to protect an area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad regarding qasama when a woman owns a village where a body is found?
A) The woman's 'aqila must take the qasama
B) The woman herself must take the qasama
C) The entire village takes the qasama
D) No qasama is required

Key Takeaway
Qasama is imposed on the person against whom suspicion lies, not necessarily the one with capacity for defense.

Liability for Qasama on Private Land Adjacent to a Village
Ruling on qasama liability for private landowner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on qasama and diyah liability when a body is found on private land adjacent to a village and apply the rationale of nusrah to similar cases.

Core Idea
The landowner, not the villagers, bears qasama and diyah for a body found on his land.

This short passage from the matn presents a specific scenario in qasama law: a killed person is found on private land next to a village, and the landowner is not from that village. The ruling is clear and hinges on the concept of nusrah—the right and duty to defend one's property. Understanding this ruling helps clarify how the Hanafi school apportions responsibility based on ownership rather than mere proximity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage and note all key elements: a dead body (قتيل) is found on someone's land (أرض رجل) which is adjacent to a village (إلى جانب قرية), and the landowner is not from the villagers (ليس صاحب الأرض من أهلها).
The key phrase 'ليس صاحب الأرض من أهلها' distinguishes this case from one where the landowner is also a villager.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that the liability (qasama and diyah) falls on the landowner (هو على صاحب الأرض). Articulate it precisely: the landowner must perform qasama and pay diyah.
The pronoun 'هو' refers to the ruling (الحكم) or the liability.
3
Extract the rationale
The reason given is 'لأنه أحق بنصرة أرضه من أهل القرية'—because he has more right to the defense (nusrah) of his land than the villagers. Nusrah here means protective authority and responsibility.
Nusrah is a key term; it links ownership to responsibility for unexplained deaths on the property.
4
Contrast with other scenarios
Consider what the ruling would be if the landowner were from the village, or if the land were common. This ruling applies specifically when the landowner is not a villager, showing ownership overrides communal proximity.
This helps internalize the principle that qasama follows the one with primary protective duty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو وجد رجل قتيلا في أرض رجل إلى جانب قرية ليس صاحب الأرض من أهلها قال هو على صاحب الأرض لأنه أحق بنصرة أرضه من أهل القرية.
If a man is found killed on the land of a man adjacent to a village, and the landowner is not among its inhabitants, he said: It is upon the landowner, because he has more right to the defense of his land than the villagers.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage gives a clear ruling from the matn regarding a body found on private land adjacent to a village when the landowner is not a resident of that village. The qasama and diyah fall on the landowner alone, not on the villagers. The reason is that the landowner has a stronger claim to defend his own land than the villagers do. This is based on the principle that qasama attaches to those who have the duty of protection (nusrah) for the area. Since the land is privately owned by him, he is primarily responsible for any unexplained death found on it.

Key Terms
نصرة (nusrah): Support, defense; the capacity and responsibility to protect an area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a body is found on private land adjacent to a village and the landowner is not from the village, who is liable for qasama and diyah?
A) The villagers
B) The landowner
C) Both equally
D) No one

Key Takeaway
Ownership, not proximity, determines the primary liability for unexplained deaths on private land.

8 min
Diyah on 'Aqila for Shibh 'Amd and Khata'
States the ruling and provides both naqli and aqli proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who bears the diyah in cases of shibh 'amd and khata', and explain both the textual (hadith) and rational (istihsan) proofs.

Core Idea
In shibh 'amd and khata', diyah is wajib on the 'aqila, not the killer, to combine justice with mercy.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling: when a killing is not fully intentional (shibh 'amd) or accidental (khata'), the diyah is paid by the killer's support group (the 'aqila), not by the killer himself. The passage from al-Quduri presents both a hadith proof and a rational argument based on istihsan, showing how the Hanafi school balances the inviolability of life with mercy for the excused killer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first lines of the source: the diyah in shibh 'amd and khata' is upon the 'aqila. Identify the key terms: 'aqila (the payers of diyah), shibh 'amd (quasi-intentional), khata' (accidental).
The ruling applies only when the diyah is the direct consequence of the killing (not through sulh or confession).
2
Examine the textual proof
The hadith of Hammal ibn Malik: the Prophet ordered the killer's relatives ('aqila) to pay the diyah. Note that the imperative 'Qumu' (stand up) indicates obligation (wujub) per Hanafi usul.
This hadith is ahad and zanni, but it is the primary textual basis.
3
Analyze the rational proof
The killer in shibh 'amd and khata' is excused (ma'dhur). Imposing a heavy payment on him would be punitive and ruin him, which contradicts the principle of mercy. Therefore, liability is shifted to the 'aqila, who share responsibility for the killer's actions.
This is istihsan: overriding qiyas (which would place liability on the killer) to avoid hardship.
4
Understand the concept of 'aqila
The 'aqila are those who support the killer. In the Hanafi school, they are defined as ahl al-diwan (army register) or, if not, the tribe/family. The Shafi'i school defines them as the 'ashira (clan).
This difference affects who pays in practice.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario of accidental killing, identify the type (shibh 'amd/khata') and determine that the 'aqila bears the diyah, not the killer. Check if the diyah is by reason of the killing itself.
If the killer confesses or settles, the ruling may differ (not covered here).

Source Text
