قال والدية في شبه العمد والخطاء وكل دية تجب بنفس القتل على العاقلة والعاقلة الذين يعقلون يعنى يؤدون العقل و هو الدية وقد ذكره فى الديات والاصل فى وجوبها على العاقلة قوله عليه السلام في حديث حمل بن مالک رضی الله عنه للاولياء قوموا فدوه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور دیت شبہ عمد اور خطاء میں اور ہر وہ دیت جو نفس قتل کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتی ہے وہ عاقلہ پر ہے، اور عاقلہ وہ لوگ ہیں جو عقل یعنی دیت ادا کرتے ہیں اور ہم اس کو " کتاب الدیات میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں اور اصل عاقلہ پر دیت کے وجوب میں نبی کا فرمان ہے حمل بن مالک کی حدیث میں مجرم کے اولیاء سے تم کھڑے ہو جاؤ پس اس کی دیت ادا کرو۔ تشریح ہر وہ دیت جو نفس قتل کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتی ہے یعنی دم عمد سے مصالحت کی وجہ سے نہیں اور پر ہونے کی وجہ سے نہیں بلکہ نفس قتل کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتی ہو یعنی اس قتل کا موجب ہی دیت ہو خواہ قتل بہ عہ ہو یا قتل خلکو تو ایسی دبیت خود قاتل پر واجب نہ ہوگی بلکہ اس کی مددگار برادری پر واجب ہوگی اور دیات کی تفصیل کتاب الدیات میں گذر چکی ہے۔
اب رہی یہ بات کہ دیت کا وجوب عاقلہ پر کیوں ہے؟ تو اس کے بارے میں مصنف نے ایک حدیث پیش فرما دی جس میں آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے قاتل کے اولیاء کو دیت ادا کرنے کا حکم فرمایا ہے۔
حدیث کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ حمل بن مالکٹ کی دو بیویاں تھیں ان میں سے ایک نے دوسری کو خیمہ کی لکڑی ماری جس سے اس کا حمل ساقط ہوا اور خود بھی مرگئی اس پر آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مضاربہ کے اولیاء کو حکم فرمایا کہ اس کی دیت ادا کرو۔
دلیل عقلی
ولان النفس محترمة لا وجه الى الاهدار والخاطئ معذور و كذا الذى تولى شبه العمد نظرا الى الآلة فلا وجه الى ايجاب العقوبة عليه و في ایجاب مال عظیم احجافه و استیصاله فيصير عقوبة فضم اليه العاقلة تحقيقا للتخفيف و انما خصوا بالضم لانه انما قصر لقوة فيه و تلک بانصاره و هم العاقلة فكانوا هم المقصرين في تركهم مراقبته فخصوا به
ترجمہ اور اس لئے کہ نفس محترم ہے جس کے بعدار کی کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے اور خاطی معذور ہے اور ایسے ہی وہ شخص جو شبہ عد کا متولی ہوا آلہ کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے تو اس پر عقوبت واجب کرنے کی کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے اور مال کے واجب کرنے میں اس کو پریشانی میں مبتلا کرنا اور اس کو ہلاک کرنا ہے تو یہ ایجاب مال ) عذاب ہوگا تو اسکی جانب عاقلہ کو ملا دیا جائے گا تخفیف کی تحقیق کی غرض سے اور ملانے کے ساتھ عاقلہ مختص ہیں اسلئے کہ قائل نے کوتاہی کی ہے اپنے اندر قوت کی وجہ سے اور اس کی قوت اس کے مددگاروں کے ذریعہ ہے اور مددگار عاقلہ ہیں تو عاقلہ ہی کوتاہی کرنے والے ہوئے ان کے چھوڑنے میں اس کی نگرانی کو تو ضم کے ساتھ عاقا مختص ہوئے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And the diyah in shibh 'amd (quasi-intentional) and khata' (accidental), and every diyah that becomes obligatory by reason of the killing itself (i.e., not through sulh or confession), is upon the 'aqila. And the 'aqila are those who pay the 'aql, i.e., the diyah. This has been mentioned in the Book of Diyat. The basis for its obligation on the 'aqila is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Hammal ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) to the relatives of the killer: 'Stand up and pay his diyah.' Commentary: Every diyah that is obligatory by reason of the killing itself, i.e., that the cause of the killing itself is the diyah, whether the killing is 'amd or khata', then such a diyah will not be obligatory on the killer himself but on his supporting fraternity/relatives. The details of diyah have passed in the Book of Diyat. As for why the obligation is on the 'aqila, the author presented a hadith. Summary of the hadith: Hammal ibn Malik had two wives; one struck the other with a tent peg, causing her to miscarry and die. The Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the relatives of the striker to pay the diyah. Rational proof: Because the soul is inviolable, there is no way to let it go to waste. The mistaken person is excused, and similarly the one who committed shibh 'amd, considering the instrument, so there is no justification to impose punishment on him. Imposing a large payment would cause him distress and ruin, so it would become a punishment. Therefore, the 'aqila are joined to him to achieve leniency. They are specifically joined because the killer fell short due to his own strength, and that strength is from his supporters, who are the 'aqila. Thus, the 'aqila are the ones who fell short in abandoning their watch over him, so they are specifically joined.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage combines a ruling from al-Quduri with two proofs: a textual proof (hadith) and a rational proof. The ruling: In cases of shibh 'amd (quasi-intentional killing) and khata' (accidental killing), the full diyah is obligatory upon the 'aqila, not the killer. This applies to any diyah that is the primary consequence of the killing (not diyah by sulh or confession). The hadith of Hammal ibn Malik is cited as the primary textual evidence: when a woman accidentally killed another with a tent peg, the Prophet ordered the killer's 'aqila (her relatives) to pay the diyah. The rational proof follows: The victim's life is inviolable, so blood cannot go un-avenged. The killer is excused (due to lack of intent or accident), so imposing a heavy payment on him would be destructive and punitive, contradicting the principle of mercy. Therefore, the obligation is shifted to the 'aqila, who share responsibility for the killer's actions because they failed to supervise him. This transfer realizes leniency (takhfif). The commentary explains that the rational argument is based on istihsan: although qiyas might place the liability on the killer, istihsan transfers it to the 'aqila to avoid hardship.

Key Terms
عاقلة ('āqila): The group responsible for paying diyah in cases of shibh 'amd and khata'.
شبه العمد (shibh al-'amd): Killing that resembles intentional but without intent to kill, using an instrument not generally fatal (e.g., a stick used for discipline).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Hammal ibn Malik, who did the Prophet order to pay the diyah?
A) The killer himself
B) The victim's family
C) The killer's 'aqila (relatives)
D) The state treasury

Key Takeaway
In shibh 'amd and khata', the diyah is wajib on the 'aqila to balance the inviolability of life with mercy for the excused killer.

Al-Mughrur: The Deceived Man in Marriage
Definition and ruling on the mughrur case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of al-maghruur in Hanafi fiqh and explain the ruling regarding the children and compensation.

Core Idea
A deceived man must pay the value of his free children at the time of judgment, not at birth.

This passage introduces the concept of al-maghruur (the deceived) within Hanafi marriage law. It uses the example of a man misled into marrying a slave woman who claimed to be free. The ruling clarifies both the status of the children and the father's financial liability, demonstrating a key principle of deception and compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the deceived party and the false representation
The man is deceived because the woman told him she was free when she was actually a slave.
2
State the ruling regarding the mother
The woman is returned to her rightful owner upon discovery.
3
State the ruling regarding the children
The children born from this marriage are free.
Because the marriage was apparently valid based on the woman's claim.
4
Identify the compensation and its timing
The deceived father must pay the value of the children, assessed at the Day of Judgment.
The valuation time is critical; it may be higher than at birth.
5
Define al-maghruur
Al-maghruur is the deceived party in this context, specifically the husband who relied on a false representation.
The term comes from the woman's deception (ghurur).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المغرور میں یعنی مثلا کسی عورت نے کسی مرد سے نکاح کیا اور اس مرد کو اس نے بتایا تھا کہ میں آزاد ہوں لہذا کچھ بچے ہوئے اور کسی نے دعوی کر دیا کہ یہ عورت میری باندی ہے تو وہ باندی مستحق کو واپس دی جائے گی اور اس کے بچے آزاد ہو نگے لیکن ان کی قیمت ادا کرنی یر کی ۔ اور قیمت قضاء کے دن کی معتبر ہوگی اس طرح یہاں بھی مدت کا آغاز قضا ، کے وقت سے ہوگا۔ اور اس کو مغرور اس لئے کہا گیا ہے کہ اس کو اس عورت نے دھوکہ دیا ہے۔
Regarding al-maghruur: For example, a woman married a man and she had told him that I am free. Then some children were born. And someone claimed that this woman is my slave-girl. So that slave-girl will be returned to the claimant, and her children will be free, but their price must be paid. And the price will be considered as of the Day of Judgment. Similarly here the beginning of the period will be from the time of judgment. And it is called maghruur because the woman deceived him.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'al-maghruur' (the deceived) in the context of 'Aqila. It presents a case where a man marries a woman who falsely claims to be free, but she is actually a slave. The ruling: the woman is returned to her owner, but the children born from this marriage are free. However, the father (the deceived man) must pay their market value as assessed on the Day of Judgment. This illustrates a general principle: the deceived party's liability is measured at the time of judgment. The passage is an example within the broader discussion of blood money and 'Aqila, showing how deception affects liability.

Key Terms
مغرور (al-maghruur): The deceived person, specifically a man who marries a woman believing she is free but she is a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) They are free but their price is paid by the father.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on al-maghruur protects the innocent children's freedom while requiring the deceived father to compensate the owner at the valuation of the Day of Judgment.

Aqila for Non-Diwan Members is Their Tribe
Ruling that the 'aqila of one not in the diwan is his tribe

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the 'aqila of a person not registered in the diwan and explain the basis of the ruling.

Core Idea
For those outside the military register, the 'āqilah is the tribe — mutual support determines responsibility.

This lesson examines a key rule from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The diwan was the official military register; those registered had their 'aqila among fellow soldiers. But what about everyone else? The ruling clarifies that for non-registrants, the 'aqila is their tribe (qabilah), because the basis of 'aqila is mutual support (nusrah), which comes from one's kinship network. Understanding this distinction is essential for applying the law of blood money correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Determine who this ruling applies to: those who are 'not from ahl al-diwan' (people of the military register).
The text begins 'wa man yaku min ahl al-diwan' with a negative implication: the ruling is for the opposite.
2
State the ruling
For such a person, his 'aqila is his tribe (qabilah). This means the group responsible for paying diyah on his behalf is his extended family or clan.
The exact phrase is 'fa-'āqilatuhu qabīlatahu'.
3
Extract the 'illa (legal cause)
The reason given is 'because his support (nusrah) is through them, and nusrah is what is considered in 'aqila.' The illa is mutual support, not official registration.
The text: 'li-anna nusratahu bihim wa hiya al-mu'tabarah fi al-ta'āqul'.
4
Contrast with the default
For those in the diwan, their 'aqila is their fellow soldiers. This contrast highlights that the diwan creates an artificial support network, while outside it, natural kinship prevails.
This is implied; the text only explicitly states the rule for non-diwan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن يكن من اهل الديوان فعاقلته قبيلته لان نصرته بهم وهي المعتبرة في التعاقل ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جو اہل دیوان میں سے نہ ہو تو اسکا عاقلہ اس کا قبیلہ ہے اس لئے کہ اس کی نصرت انہیں کی وجہ سے ہے اور عاقلہ ہونے میں نصرت ہی معتبر ہے۔ تشریح اگر کوئی اہل دیوان میں سے نہ ہو تو اس کے عاقلہ اس کا قبیلہ اور اس کا خاندان ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس کے بعد گا ر اس کا خاندان ہوتا ہے اور نصرت ہی کی بنیاد پر عاقلہ ہونے کا مدار ہے۔
He (Al-Quduri) said: And whoever is not among the people of the diwan, his 'aqila is his tribe, because his support is through them, and support is what is considered in 'aqila. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And whoever is not among the people of the diwan, his 'aqila is his tribe, because his support is through them, and support is what is considered in 'aqila. Commentary: If someone is not among the people of the diwan, his 'aqila is his tribe and his family, because his helper is his family, and the basis of being 'aqila is support.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This is a ruling from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It establishes that for a person not enrolled in the official military register (diwan), the 'aqila responsible for paying blood money on his behalf is his tribe (qabilah) or family. The reason ('illa) given is that support (nusrah) comes from them, and the concept of 'aqila is built on mutual support. The commentary emphasizes that the criterion is nusrah, not official registration. This ensures that even non-soldiers have a group to share the burden of diyah.

Key Terms
عاقلہ (‘āqilah): The group (tribe or family) that pays blood money (diyah) on behalf of a killer among them.
اهل الديوان (ahl al-dīwān): Those registered in the military register, entitled to state stipends and subject to certain rules.
قبيلة (qabīlah): Tribe or clan, the group to which a person belongs by lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what determines the 'aqila for a person not in the diwan?
A) His employer
B) His tribe (qabilah)
C) The state treasury
D) The closest mosque

Key Takeaway
For a person not in the military register, the 'aqila is his tribe because the criterion for 'aqila is mutual support.

Maximum Diyah Contribution: Dispute Between Quduri and Imam Muhammad
Ruling on diyah distribution with intra-Hanafi dispute on per-person cap

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah collection over three years and identify the correct maximum per person according to Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
The total diyah per 'aqila member over three years is capped at 3–4 dirhams, not 4 per year.

Diyah (blood money) is a financial obligation paid by the 'aqila (tribe) over three years. Within the Hanafi school, there is a subtle but important dispute about how much each individual can be required to pay. The passage presents the views of two major Hanafi authorities: Al-Quduri and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The commentator resolves the disagreement, guiding us to the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the beginning of the passage: diyah is divided among the 'aqila over three years, and each person cannot be charged more than four dirhams per year, though it can be less.
This is the basic framework from Al-Quduri's text.
2
Spot the apparent ambiguity
Al-Quduri's wording: 'لا يزاد الواحد على اربعة دراهم فى كل سنة' appears to set an annual cap of 4 dirhams. The commentator notes this could be read as allowing the total over three years to exceed 4 dirhams (up to 12).
The word 'فى كل سنة' (in each year) is key.
3
Introduce Imam Muhammad's explicit clarification
Imam Muhammad explicitly states: the total over three years should not exceed 3 or 4 dirhams per person. Thus per year, only 1 dirham or 1⅓ dirham should be collected.
This is a direct nass (text) from Imam Muhammad.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference)
The commentator declares Imam Muhammad's view as al-ashah (the most correct). The reason is likely that it is a lighter burden on the 'aqila and is explicit (nass) while Quduri's text is open to interpretation.
Tarjih is based on textual clarity and ease.
5
Apply the correct ruling
In practice, the 'aqila member pays either 1 dirham per year (total 3) or 1⅓ dirham per year (total 4) over three years. More than that is not allowed.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتقسم عليهم في ثلث سنين لا يزاد الواحد على اربعة دراهم فى كل سنة وينقص منها قال رضى الله عنه كذا ذكره القدورى فى مختصره وهذا اشارة الى انه يزاد على اربعة من جميع الدية وقد نص محمد على انه لا يزاد على كل واحد من جميع الدية فى ثلث سنين على ثلثة او اربعة فلا يؤخذ من كل واحد في كل سنة الادرهما او درهما وثلث درهم وهو الاصح ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور دیت کو قبیلہ پر تین سالوں میں تقسیم کر دیا جائیگا ہر سال میں ایک سے چار درہموں سے زیادہ نہیں لیا جائے گا اور اس سے کم کیا جا سکتا ہے ، مصنف نے فرمایا کہ قدوری نے اپنی مختصر میں یونہی ذکر کیا ہے اور یہ اس بات کی جانب اشارہ ہے کہ پوری دیت میں چار سے بڑھایا جا سکتا ہے حالانکہ امام محمد نے صراحت کی ہے کہ ایک پر پوری دیت میں تین سالوں کے اندر تین یا چار درہموں پر بڑھا یا نہیں جائے گا تو ہر سال میں ہر ایک سے صرف ایک درہم یا ایک درہم اور ایک درہم کا ( ) لیا جائے گا اور یہی اصح ہے۔ تشریح جب قبیلہ والوں پر دیت کو تقسیم کیا جائے تو اس میں یہ خیال رہے گا کہ پوری دیت ان سے تین سال میں قسط وار وصول ہوگی اور سالانہ ہر ایک سے صرف ایک درہم لیا جائے تا کہ مجموعہ تین ہو جائے یا ہر ایک سے ایک درہم اور درہم کا تہائی لیا جائے تا کہ مجموعہ چار در اہم ہو جائے کیونکہ کسی سے چار سے زیادہ لینا جائز نہیں ہے اگر چہ کم کر دینے کی گنجائش ہے لیکن زیادتی کی نہیں ہے۔ امام قدوری کا کلام سامنے ہے اس سے بظاہر یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ تین سال میں ہر ایک سے چار درہموں سے زیادہ کیا جا سکتا ہے کیونکہ انہوں نے یہ فرمایا ہے کہ کسی سے سالانہ چار سے زیادہ نہیں لئے جا سکتے البتہ چار سے کم کئے جاسکتے ہیں اور یہ امام محمد کی تصریح کے خلاف ہے اور اصح وہی جو امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے۔
He said: And it is divided among them over three years; each one is not increased upon more than four dirhams in each year, and it may be decreased from that. He (the author) said, may Allah be pleased with him: Thus Al-Quduri mentioned it in his Mukhtasar, and this indicates that it is increased above four from the total diyah. And Muhammad explicitly stated that he is not increased upon each one from the total diyah over three years to more than three or four, so from each one in each year only one dirham or one and one-third dirham is taken, and this is the correct view. Translation: Al-Quduri said: The diyah is divided among the tribe over three years; each person is not charged more than four dirhams per year, and it may be less. The author said that Al-Quduri mentioned this in his Mukhtasar, and this indicates that the total diyah can be increased beyond four (per person). However, Imam Muhammad explicitly stated that a person should not be charged more than three or four dirhams in total over the three years, so per year only one dirham or one and one-third dirham is taken, and this is the correct view. Commentary: When the diyah is distributed among the tribe, it should be collected in three annual installments. Each year, from each person only one dirham is taken so that the total becomes three, or one and one-third dirham so that the total becomes four, because taking more than four from anyone is not permissible, though decreasing is allowed. Al-Quduri's statement apparently suggests that over three years a person can be charged more than four dirhams total, because he said that per year more than four cannot be taken, but the total can be more. This contradicts Imam Muhammad's explicit text, and the correct view is what Imam Muhammad stated.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage addresses the method of collecting diyah (blood money) from the 'aqila. The diyah is to be paid over three years in installments. There is a dispute within the Hanafi school about the maximum amount each individual in the 'aqila can be required to pay. Al-Quduri's text is interpreted by the commentator as allowing up to four dirhams per person per year, implying the total over three years could be up to twelve dirhams. However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani explicitly states that the total per person over the three years should not exceed three or four dirhams. The commentator declares Imam Muhammad's view as the correct one (al-ashah). Thus, the actual practice is that each member pays either one dirham per year (total three) or one and one-third dirham per year (total four). This ensures the burden is light and does not exceed the cap.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid to the heirs of a victim in cases of homicide or bodily harm.
درهم (dirham): A silver coin used as currency; here used as a unit for calculating diyah contributions.
العاقلة (al-'aqila): The tribe or group responsible for paying diyah on behalf of the offender.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi view, what is the maximum total a person can be required to pay from diyah over three years?
A) 12 dirhams
B) 3 or 4 dirhams
C) 1 dirham per year
D) No maximum

Key Takeaway
The correct Hanafi position is that each 'aqila member pays at most 3-4 dirhams total over three years for diyah.

Adding Nearest Tribes When 'Aqila is Insufficient
Ruling on adding nearest tribes in 'asaba order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order in which additional tribes are added to the 'aqila when the immediate tribe cannot pay the diyah, and explain the underlying principle of takhfif (lightening the burden).

Core Idea
When the immediate 'aqila cannot pay, add the nearest lineage in 'asaba order to spread the burden.

In cases where the immediate 'aqila tribe cannot bear the full diyah without overburdening individuals, the Hanafi fiqh provides a mechanism to distribute the payment across additional tribes. This principle, known as al-aqrab fal-aqrab, ensures that the burden is spread fairly. In this lesson, we will examine the precise order of addition as established by Al-Quduri and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering condition
The immediate 'aqila tribe is insufficient to pay the full diyah without any individual exceeding the maximum contribution of four dirhams. This insufficiency triggers the addition of other tribes.
The per-person limit is based on takhfif.
2
Recognize the principle of takhfif
The entire 'aqila system is designed to lighten the killer's burden. Adding more tribes further spreads the cost, ensuring no individual is overburdened.
3
Learn the order of addition
Additional tribes are added in order of lineage closeness, following the order of 'asaba (residuary heirs): brothers, then their sons (nephews), then paternal uncles, then their sons (paternal cousins).
This order is specified in the source text.
4
Apply to a scenario
If the killer's brothers cannot cover the diyah, add the nephews; if still insufficient, add the uncles, and so on until the burden is distributed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان لم يكن تتسع القبيلة لذلك ضم اليهم اقرب القبائل معناه نسبا كل ذلك لمعنى التخفيف ويضم الاقرب فالاقرب على ترتيب العصبات الاخوة ثم بنوهم ثم الأعمام ثم بنوه ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر قبیلہ اس کے لئے وسیع نہ ہو تو باعتبار نسب اقرب القبائل کو ان کی طرف ملا دیا جائے یہ تمام باتیں تخفیف کی وجہ سے ہیں اور اقرب فالا قرب کو ملایا جائے عصبات کی ترتیب کے مطابق بھائیوں کو پھر بھتیجوں کو پھر بچاؤں کو پھر ان کے بیٹوں کو۔ تشریح جس قبیلہ کو اس کا عاقلہ شمار کیا گیا تھا وہ اداء دیت کے لئے ناکافی ہے، تو دوسرا وہ قبیلہ ان کی طرف ملا دیا جائے گا جو نسب کے اعتبار سے ان کے قریب ہو اس لئے کہ عاقلہ پر دیت کا وجوب تخفیف کی غرض سے ہے اور تخفیف اس میں ہے جو ہم نے بتایا کہ ایک شخص پر پوری دیت کے اندر چار درا ہم سے زیادہ نہ ہونے پائیں لہذا الا قرب فالا قرب کے لحاظ سے قبائل کو ملا دیا جائے گا اور الا قرب درہم الاقر فالاقرب کی وہی ترتیب ہے جو عصبات کی ترتیب ہے یعنی اولا قاتل کے بھائیوں کو ملایا جائے گا پھر بھائیوں کے بیٹوں کو پھر چچاؤں کو پھر چچا زاد بھائیوں کو۔ (وقد بين ترتيب العصبات مفصلاً في درس السراجي)۔
He said: And if the tribe is not extensive enough for that, then the nearest tribes in terms of lineage are added to them. All of that is for the purpose of lightening (the burden). And they are added nearest then nearest according to the order of 'asaba: brothers, then their sons, then paternal uncles, then their sons. Translation: Al-Quduri said: If the tribe is not sufficient for that, then the nearest tribes in terms of lineage are joined to them. All these are for the purpose of lightening. And they are added nearest then nearest in the order of 'asaba: brothers, then their sons, then paternal uncles, then their sons. Commentary: The tribe that was considered his 'aqila is insufficient for paying the diyah. So another tribe that is closer in lineage is added to them. This is because the obligation of diyah on the 'aqila is for the purpose of lightening, and lightening is as we have stated: that one person should not have to pay more than four dirhams from the total diyah. Therefore, tribes are added according to the principle of al-aqrab fal-aqrab, and the order of al-aqrab fal-aqrab is the same as the order of 'asaba: first the killer's brothers are added, then the sons of brothers, then paternal uncles, then the sons of paternal uncles (paternal cousins).
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri deals with the situation where the immediate tribe (qabilah) that is the 'aqila does not have enough members to bear the diyah without exceeding the per-person limit of four dirhams. In that case, additional tribes are added, starting with the closest in lineage. The order of addition follows the order of 'asabah (residuary heirs) in inheritance: brothers, then their sons, then paternal uncles, then their sons. This ensures the burden is spread widely enough that no individual pays more than the prescribed maximum. The commentary emphasizes that the entire system of 'aqila is designed for takhfif (lightening), so adding more people is consistent with that goal.

Key Terms
عصبات (‘aṣabāt): Male agnatic relatives who inherit as residuaries; here used as the order for adding to the 'aqila.
تخفیف (takhfīf): Lightening or reducing the burden; the underlying principle for 'aqila rules.
اقرب فالاقرب (al-aqrab fa al-aqrab): The nearest then the nearest; a principle of priority in inheritance and here in adding to 'aqila.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In what order are additional tribes added when the immediate 'aqila is insufficient?
A) By wealth
B) By age
C) By closeness of lineage following the order of 'asaba
D) By distance of residence

Key Takeaway
The order of adding tribes is the order of 'asaba: brothers, then their sons, then uncles, then their sons.

Including Killer's Ascendants and Descendants in the 'Aqila
Intra-Hanafi dispute on killer's ascendants/descendants in 'aqila

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on including the killer's ascendants and descendants in the 'aqila and explain the legal basis (dalil) for each position.

Core Idea
Including the killer's father/son in the 'aqila is disputed: they are closest but few—does that serve the purpose of lightening the burden?

This passage presents an internal Hanafi disagreement about who qualifies as part of the killer's 'aqila for diyah payments. The key question is whether the killer's own father(s) and son(s) are included. Two contrasting positions emerge, each grounded in a different aspect of the 'aqila's purpose: one emphasizes closeness and support, the other emphasizes spreading the burden to achieve relief.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the two opinions: (1) Fathers and sons are included because of their closeness and support. (2) They are not included because the purpose of adding is to remove hardship, which requires abundance, and they are few.
Note that the passage presents both without giving preference.
2
Extract the dalil for inclusion
The first opinion relies on the basis of the 'aqila: support (nusrah) and closeness (qurb). Since fathers and sons are the closest supporters, they are included a fortiori.
3
Extract the dalil for exclusion
The second opinion relies on the purpose of expanding the 'aqila: removal of hardship (nafy al-haraj) by limiting each member's share to no more than three or four. Fathers and sons are few, so including them does not achieve this.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider a concrete case: if included, the father and sons must contribute; if excluded, they are exempt and more distant relatives pay a larger share.
This practical difference affects the distribution of diyah.
5
Assess the tarjih
The passage gives no preference. Later Hanafi texts may favor one view; students should recognize this as an unsettled ikhtilaf.
Muftis may choose based on context and maslahah.

Source Text

And as for the fathers and sons: some said they enter (the 'aqila) due to their closeness, and some said they do not enter because joining (others) is to remove hardship, so that each one does not get more than three or four. And this meaning is only realized when there is abundance, and fathers and sons are not abundant. Translation: As for the fathers and sons: it is said that they are included due to their closeness, and it is said that they are not included because joining is for removing hardship, so that each one does not receive more than three or four. This meaning is only realized when there is abundance, and fathers and sons are not abundant. Commentary: Here the question is whether the killer's fathers and his sons are included in the list of 'aqila. There are two sayings. One: Since the basis of being 'aqila is support and closeness, the fathers should be included a fortiori. The second saying: Fathers and sons are not included because the purpose of adding others to the 'aqila is lightening (takhfif), and lightening is achieved when many people are included so that each person's share is small. Since fathers and sons are generally few, including them does not achieve lightening.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage presents an internal Hanafi dispute about whether the killer's own father(s) and son(s) are counted among his 'aqila. Two positions are given: (1) They should be included because they are the closest relatives and support (nusrah) is strongest from them. (2) They should not be included because the entire system of adding to the 'aqila is meant to lighten the burden by spreading it over many people. Fathers and sons are few in number, so including them does not significantly lighten the burden; rather, they themselves would bear a heavy share. The passage does not give a definitive tarjih, leaving both opinions as valid within the school.

Key Terms
آباء (ābā’): Fathers, meaning ascendants (father, grandfather, etc.).
أبناء (abnā’): Sons, meaning descendants (sons, grandsons, etc.).
حرج (ḥaraj): Hardship or difficulty; the removal of which is the purpose of spreading diyah over many.
نصرت (nuṣrah): Support; the basis for considering someone part of the 'aqila.

Key Takeaway
The inclusion of the killer's father and sons in the 'aqila is an unsettled debate within the Hanafi school, hinging on whether the primary purpose is support or hardship removal.

Adding Closer Banners (Rayaat) for Insufficient 'Aqila
States the ruling when one banner is insufficient for diyah payment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one 'aqila banner is insufficient for diyah and apply the principle of al-aqrab fa al-aqrab to determine the next responsible group.

Core Idea
When one banner fails to cover diyah, the next closest banner in support is added, delegated to the imam.

The 'aqila system distributes the burden of blood money among the kin of the killer. But what if one clan or military unit cannot pay the full amount? This passage from Kitab al-Ma'aqil provides the Hanafi solution: the imam adds the next closest banner in terms of support, following the principle 'the closest then the closest.' This ensures fairness and prevents financial collapse on a single group.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Recognize the scenario: the members of one banner (raya) are insufficient to collectively pay the required diyah.
The banner represents a subdivision of the 'aqila, such as a military regiment or tribal unit.
2
State the Default Ruling
The ruling states: 'ضم اليهم اقرب الرايا' – the closest banner in support is added to them.
Closeness is defined by support (nusrah), not necessarily blood relation.
3
Apply the Sequential Principle
If the added banner is also insufficient, the next closest is added, continuing with 'al-aqrab fa al-aqrab' (the closest then the closest).
This chain continues until the total diyah can be covered.
4
Recognize the Imam's Role
The determination of which banner is closest is delegated to the imam (ruler), who has full knowledge of the tribal and military hierarchies.
The imam must use his judgment based on evidence of support, not arbitrarily.
5
Confirm the Hanafi Stance
The text concludes 'ثم هذا كله عندنا' – this is the Hanafi position.
Other schools may have different methods for apportioning diyah among the 'aqila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسی طرح ایک کمپنی ادائیگی دیت کے لئے ناکافی ہو تو دوسری کمپنی جو نصرت و مدد کے لحاظ سے قریب ہوا سے شامل کیا جائے گا
وعلى هذا حكم الرايات اذا لم يتسع لذلك اهل راية ضم اليهم اقرب الرايا يعني اقربهم نصرة اذا حزبهم امر الاقرب فالاقرب ويفوض ذلك الى الامام لانه هو العالم به ثم هذا كله عندنا ترجمہ اور اسی طریقہ پر رایات کا حکم ہے جب کہ اس کے لئے ایک جھنڈے والے ناکافی ہوں تو ان کی اقرب الرایات کو ملا دیا جائے گا یعنی ان میں سب سے زیادہ قریب ہوں نصرت کے اعتبار سے جب کہ ان کو کوئی امر پیش آ جائے الا قرب فالاقرب کے لحاظ سے اور اس کو امام کے سپر د کر دیا جائے اس لئے کہ اس بات کو وہی جانتا ہے۔ پھر یہ ساری تفصیل ہمارے نزدیک ہیں۔ تشریح اگر یہی صورت لشکر کی کمپنیوں میں ہوگئی ہو تو ایک کمپنی یا ایک رجسٹر میں جن کا نام درج ہے وہ اداء دیت کے لئے ناکافی ہیں تو انکی طرف اس دوسری کمپنی کو ملا دیا جائے گا جو ان کے نصرت و مدد کے لحاظ سے قریب ہو اور یہی الا قرب فالا قرب کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے آگے بھی ملایا جا سکتا ہے اور چونکہ ان امور سے امام واقف ہے اس لئے اس کو امام کے حوالہ کر دیا جائے گا بہر حال تفصیلات مذکورہ حنفیہ کے مسلک کے مطابق ہیں
Similarly, if one company is insufficient for the payment of blood money, then another company which is close in terms of support and assistance will be included. And upon this is the ruling of the banners: when the people of one banner are not sufficient for that, then the closest of the banners are added to them, meaning the closest to them in support. When an incident befalls them, the closest then the closest. And that is delegated to the imam because he is the one who knows it. Then all of this is according to us. Translation: And likewise is the ruling of the banners: when the people of one banner are insufficient for it, then their closest banners are added, i.e., those who are most close in terms of support, when an incident befalls them, the closest then the closest, and it is delegated to the imam because he is the one who knows it. Then all of this detail is according to us. Commentary: If this situation occurs in the companies of the army, and one company or register in which names are recorded is insufficient for paying the blood money, then the next company which is close in support and assistance will be added to them, and this principle of 'closest then closest' can be applied further. And since the imam is aware of these matters, it will be referred to him. In any case, the mentioned details are according to the Hanafi school.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Kitab al-Ma'aqil. It addresses the practical scenario when the 'aqila (the clan responsible for paying blood money) is insufficient. The text explains that when the members of one 'raya' (banner/regiment) are unable to collectively pay the diyah, the next closest banner in terms of support and proximity is added. This process continues with 'al-aqrab fa al-aqrab' (the closest then the closest). The determination of who is closest is delegated to the Imam (ruler), who has knowledge of the tribal and military groupings. The author emphasizes that this is the Hanafi position. The commentary illustrates this with the modern example of companies or registers in an army. This ruling ensures that the burden of blood money is distributed fairly among those most closely connected to the killer.

Key Terms
عاقلة ('a'ila): The clan or group responsible for paying diyah (blood money) on behalf of a killer from among them.
راية (raya): A banner or flag representing a military unit or tribal contingent; used here to denote a group of people collectively responsible for diyah.
دية (diya): Blood money paid in cases of homicide or bodily injury to the victim's heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The state treasury pays the diyah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when the 'aqila of one banner cannot pay the full diyah, the next closest banner in support is added, with the imam determining proximity.

Collecting Diyah from Stipends: The Three-Year Rule
States the ruling when the 'aqila are stipend recipients.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for collecting diyah from stipend recipients over three years and calculate the proportional share to be taken from each stipend distribution based on its frequency.

Core Idea
A stipend (rizq) stands in place of an annual grant ('ata); diyah is spread over three years, taken proportionally from each payment.

When the 'aqila (helper group) responsible for paying diyah are not recipients of annual grants ('ata) but rather receive stipends (rizq) from the state treasury, the Hanafi school provides a detailed method for collection. This lesson explains the principle that stipends are equivalent to grants and how to calculate the amount to be taken from each stipend distribution—whether annual, semi-annual, or monthly—so that one-third of the diyah is collected each year.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying analogy
Recognise that the passage equates stipends (rizq) with annual grants ('ata) because both are gratuitous payments from the treasury. This analogy is the basis for the ruling.
The key phrase is 'الرزق فى حقهم بمنزلة العطاء' (the stipend is in the position of 'ata).
2
State the base ruling
The diyah is to be paid over three years, with one-third collected each year. This is the default schedule.
This mirrors the rule for 'ata recipients.
3
Determine the frequency of stipends
The passage considers three frequencies: annual, semi-annual, and monthly. Identify which frequency applies to the 'aqila.
The frequency affects how much is taken from each distribution.
4
Calculate the per-distribution share
For annual stipends, take one-third per distribution. For semi-annual, take one-sixth per distribution (so that two distributions give one-third). For monthly, take a monthly share such that the sum over twelve months equals one-third.
The goal is that the total collected in each year amounts to exactly one-third of the diyah.
5
Handle the first distribution after judgment
If the stipend is released after the judgment (even by a day), take from that distribution the share proportional to the remaining part of the month or period.
This ensures the one-third per year is not exceeded.

Source Text

And if the 'aqila of a man are the people of stipends (as-hab al-rizq), judgment is made of the diyah on their stipends over three years, one third each year, because the stipend for them is in the position of 'ata (grant), standing in its place, since each of them is a gratuitous payment from the treasury. Then it is considered: if their stipends are released every year, then as the stipend is released, one third is taken from it, in the manner of 'ata. And if it is released every six months, and it is released after the judgment, one sixth of the diyah is taken from it. And if it is released every month, from each stipend is taken according to the share of the month, so that the total collected in each year amounts to one third. And if it is released after the judgment by one day or more, from the stipend of that month the share of the month is taken. Translation: And if a man has stipend-holders, then judgment is made of the diyah on their stipends over three years, one third each year, because the stipend for them is in the rank of 'ata, it stands in its place, because each of them is a gratuitous payment from the treasury. Then it is looked: if their stipends come out every year, then whatever comes out, one third is taken from it, in the rank of 'ata. And if the stipend comes out every six months and it comes out after the judgment, one sixth of the diyah is taken from it. And if it comes out every month, from each stipend the share of the month is taken, until the total collected in the year amounts to one third. And if the stipend comes out after the judgment by a day or more, from the stipend of that month the share of the month is taken. Commentary: 'Ata (grant) is what is given annually to the people of the register (ahl al-diwan). As for stipend (rizq), there are various interpretations: it is the stipend given to the poor from the treasury due to their poverty; it is also called the monthly allowance given to soldiers for necessities. In any case, the author intends to say that if the killer is not from among the people of 'ata but rather from among the stipend-holders, then the stipend stands in place of 'ata. Therefore, the judgment of diyah will be made on the stipends, to be collected over three years, with one third collected annually. Then, if the stipend is given annually from the treasury, this calculation applies. And if it is given every six months, then whenever it is given, one sixth is taken so that it becomes one third in a year. And if the stipend is monthly, then each month a portion is taken so that it becomes one third in a year. The rest of the text is clear.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling for collecting diyah when the 'aqila are not recipients of annual grants ('ata) but rather stipends (rizq) from the state treasury. The principle is that stipends are treated like grants; they are gratuitous payments from the treasury. The diyah is to be paid over three years, with one-third collected each year. The calculation adjusts based on the frequency of stipends: for annual stipends, one-third is taken each year; for semi-annual stipends, one-sixth is taken each distribution so that the annual total is one-third; for monthly stipends, a monthly share is taken to reach one-third annually. This ensures that the burden is spread evenly. The commentary explains that 'ata is for registered soldiers/officials (ahl al-diwan), while rizq is for the poor and soldiers for daily needs. The ruling ensures that those who rely on stipends are not overburdened in a single payment.

Key Terms
عطاء ('ata): Annual grant from the treasury to registered soldiers or officials.
رزق (rizq): Stipend paid to the poor or soldiers, often monthly or semi-annually.
دية (diya): Blood money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the 'aqila are stipend recipients (as-hab al-rizq) and the stipend is paid monthly, how is the diyah collected over the year?
A) A full third is taken from the first month's stipend.
B) One thirty-sixth is taken each month.
C) A monthly share is taken so that the annual total equals one third.
D) Nothing is taken until the end of the year.

Key Takeaway
When the 'aqila are stipend recipients, diyah is collected over three years by taking a proportional share from each stipend distribution so that one-third is collected annually.

Children and Women in the 'Aqila: Who Pays Diyah?
Ruling with proof on exclusion of children and women from aqila

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether children and women are included in the 'aqila for diyah payment and explain the basis of the ruling using the nusra criterion.

Core Idea
Children and women lack nusra, so they are not in the aqila and pay no diyah personally.

This passage clarifies the Hanafi position on who is considered part of the 'aqila – the group responsible for paying blood money in accidental killings. The author distinguishes between those who provide military assistance (nusra) and those who do not, explaining why children and women are excluded from personal contribution. A later intra-Hanafi difference is addressed, affirming the original madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is the question about children and women in relation to the 'aqila? The passage addresses whether they contribute to diyah when they commit accidental killing.
2
State the Hanafi position
The original Hanafi ruling is that children and women are not part of the 'aqila and do not personally contribute to diyah.
This is from zahir al-riwayah.
3
Understand the key criterion: nusra
The basis for exclusion is the lack of nusra (military assistance capability). Children and women are not capable of providing military aid, so they are not counted as individuals of the 'aqila.
An adult male killer contributes like one member because he has nusra.
4
Distinguish the later opinion
Some later Hanafis (mutakhkhirin) said women enter the 'aqila, but the author clarifies that this is not from the original narrations; the original madhhab excludes them.
The later opinion is marjuh (not relied upon).
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete case
If a child or woman kills, their 'aqila pays the diyah, but they contribute nothing. If an adult male kills, he contributes like one member of the 'aqila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد ۱۹- میں ) نہیں پائے جاتے اور ان دونوں کے لئے ( بچہ اور عورت کے لئے ) عطاء کا حصہ معونت کے لئے ہے نہ کہ نصرت کے لئے جیسے نبی علیہ السلام کی ازواج مطہرات رضی اللہ عنہن کا حصہ ۔ تشریح اور اگر بچہ یا عورت خود قتل کر دیں تب بھی دیت کا وجوب ان کے عاقلہ پر ہو گا بچہ اور عورت پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا ہاں اگر کوئی بالغ مرد قاتل ہو تو اس پر عاقلہ میں سے ایک فرد کے مثل دیت کا کچھ حصہ واجب ہوگا کیونکہ اس کے اہل نصرت میں سے ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کو عاقلہ میں سے شمار کرتے ہوئے عواقل کا ایک فرد شمار کیا جائے گا کیونکہ بہر حال وہ اپنی نصرت تو کرتا ہی ہے اور بچہ اور عورت میں یہ بات موجود نہیں ہے۔
سوال .. جب بچے اور عورتیں اہل نصرت میں نہیں ہیں تو یہ اہل عطاء میں سے کیسے ہوں گے؟ جواب ان کے لئے جو عطا یا مقرر ہیں وہ اہل نصرت میں سے ہونے کی بنیاد پر نہیں ہے بلکہ ان کی معونت کی وجہ سے ہے یعنی امام ان ان کی معونت و مدد کرنا چاہتا ہے کیونکہ یہ بعض امور میں کچھ معین ہو سکتے ہیں۔
جیسے حضور اقدس صلى الله عليه وسلم کی ازواج مطہرات کو جو حصہ دیا جاتا تھاوہ نصرت کی بنیاد پر نہیں تھا بلکہ بناء پر معونت تھا۔ سوال یہاں یہ فرمایا گیا ہے کہ عورت عاقلہ کے ساتھ دیت میں شامل نہ ہوگی اور پہلے یہ مسئلہ گذرا ہے قال المتاخرون ان المرآة تدخل مع العاقلة الخ تويه تعارض كيسان یہ کیسا؟
جواب وہ اصل روایت نہیں بلکہ بعض متاخرین کا قول ہے اور یہ اصل مذہب ہے۔
Kitab al-Ma'aqil. 74. Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Bidayah Volume 19 - they are not found, and for both (child and woman) the share of 'ata is for support, not for nusra, like the share of the pure wives of the Prophet (peace be upon him), may Allah be pleased with them. Explanation: And if a child or woman themselves commit murder, then the obligation of diyah will be upon their 'aqila, nothing is wajib upon the child or woman. Yes, if an adult man is the killer, then a portion of diyah like one individual of the 'aqila will be wajib upon him, because due to his being from the people of nusra, he will be counted as one individual of the 'awqil while counting him among the 'aqila, because he certainly provides his nusra, and this quality is not present in the child and woman. Question: When children and women are not people of nusra, how can they be among the people of 'ata? Answer: The 'ata that is fixed for them is not based on their being from the people of nusra, but rather due to their support, meaning the imam wants to support and help them, because they can be helpful in some matters. Like the share given to the pure wives of the Prophet (peace be upon him) was not based on nusra, but on support. Question: Here it is stated that a woman will not be included with the 'aqila in diyah, and earlier this issue passed: 'the later scholars said that the woman enters with the 'aqila' etc. There is contradiction. How is this? Answer: That is not the original narration, but the saying of some later scholars, and this is the original madhhab.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the status of children and women in the 'aqila system for paying diyah (blood money) in cases of accidental killing. The author establishes that children and women are not considered from 'ahl al-nusra' (people who provide military assistance), and therefore they are not included in the 'aqila group responsible for paying diyah. If they commit murder, their 'aqila pays, but they personally contribute nothing. For an adult male killer, he contributes like one individual of the 'aqila because he can provide nusra. The passage then addresses a question about how children and women can receive 'ata (stipend) if they are not from ahl al-nusra. The answer is that their 'ata is for support (mu'awnah), not for nusra, as was the case with the Prophet's wives. Finally, a perceived contradiction with a later scholarly view is resolved: the view that women enter the 'aqila is not from the original sound transmissions but from some later scholars; the relied-upon position is that women are not included. This is an intra-Hanafi clarification, affirming the original madhhab over later opinions.

Key Terms
عاقلہ (‘āqila): The group of male agnatic relatives (or others) liable to pay diyah for accidental killing.
نصرت (nuṣra): Military assistance or defense capability; being able to help in battle.
عطاء (‘aṭā’): Stipend or allowance given by the state, originally to soldiers/registered individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because women are exempt from all financial penalties.
B) Because women are not from ahl al-nusra and cannot provide military assistance.
C) Because the 'aqila always pays regardless of the killer's gender.
D) Because women are considered minors in Islamic law.

Key Takeaway
Children and women are not part of the 'aqila because they lack nusra; their diyah is paid by others, and they personally contribute nothing.

One City's People Do Not Pay for Another City's Diyah
Ruling on diyah liability between separate cities with distinct diwans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on diyah liability between separate cities with distinct diwans and explain why the diwan is the primary basis for 'aqila.

Core Idea
Diyah liability follows the military register (diwan), not city boundaries or lineage.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key question: when a person from one city causes accidental death, which group pays the diyah? The Hanafi school, through the principle of tanasur (mutual assistance), ties the 'aqila obligation to the diwan—the military registration list. This lesson explains the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the key distinction
The ruling: people of one city do not pay for another city's diyah. This applies when each city has a separate diwan (military register).
The diwan is the decisive factor.
2
Understand the legal basis (ta'lil)
The reason is tanasur (mutual assistance), which is based on the diwan when it exists. The diwan indicates the group with whom one has a connection of military solidarity.
tanasur is the underlying principle.
3
Consider the secondary basis
If no diwan exists, proximity of residence is considered. In that case, one's own city people are closer than those from another city.
Residence is a fallback.
4
Recognize the practical consequence
The 'aqila is determined by the diwan, not merely the city of residence. This ensures liability falls on the group with actual ties.
5
Contrast with other potential criteria
Other schools may use lineage or neighborhood. The Hanafi school uniquely prioritizes the diwan as the formal register of mutual assistance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يعقل اهل مصر عن مصر اخر يريد به انه اذا كان لاهل كل مصر ديوان على حدة لان التناصر بالديوان عند اخر وجوده ولو كان باعتبار القرب في السكنى فاهل مصره اقرب اليه من اهل مصر ترجمہ اور ایک شہر والے دو سر شہر والوں کی طرف سے دیت نہیں دیں گے مصنف کی مراد یہ ہے کہ جب کہ ہر شہر والوں کے لئے علیحدہ دیوان ہو اس لئے کہ دیوان کے موجود ہونے کے وقت تناصر دیوان کے ذریعہ ہوتا ہے اور اگر تناصر سکنی کے اندر قرب کی وجہ سے ہو تو آدمی کے شہر والے اس کے زیادہ قریب ہیں دوسرے شہر والوں سے۔ تشریح اگر ہر شہر کے فوجیوں کی کمپنی الگ الگ ہے تو جس کمپنی میں وہ ہے وہ کمپنی اس کی عاقلہ ہوگی اور وہی اس کی دیت ادا گھرے تھی۔ تو اس کو مصنف نے فرمایا کہ ایک شہر والے دوسرے شہر والوں کی طرف سے دیت ادا نہیں کریں گے ۔ اور اگر ناصر کی بنیاد مسکنی کے اندر قربت کی وجہ سے ہو تو آدمی کے شہر والے دوسرے شہر والوں کے مقابلہ میں زیادہ قریب ہوں گے۔
And the people of one city do not pay diyah for another city. He intends that when the people of each city have a separate diwan, because mutual assistance (tanasur) is through the diwan when it exists. And if it were based on proximity of residence, then the people of his city are closer to him than the people of another city. Translation: The people of one city will not pay diyah on behalf of the people of another city. The author's meaning is that when each city's people have a separate diwan, because at the time of the diwan's existence, mutual assistance is through the diwan. And if mutual assistance is due to proximity in residence, then the people of his city are closer to him than the people of another city. Explanation: If each city's military company is separate, then the company he is in is his 'aqila and will pay his diyah. Thus the author stated that the people of one city will not pay diyah on behalf of another city. And if the basis of nusra is proximity in residence, then the people of his city are closer to him compared to the people of another city.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the territorial scope of the 'aqila. The author, based on the principles of the Hanafi school, states that when different cities have separate military registers (diwans), the people of one city are not liable to pay diyah for accidental killings committed by a resident of another city. The reason is that mutual assistance (tanasur) and thus the 'aqila relationship is tied to the diwan—the military unit to which one is registered. If there is no diwan, then proximity of residence may be considered, but even then, one's own city people are closer than those of another city. The explanation clarifies that the diwan-based system is stronger: the 'aqila is the company (regiment) one belongs to. This ruling ensures that the burden of diyah falls on the group most naturally connected to the killer in terms of solidarity and assistance.

Key Terms
دیوان (dīwān): A military register or department listing soldiers/stipend recipients; used to determine 'aqila groups.
تناصر (tanāṣur): Mutual assistance and solidarity, especially in military matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary basis for determining which group is the 'aqila according to this ruling?
A) The city of residence
B) The diwan (military register)
C) The nearest relatives
D) The employer

Key Takeaway
The 'aqila for diyah is determined by the diwan (military register) when it exists, reflecting the principle of tanasur (mutual assistance); city boundaries are secondary.

City Dwellers Pay for Their Villagers
Ruling that city people pay diyah for their dependent villagers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah liability for dependent villagers and explain the legal rationale of nusra and dependency.

Core Idea
A city is responsible for the diyah of its dependent villagers because of mutual support and dependency.

In Hanafi fiqh, the concept of 'aqila (the group liable for diyah) extends beyond blood relatives to include territorial and dependency-based relationships. This lesson explores a ruling from Al-Hidayah that holds city dwellers liable for diyah of accidental killings in their dependent villages, based on the bond of mutual assistance (nusra) and subordination (ittiba'). This illustrates how the school derives legal obligations from social and structural ties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The ruling concerns accidental killing (qatl al-khata') in a village. The hukm is that the city residents must pay the diyah if the villagers themselves cannot afford it.
2
Locate the 'illah (legal cause)
The text gives the reason: villagers are followers (atba') of the city, and there is a relationship of mutual assistance (nusra). The city seeks help from villagers in times of need, creating a bond that justifies liability.
This is a talil-based reasoning, not a textual proof.
3
Understand the scope of 'aqila in Hanafi
The Hanafi school broadens 'aqila beyond blood relatives to include any group bound by mutual support, such as territorial dependency. This is a distinctive feature compared to other schools.
This extension is based on custom and necessity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools, like the Shafi'i, restrict 'aqila to blood relatives and do not extend liability to city dwellers based solely on territorial dependency. The Hanafi view is mufta bihi within the school.
The dispute is over the definition of 'aqila.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Consider a village in a rural district that is administratively dependent on a nearby city. If an accidental killing occurs and the village cannot pay, the city's residents would be collectively liable according to the Hanafi ruling.
This shows the living relevance of classical fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعقل اهل كل مصر من اهل سواد هم لانهم اتباع لاهل المصر فانهم اذا حزبهم امر استنصر وابهم فيعقلهم اهل المصر باعتبار معنى القرب والنصرة
ترجمہ اور ہر شہر والے اپنے گاؤں والوں کی طرف سے دیت ادا کریں گے اس لئے کہ گاؤں والے شہر والوں کے تابع ہیں اس لئے کہ شہر والوں کو جب کوئی امر پیش آتا ہے تو گاؤں والوں سے مدد طلب کرتے ہیں تو اہل شہر ان کی دیت ادا کریں گے قرب اور نصرت کے معنی کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے ۔ تشریح اگر کسی گاؤں میں قتل خطا کا کیس ہوا اور گاؤں والے اداء دیت کے لئے ناکافی ہیں تو وہ شہر جس کے یہ گاؤں تابع ہے جوڑا جائے گا اس لئے کہ گاؤں والے شہر والوں کے تابع ہیں اور بوقت ضرورت اہل شہر گاؤں والوں سے مدد لیتے ہیں تو قرب اور نصرت کے معنی موجود ہیں اس لئے اہل شہر ان کی دیت ادا کریں گے
And the people of every city pay diyah for the people of their rural areas (sawad) because they are followers of the city people. For when an affair befalls them, they seek assistance from them. So the city people pay their diyah, considering the meaning of proximity and nusra. Translation: The people of every city will pay diyah on behalf of their villagers, because the villagers are followers of the city people. Because when an affair occurs to them, they seek help from the villagers, so the city people will pay their diyah, considering the meaning of proximity and nusra. Explanation: If an accidental killing occurs in a village and the villagers are insufficient to pay the diyah, then the city to which this village is subordinate will be joined, because the villagers are followers of the city people, and at times of need, the city people seek help from the villagers. Thus the meanings of proximity and nusra exist, so the city people will pay their diyah.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the relationship between city dwellers and their dependent villagers regarding diyah liability. The Hanafi school holds that if an accidental killing occurs in a village and the villagers themselves cannot afford to pay the full diyah, then the city to which the village is subordinate is obligated to pay. The reason is that villagers are considered followers (atba') of the city people. There is a mutual relationship: city people seek assistance from villagers in times of need, establishing a bond of proximity and nusra (mutual support). Hence, the city people are liable to pay the diyah for their villagers. This extends the 'aqila concept beyond immediate relatives to include territorial and dependency-based solidarity.

Key Terms
سواد (sawād): Rural areas or villages attached to a city; the countryside dependent on the city.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because they are relatives by blood.
B) Because the villagers are followers of the city and there is mutual assistance.
C) Because the city dwellers are richer.
D) Because the village is owned by the city.

Key Takeaway
City dwellers are liable for diyah of dependent villagers due to the bond of mutual support, extending 'aqila beyond kin.

Diyah Liability Based on Diwan Not Residence
Ruling on diyah liability when diwan and residence differ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah liability when a person's diwan and residence differ and explain the principle of istinṣār that underlies it.

Core Idea
The diwan determines the 'aqila, not residence, because a person seeks assistance from diwan members.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from the chapter on ma'aqil (the system of collective liability for diyah). The Hanafi school holds that when a person's military registration (diwan) is in one city but he lives in another, his 'aqila—the group that pays diyah on his behalf—is the people of his diwan. This is based on the principle that he naturally seeks support from his diwan comrades. We will unpack the reasoning behind this rule and see how it applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage gives a case where a person's residence (Basra) differs from his diwan (Kufa). Recognize this as a conflict between two potential bases for the 'aqila.
2
State the ruling
The Hanafi ruling is that the people of Kufa (the diwan city) pay diyah on his behalf. This is the clear legal outcome.
This overrides the default expectation that residence or lineage would determine liability.
3
Understand the proof
The proof is the principle of istinṣār: the person seeks military assistance from his diwan members, not from his neighbors. Thus, the diwan members are his true support network and should bear the liability.
The reasoning is based on customary practice (urf) and the actual social dependency.
4
Apply the principle of hierarchy
The passage explains that diwan-based nusra (assistance) is 'more apparent' and therefore overrides nusra based on kinship, lineage, wala, or proximity of residence. Only when there is no diwan does lineage-based nusra come into play.
This establishes a clear hierarchy: diwan > lineage > residence.
5
Derive further applications
The principle can be extended to many other cases in the chapter of ma'aqil. For example, if a person has no diwan, his 'aqila is his lineage (asabah), not necessarily his neighbors.
The passage mentions that many forms of issues are derived from this principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من كان منزله بالبصرة و ديوانه بالكوفة عقل عنه اهل الكوفة لانه يستنصر باهل ديوانه لا بجيرانه والحاصل ان الاستنصار بالديوان اظهر فلا يظهر معه حكم النصرة بالقرابة والنسب والولاء وقرب السكني وغيره وبعد الديوان النصرة بالنسب على ما بيناه وعلى هذا يخرج كثير من صور مسائل المعاقل
ترجمہ اور وہ شخص جس کی منزل بصرہ میں ہو اور اس کا دیوان کوفہ میں ہو تو اس کی جانب سے اہل کوفہ دیت دیں گے اس لئے کہ وہ اپنے اہل دیوان سے مدد طلب کرتا ہے نہ کہ اپنے پڑوسیوں سے ، اور حاصل یہ ہے کہ دیوان سے مدد طلب کرنا زیادہ ظاہر ہے تو دیوان کے ساتھ قرابت اور نسب اور ولاء وقرب سکنی وغیرہ کی نصرت کا حکم ظاہر نہ ہو گا اور دیوان کے بعد نصرت بالنسب ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اسی اصول پر معاقل کے مسائل کی بہت سی صورتوں کی تخریج ہوتی ہے۔
And whoever has his residence in Basra and his diwan in Kufa, the people of Kufa pay diyah for him, because he seeks assistance from the people of his diwan, not from his neighbors. The conclusion is that seeking assistance through the diwan is more apparent, so with its existence, the ruling of nusra through kinship, lineage, wala, proximity of residence, and other things is not apparent. And after [absence of] diwan, nusra is through lineage, as we have explained. And on this principle many forms of issues of ma'aqil are derived. Translation: And a person whose residence is in Basra and his diwan is in Kufa, then the people of Kufa will pay diyah on his behalf, because he seeks help from the people of his diwan, not from his neighbors. And the conclusion is that seeking help through the diwan is more apparent, so with the existence of the diwan, the ruling of nusra through kinship, lineage, wala, proximity of residence, etc., will not appear. And after the diwan, nusra is through lineage, according to the detail we have explained. And on this principle many forms of ma'aqil issues are derived.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a ruling that establishes the precedence of the diwan over other factors in determining who constitutes the 'aqila. If a person is registered in the diwan of one city but resides in another, his 'aqila is the people of the city where his diwan is located. The reason is that he naturally seeks military assistance from his diwan members, not his neighbors. The principle is that the diwan-based nusra is strongest and overrides nusra based on kinship, lineage, wala (clientage), or proximity of residence. Only when there is no diwan does lineage-based nusra come into play. This principle is a key tool for deriving many specific rulings in the chapter of ma'aqil.

Key Terms
ديوان (dīwān): Military or government registry; the official record of soldiers or civil servants. In this context, it refers to the city or group where a person is registered for military or official purposes.
عاقلة (ʿāqila): The group of people (usually male relatives or tribesmen) who are collectively liable to pay diyah (blood money) on behalf of a person who commits accidental homicide.
استنصار (istinṣār): Seeking military assistance or support.
نصرة (nuṣra): Assistance, support, especially in the context of mutual aid and blood money liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The diwan, not the residence, determines who pays diyah on behalf of a liable person.

City Dweller's Diyah: When the Diwan Prevails Over Blood Relatives
Ruling on diyah liability for a city dweller

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the 'aqila for a city dweller without a diwan stipend and identify the decisive factor (residence) that overrides closer kinship.

Core Idea
For diyah, the city's diwan pays even if the offender has rural relatives and no stipend.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: a city dweller commits a crime requiring diyah, but he has no stipend in the diwan and his closer relatives live in the countryside. The Hanafi ruling establishes that his residence in the city creates liability for the city's diwan, not his blood relatives. The passage is incomplete, but the core ruling is clear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and conditions
Note the offender: a city dweller (ahl al-misr) with no stipend in the diwan. The closer relatives are in the countryside (ahl al-badiyah), but his residence is the city. These are the only facts given.
The diwan here refers to the military register; stipend ('ata) is the salary.
2
State the ruling
The passage rules that the people of the diwan from that city pay the diyah (blood money) for him. This is the operative legal consequence.
It is not conditional on there being kinship between him and the diwan people.
3
Recognize what is omitted
The passage cuts off with 'because' (لان), indicating a proof or reasoning that is missing. This is a textual gap; the ruling stands on its own but its complete justification is not provided in this excerpt.
The phrase 'wa qila huwa saheeh' suggests a transmitted opinion that this ruling is correct.
4
Appreciate the practical effect
Even though the offender has closer rural relatives, the city's diwan is still liable. This shows that residence in the city creates a stronger tie to the city's 'aqila system than blood kinship from the countryside.
This ruling emphasizes the role of the diwan as a social support system for liability.

Diwan Affiliation Overrides Residence in 'Aqila
Ruling on aqila when diwan differs from residence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for determining 'aqila when diwan differs from residence and explain why the diwan takes priority.

Core Idea
A person's 'aqila is determined by his diwan, not his residence, because diwan-based assistance is strongest.

The Hanafi school uses a hierarchical system to determine who pays blood money on behalf of a wrongdoer. While many might assume that residency or kinship decides this, a stronger factor exists: the diwan, or official administrative/military register. This passage explains why the diwan overrides all other ties and how this principle unlocks many derived cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
From the text, state the ruling: when a person's residence is in Basra but his diwan is in Kufa, which group is responsible for paying his diya?
Always pinpoint the exact hukm before analyzing its basis.
2
Classify the evidence
The text uses reasoning (ta'lil) based on 'nusra' (assistance). Identify that the evidence is qiyas/juristic reasoning rooted in 'urf (custom) and the stronger tie of diwan affiliation.
No explicit Quran/hadith; it's derived from practical custom.
3
Trace the 'illa (effective cause)
Why does diwan override? Because the person 'seeks help' (yastansir) from his diwan people, not from neighbors or relatives. The 'illa is the strength of mutual assistance in the diwan.
The 'illa is zanni (speculative) but accepted by the school.
4
Consider the hierarchy
The text establishes a priority: diwan first, then lineage, then other ties. Confirm that when diwan exists, it blocks (hajb) other forms.
This is similar to hajb in inheritance but applied to 'aqila.
5
Connect to the kulliyah
This ruling is not isolated; it is a general principle (kulliyah) from which many specific cases of 'aqila are derived.
Recognize the maxim: 'al-nusra bi al-diwan aqwa'.

Source Text

و من كان منزله بالبصرة و ديوانه بالكوفة عقل عنه اهل الكوفة لانه يستنصر باهل ديوانه لا بجيرانه والحاصل ان الاستنصار بالديوان اظهر فلا يظهر معه حكم النصرة بالقرابة والنسب والولاء وقرب السكني وغيره وبعد الديوان النصرة بالنسب على ما بيناه وعلى هذا يخرج كثير من صور مسائل المعاقل
ترجمہ: اور وہ شخص جس کی منزل بصرہ میں ہو اور اس کا دیوان کوفہ میں ہو تو اس کی جانب سے اہل کوفہ دیت دیں گے اس لئے کہ وہ اپنے اہل دیوان سے مدد طلب کرتا ہے نہ کہ اپنے پڑوسیوں سے، اور حاصل یہ ہے کہ دیوان سے مدد طلب کرنا زیادہ ظاہر ہے تو دیوان کے ساتھ قرابت اور نسب اور ولاء وقرب سکنی وغیرہ کی نصرت کا حکم ظاہر نہ ہو گا اور دیوان کے بعد نصرت بالنسب ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اسی اصول پر معاقل کے مسائل کی بہت سی صورتوں کی تخریج ہوتی ہے۔

And whoever has his residence in Basra and his diwan in Kufa, the people of Kufa pay blood money for him, because he seeks help from his diwan people, not from his neighbors. The conclusion is that seeking help from the diwan is more manifest, so the ruling of assistance through kinship, lineage, patronage, proximity of residence, and others does not appear with it. And after the diwan, assistance is through lineage, as we have explained. And on this basis many cases of the issues of 'aqila are derived. Translation: And the person whose residence is in Basra and his diwan is in Kufa, then the people of Kufa will pay the blood money on his behalf, because he seeks help from his diwan people, not from his neighbors. The gist is that seeking help from the diwan is more apparent, so with the diwan, the ruling of assistance through kinship, lineage, patronage, proximity of residence, etc., does not appear. And after the diwan, assistance is through lineage according to the detail we have explained. And on this principle many forms of issues of 'aqila are derived. Explanation: A person lives in Basra but his diwan people are in Kufa, so the people of Kufa will pay the blood money on his behalf because he is from the diwan people and seeks help from them, not from his neighbors. In any case, among the different types of assistance, assistance through diwan is the strongest, so when this assistance exists, no other assistance will be considered. After this, assistance through lineage comes next. And this is a principle on which many issues of blood money are derived.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This ruling establishes the priority of diwan (official military or administrative registration) over residence in determining the 'aqila. The Hanafi school holds that the diwan affiliation is the strongest form of nusra (assistance) because a person seeks help from those with whom he is registered, not necessarily his neighbors. Therefore, even if one resides in a different city, his 'aqila are the people of his diwan. This principle overrides kinship, patronage, and proximity of residence. Only if the diwan is absent does one revert to lineage-based nusra. This is a key rule (kulliyah) from which many specific cases are derived.

Key Terms
دیوان (dīwān): Official military or administrative registry determining a person's affiliation for 'aqila purposes.
نصرت (nuṣra): Assistance, specifically the duty of helping in times of need, forming the basis of 'aqila obligation.
قرابت (qarābat): Kinship; here considered secondary to diwan in establishing 'aqila.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The strength of mutual assistance (nusra) in the diwan
C) The geographical distance from residence
D) The number of relatives in the diwan

Key Takeaway
The diwan is the primary determinant of 'aqila in the Hanafi school, overriding residence, kinship, and other forms of assistance.
