City Diwan Pays Diya for Resident with Village Relatives
Ruling on aqila when city resident has village relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of the city diwan to pay diya for a resident with village relatives and evaluate the dispute on the condition of kinship.

Core Idea
The city diwan pays diya for any resident even without kinship because they are the defenders of all.

This passage from the Hidayah deals with a specific scenario: a city resident commits an accidental killing, has no stipend in the diwan, and his blood relatives live in the desert or village. The ruling of Imam Muhammad is that the city diwan pays the diya. However, an alternative interpretation suggests that kinship is required. Understanding this ruling clarifies the basis of 'aqila obligation in Hanafi law and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage and extract the facts: city resident, accidental killing, no stipend, relatives in village. State the ruling: diwan pays diya.
Note that the criminal has no stipend – this is not a condition but shows the diwan's duty extends beyond stipend-holders.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The reasoning is that the diwan are the defenders (yadhabbuna) and assistants of all city dwellers. This is the 'illa for the obligation.
No explicit Quran or hadith is cited; the proof is based on the function of the diwan as protectors.
3
Identify the alternative interpretation
Some scholars interpret Imam Muhammad's statement differently: they require kinship between the criminal and the diwan, based on the book's earlier remark that 'the people of the desert are closer to him in lineage'.
This interpretation treats kinship as the basis of obligation, not the protective role.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjih
The text rejects the restrictive interpretation by stating 'qila huwa sahih' – it is said that the first view is correct. The obligation is on the diwan because of their role, not kinship.
The phrase 'qila huwa sahih' is a tarjih indicator, favoring the broader obligation.
5
Apply the analogy of ghaybah munqati'ah
The passage draws an analogy: just as in inheritance a distant heir inherits when a closer one is absent, here the city diwan (distant in lineage) is responsible due to proximity in location and ability to assist.
This qiyas reinforces the idea that proximity in place can override distance in lineage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شہر کا رہائشی کوئی جنایت کرے اور نسبی اقرباء دیہات میں ہیں تو وہ دیت ادا کریں گے
ومن جنى جناية من اهل المصر وليس له فى الديوان عطاء واهل البادية اقرب اليه ومسكنه المصر عقل عنه اهل الديوان من ذلك المصر ولم يشترط ان يكون بينه وبين اهل الديوان قرابة وقيل هو صحيح لان الذين يذبون عن اهل المصر ويقومون بنصرتهم ويدفعون عنهم اهل الديوان من اهل المصر ولا يخصون به اهل العطاء
ترجمہ: اور اہل شہر میں جس نے کوئی جنایت کی اور دیوان میں اس کے لئے کوئی عطیہ نہیں ہے اور باعتبار نسب گاؤں اس کے زیادہ قریب ہیں اور اس کا مسکن شہر ہے تو اس شہر کے اہل دیوان اس کی دیت ادا کریں گے اور محمد نے یہ شرط بیان نہیں کی کہ اس کے اور اہل دیوان کے درمیان کوئی قرابت ہو اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہی صحیح ہے اس لئے کہ جو اہل شہر کی طرف سے دفاع کرتے ہیں اور ان کی نصرت کے لئے قائم ہوتے ہیں اور ان کی طرف سے مدافعت کرتے ہیں وہ اہل شہر میں سے اہل دیوان ہیں اور اہل دیوان مدافعت کے ساتھ اہل عطاء کو خاص نہیں کرتے ۔
تشریح: ایک آدمی شہر میں رہتا ہے اور اس کے نسبی اقرباء گاؤں میں رہتے ہیں اب اگر یہ شخص کوئی جنایت کرتا ہے تو جس شہر میں یہ ہے وہاں کے اہل دیوان اس کی دیت ادا کریں گے خواہ مجرم اور اہل دیوان کے درمیان کوئی قرابت ہو یا نہ ہو اور بعض حضرات نے اس کو صحیح قرار دیا ہے اس لئے کہ اہل شہر پر آنے والی مصیبت کی مدافعت وہ اس شہر کے اہل دیوان کا فریضہ ہے اور اہل دیوان فقط اپنی یا ابل عطا ہی کی نصرت کے ذمہ دار نہیں بلکہ تمام شہر کے لوگوں کی حفاظت و نصرت کے ذمہ دار ہیں تو اہل دیوان ہی مجرم کے اہل نصرت میں ہوں گے اور یہی عاقلہ ہوں گے ۔
یہ تفصیل اس وقت میں ہے جب کہ اہل دیوان اور اس مجرم کے درمیان کوئی قرابت نہ ہو اور اگر متن کی دوسری تاویل کی جائے کہ مجرم کے قریبی رشتہ دار گاؤں میں ہیں اور شہر کے اہل دیوان بھی اس کے رشتہ دار اور اعزہ ہیں مگر گاؤں والوں کے ساتھ قرابت کا قرب ہے اور اہل دیوان کے ساتھ قرابت کا بعد ہے جب بھی شہر کے اہل دیوان دیت ادا کریں گے۔
وقيل تاويله اذا كان قريبا لهم وفى الكتاب اشارة اليه حيث قال واهل البادية اقرب اليه من اهل المصر وهذا لان الوجوب عليهم بحكم القرابة واهل المصر اقرب منهم مكانا فكانت القدرة على النصرة لهم وصار نظير مسالة الغسة المنقطعة [؟]
ترجمہ: اور کہا گیا ہے کہ اس کی تاویل یہ ہے کہ جب کہ وہ مجرم ان کا قریبی ہو اور کتاب میں اس کی جانب اشارہ ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ کتاب میں کہا ہے اور گاؤں والے شہر والوں کے مقابلہ میں اس کے زیادہ قریبی ہیں اور یہ اس لئے کہ ان پر وجوب قرابت کے حکم سے ہے اور شہر والے گاؤں والوں سے زیادہ قریب ہیں جگہ کے اعتبار سے تو نصرت کے اوپر قدرت انہی کو ہوگی اور یہ غیبت منقطعہ کے مسئلہ کی نظیر ہو گیا۔
تشریح: بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ امام محمد کے قول میں جو یہ فرمایا گیا ہے ” عقل عنه اهل الديوان من ذلك المصريال“ وقت ہے جب کہ مجرم اور ان اہل دیوان کے درمیان قرابت ہو چونکہ امام محمد کا قول جو اس سے پہلے گذرا ہے یعنی اهل البادية اقرب اليه اس کی جانب مشیر ہے۔
A city resident commits an offense and his relatives by lineage are in the village, then they will pay the blood money. And whoever commits an offense from among the people of the city and he has no stipend in the diwan, and the people of the desert are closer to him in lineage, and his residence is the city, the people of the diwan of that city pay blood money for him. And Muhammad did not stipulate that there be kinship between him and the people of the diwan. And it was said: this is correct, because those who defend the people of the city and stand for their assistance and repel from them are the people of the diwan from the people of the city, and they do not restrict it to the people of the stipend. ... And it was said: its interpretation is when he is a relative of them, and in the book there is an indication to it where he said 'and the people of the desert are closer to him than the people of the city'. And this is because the obligation upon them is by virtue of kinship, and the people of the city are closer to them in place, so they have the ability for assistance, and it becomes similar to the case of ghaybah munqati'ah [?]. Translation: ... And some said: its interpretation is that when he is a relative of them, and in the book there is an indication to it where it said 'and the people of the desert are closer to him than the people of the city'. And this is because the obligation upon them is by virtue of kinship, and the people of the city are closer than them in place, so they have the ability for assistance, and it became similar to the case of disconnected ghaybah. Explanation: Some scholars said that in Imam Muhammad's statement where he said 'the people of the diwan of that city pay blood money for him', the time is when the criminal and those diwan people are relatives, because Imam Muhammad's earlier statement 'and the people of the desert are closer to him' points to it.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a city resident commits an accidental killing, has no stipend (ata') in the diwan, and his blood relatives live in the desert/village. The ruling from Imam Muhammad is that the people of the diwan of his city pay the diya, without requiring kinship between them. This is the relied-upon position. The reason is that the diwan people are the defenders and assistants of all city dwellers, not just stipend holders. However, an alternative interpretation (ta'wil) suggests that the ruling applies specifically when the criminal is a relative of the diwan people, because the obligation is based on kinship, and the city diwan are closer in location, making them more capable of assistance. This interpretation is supported by the book's earlier statement that 'the people of the desert are closer to him in lineage'. The difference has practical consequences: under the first view, the diwan pays even without kinship; under the second, they only pay if they are relatives. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is the first, as indicated by the phrase 'qila huwa sahih' (it was said it is correct). The analogy with ghaybah munqati'ah (disconnected absence) is used: just as in inheritance, a distant relative inherits when closer ones are absent, here the city diwan (though distant in lineage) are responsible due to proximity.

Key Terms
عطاء (‘aṭā’): Stipend or salary from the diwan; a person without ata' is still under the diwan's protection.
تاویل (ta’wīl): Interpretation; here an alternative understanding of Imam Muhammad's statement.
غیبت منقطعہ (ghaybah munqaṭi‘ah): Disconnected absence; a legal analogy from inheritance where distant heirs inherit when closer ones are absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, when a city resident without a stipend commits accidental killing and his relatives are in the village, who pays the diya?
A) His relatives in the village
B) The city diwan people only if they are his relatives
C) The city diwan people regardless of kinship
D) The city residents collectively

Key Takeaway
When a city resident commits accidental killing and has no stipend, the city's diwan must pay the diya, even if they are not his relatives, because they are the protectors of all city dwellers.

Mutual 'Aqila Among Non-Muslims: The Condition of Open Enmity
Ruling on 'aqila among non-Muslims of differing creeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'aqila liability among non-Muslims of different religions and identify the condition that negates mutual liability.

Core Idea
Mutual 'aqila among non-Muslims is severed by open enmity, not by difference in creed.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the liability of non-Muslims to pay diyah for one another. The key principle is that all non-Muslims, regardless of their specific religious affiliation, are considered one 'aqila group—unless open hostility exists between them. Understanding this exception is crucial for correctly applying the rules of 'aqila in a multi-faith context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
The passage states that non-Muslims of different creeds are each other's 'aqila because 'disbelief is all equal'. This is the default rule.
The ruling applies to all non-Muslim groups, regardless of their specific religion.
2
Identify the Exception
The exception is when there is open enmity between the groups. In that case, they are not each other's 'aqila.
Open enmity (kholī hū'ī 'adāwat) is the key condition that nullifies mutual liability.
3
Understand the Basis
The basis of 'aqila is mutual support (tanasur). Open enmity cuts off this support, severing the 'aqila relationship.
Mutual support is the underlying reason for the liability.
4
Note the Example
Jews and Christians are cited as an example of groups with open enmity, even though both are non-Muslim.
This illustrates that enmity, not religious difference, is the deciding factor.
5
Recall the Authority
The ruling is transmitted from Imam Abu Yusuf, one of the major Hanafi authorities.
This gives the ruling weight within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور کفار اگر چہ باہم مختلف ملت رکھتے ہوں لیکن کفر سب برابر ہے اس لئے وہ دوسرے کی دیت دیں گے۔ لیکن یہ اس وقت ہے جب کہ ان میں کھلی ہوئی عداوت نہ ہو جیسے یہودو نصاری اگر چہ دونوں کا فر ہیں لیکن آپس میں کھلی ہوئی دشمنی ہے اس لئے ان میں سے ایک دوسرے کی دیت ادا نہیں کریں گے کیونکہ با ہمی تناصر جو عاقلہ ہونے کا مدار ہے منقطع ہے امام ابو یوسف سے بھی ایسے ہی منقول ہے۔
And if non-Muslims, even if they follow different creeds, but disbelief is all equal, therefore they will pay the diyah of one another. But this is when there is no open enmity among them. For example, Jews and Christians, although both are disbelievers, but there is open hostility between them, therefore they will not pay the diyah of one another, because mutual support (tanasur) which is the basis of being an 'aqila is cut off. Similarly, it is transmitted from Imam Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on 'aqila liability among non-Muslims. The general principle is that all non-Muslims, despite difference in religion, are considered one group for purposes of mutual liability of diyah because their disbelief is equal. However, this applies only when there is no open enmity between them. If there is open hostility, like between Jews and Christians, they do not act as each other's 'aqila. The reasoning is that mutual support, which is the basis of 'aqila, is severed by such enmity. This ruling is transmitted from Imam Abu Yusuf and is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
عاقلة ('āqila): The group responsible for paying diyah (blood money) for accidental killing, typically the male relatives or tribe.
دية (diyah): Financial compensation paid to the heirs of a victim in cases of accidental killing or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition do non-Muslims of different religions not act as each other's 'aqila?
A) If they follow different religions
B) If there is open enmity between them
C) If they are from different countries
D) If they are of different genders

Key Takeaway
Non-Muslims of different religions are each other's 'aqila unless open enmity severs mutual support.

Transfer of Diwan and 'Aqila Liability: The Hanafi Position
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'aqila liability with proof and distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on 'aqila liability when a killer's diwan is transferred before judgment, and distinguish between naql and damm.

Core Idea
Who is liable for diyah when the killer moves? The Hanafi school says the 'aqila at judgment; Zufar says at the crime.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about which 'aqila (group responsible for diyah) bears liability when a killer is transferred from one military diwan to another before a judge issues a ruling. The Hanafi majority holds that the 'aqila at the time of judgment is liable, while Imam Zufar and one narration from Abu Yusuf hold that the 'aqila at the time of the crime is liable. We will analyze both proofs and also explore the distinction between impermissible transfer (naql) and permissible addition (damm) when the 'aqila becomes insufficient after judgment.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf (in the apparent madhhab), and Muhammad al-Shaybani: the 'aqila at the time of judgment is liable for diyah.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
2
Identify the Opponent and Their View
State that Imam Zufar and a narration from Abu Yusuf hold that the 'aqila at the time of the crime is liable.
This is a weaker view within the Hanafi school.
3
Follow the Opponent's Proof
Zufar argues that the obligation arises from the crime itself, which occurred when the killer was registered in Kufa's diwan. He analogizes to the case where judgment is passed first and then transfer: there, the obligation remains with the original 'aqila.
The analogy is based on the idea that the cause (crime) fixes liability.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response is that wealth (diyah) becomes obligatory only at judgment. Before judgment, only the killer owes a 'mithl' (like). The transfer from killer to 'aqila occurs via judgment. Therefore, the 'aqila at judgment bears liability. After judgment, transfer is impermissible because the duty is fixed.
The key distinction is that judgment is the operative cause for 'aqila liability, not the crime itself.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: if the killer moves from Kufa to Basra before judgment, the Hanafis impose diyah on the Basra 'aqila; Zufar imposes it on the Kufa 'aqila.
This directly affects which community pays diyah.
6
Distinguish Naql from Damm
If the 'aqila becomes insufficient after judgment, the solution is not to transfer (naql) liability to another group, but to add (damm) the closest relatives. Naql abrogates the first judgment; damm confirms it by increasing the number of bearers.
This distinction is crucial to preserving the validity of the judge's ruling.

Source Text

ولو كان القاتل من اهل الكوفة وله بها عطاء فحول ديوانه الى البصرة ثم رفع الى القاضي فانه يقضى بالدية على عاقلته من اهل البصرة وقال زفر يقضى على عاقلته من اهل الكوفة وهو رواية عن ابي يوسف لان الموجب الجناية وقد تحققت وعاقلته اهل الكوفة وصار كما اذا حول بعد القضاء
ترجمہ اور اگر قاتل اہل کوفہ میں سے ہو اور اس کے لئے کوفہ میں عطاء ہو پس اس کا دیوان بصرہ کی طرف پھیر دیا گیا پھر معاملہ قتل کا خاص کی طرف مرافعہ کیا گیا تو قاضی دیت کا فیصلہ اس عاقلہ پر کرے گا جو اہل بصرہ میں سے ہیں اور زقر نے فرمایا کہ قاضی اس کے اس عاقلہ پر فیصلہ کرے گا جو اہل کوفہ میں سے ہیں اور یہی ایک روایت ہے ابو یوسف سے اس لئے کہ واجب کرنے والی چیز وہ جنایت ہے اور وہ تحقیق ہو چکی ہے حالانکہ اس کے عاقلہ اہل کوفہ ہیں اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے دیوان متحول کیا گیا ہو قضاء قاضی کے بعد ۔ تشریح ایک شخص کو فہ کا باشندہ ہے اور وہ کوفہ ہی کے اندر اہل دیوان میں سے ہے تو یہی اہل دیوان اس کے عاقلہ تھے [كمائر انتو] اگر اس نے خطاء کسی کو قتل کیا تو اہل دیوان پر دبیت آتی لیکن بعد قبل القضاء، قاتل کو بصرہ کے دیوان میں منتقل کر دیا اور بعد انتقال قاضی کے سامنے یہ مشتاقبل پیش کیا گیا تو اب قاضی دیت کا فیصلہ عاقلہ پر کرے گا لیکن سوال یہ ہے کہ دیت کا فیصلہ کوفہ کے اہل دیوان پر ہوگا یا بصرہ کے تو ہمارا مسلک یہ ہے کہ بصرہ کے اہل دیوان پر دیت کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا اور امام زفر اور ایک روایت میں امام ابو یوسف یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ کوفہ کے اہل دیوان پر دیت کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔ ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دیت کا اصل وجوب جرم و جنایت کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور جب یہ جنایت اس باتل سے صادر ہوئی تھی اس وقت اس کا نام کوفہ کے دیوان میں تھا لہذا انہی پر دیت واجب ہوگی کیونکہ اگر قاضی نے کوفہ والوں پر دیت کا فیصلہ کر دیا ہو اور بعد قضاء قاضی کے اس کو بصرہ کے دیوان میں منتقل کیا گیا ہو تو وہاں بالاتفاق دیت کا وجوب اہل کوفہ پر برقرار رہے گا لہذا یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہونا چاہئے ۔
دلیل احناف
ولنا ان المال انما يجب عند القضاء لما ذكرنا ان الواجب هو المثل وبالقضاء ينتقل الى المال وكذا الوجوب على القاتل وتتحمل عنه عاقلته واذا كان كذلك يتحمل عنه من يكون عاقلته عند القضاء بخلاف ما بعد القضاء لان الواجب قد تقرر بالقضاء فلا ينتقل بعد ذلك لكن حصة القاتل تؤخذ من عطائه بالبصرة لانها تؤخذ من العطاء وعطاءه بالبصرة
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مال بوقت قضا واجب ہوتا ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں کہ واجب وہ مثل ہے اور قضاء کی وجہ سے وجوب مال کی طرف منتقل ہوتا ہے اور ایسے ہی وجوب قاتل کے اوپر ہے اور قاتل کی طرف سے اس کا عا قدم تحمل کرتا ہے اور جب بات ایسے ہے تو بوقت قضاء جو اس کا عاقلہ ہو گا وہ اس کا مکمل کرے گا بخلاف مابعد القضاء کے اس لئے کہ واجب قضاء کی وجہ سے منتقر ر ہو چکا ہے پس اس کے بعد واجب منتقل نہ ہوگا لیکن قاتل کا حصہ اس کے اس عطیہ میں سے لیا جائے گا جو بصرہ میں ہو اس لئے کہ دیت عطاء میں سے لیجاتی ہے اور اس کی عطاء بصرہ میں ہے۔
تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مال کا وجوب اصل جنایت کی وجہ سے نہیں ہوتا اور نہ اصل جنایت سے مثل کا وجوب ہوتا ہے نیز اصل جنایت سے مثل کا وجوب قاتل پر ہوتا ہے، پھر مثل سے قیمت کی جانب اور قاتل سے عاقلہ کی جانب جو تحول ہے یہ قضاء قاضی کی وجہ سے ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ مال کا وجوب قضاء کی وجہ سے ہے لہذا بوقت قضاء قاضی جو اس کے عاقلہ ہوں گے انہی پر دیت واجب کی جائے گی اور اس وقت اس کے عاقلہ اہل بصرہ ہیں لہذا انہی پر دیت واجب ہوگی۔
رہا دوسرا مسئلہ جس پر امام زفر نے اس مسئلہ کو قیاس کیا ہے یعنی اگر قاتل ابھی کوفہ کے دیوان میں ہے اور کوفہ کے اہل دیوان پر قاضی نے دیت کا فیصلہ کر دیا پھر قاتل کو بصرہ کے دیوان میں منتقل کر دیا گیا ہے تو اب وجوب جن پر ہوا ہے وہاں سے بہے گا نہیں کیونکہ اس کا نام نقل ہے اور نقل نا جائز ہے۔ ہاں اس میں اتنا خیال ضرور رکھا جائے گا کہ قاتل بھی عاقلہ کا ایک فرد بن کردیت دیتا ہے تو قاتل سے جو دیت کا حصہ وصول کیا جائے گا اس عطاء میں سے وصول کیا جائے گا جو بصرہ کی ہوگی اور جو اس کو پہلے کوفہ کی عطا یا ہوتی ہیں ان میں سے دیت وصول نہیں کی جائے گی کیونکہ آئندہ عطایا میں سے دیت لی جاتی ہے اور آئندہ عطا یا اس کو بصرہ میں ہوں گی نہ کہ کوفہ کے اندر۔ قضاء قاضی کے بعد عاقلہ اتنی کم ہو جائے کہ ادائیگی دیت کے لئے ناکافی ہو تو کون سا راستہ اختیار کیا جائے گا ؟
بخلاف ما اذا قلة العاقلة بعد القضاء عليهم حيث يضم اليهم اقرب القبائل في النسب لان في النقل ابطال حكم الاول فلا يجوز بحال و فى الضم تكثير المتحملين لما قضى به عليهم فكان فيه تقرير الحكم الأول لا ابطاله
ترجمہ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ عاقلہ پر فیصلہ کے بعد عاقلہ کم ہو جائے تو ان کی طرف نسب کے اعتبار سے اقرب القبائل کو ملا دیا جائے گا اس لئے کر نقل میں حکم اول کا ابطال ہے تو یہ کسی حال میں جائز نہیں ہے اور ملا دینے میں ان لوگوں کی تکثیر ہے جو اس کو اٹھانے والے ہیں جس کا ان پر فیصلہ کیا گیا ہے تو اس میں حکم اول کی تقریر ہے نہ کہ اس کا ابطال ۔ تشریح سوال ، آپ نے فرمایا کہ فقل جائز نہیں ہے لہذا اہل کوفہ پر فیصلہ کے بعد پھر اہل بصرہ پر فیصلہ وجوب دبیت کا نہ ہوگا ور نہ نقل
A resident of Kufa whose name was in the diwan of Kufa was transferred to Basra, so will his 'aqila be the people of Basra or the people of Kufa? The madhhab of Ahnaf: And if the killer is from the people of Kufa and has a stipend ('ata') there, then his diwan is transferred to Basra. Then the case is raised to the judge. He will decide the diyah on his 'aqila from the people of Basra. Zufar said: He will decide on his 'aqila from the people of Kufa, and this is a narration from Abu Yusuf, because the cause is the crime, and it has occurred while his 'aqila are the people of Kufa. It is as if he transferred after the judgment. Commentary: A person is a resident of Kufa and he is among the people of the diwan of Kufa, so these are his 'aqila. [As before], if he accidentally kills someone, the diyah is due on the people of the diwan. But before judgment, the killer's diwan is transferred to Basra, and after the transfer the case is brought before the judge. Now the judge will decide the diyah on the 'aqila. The question: will it be decided on the diwan of Kufa or of Basra? Our madhhab: it will be decided on the diwan of Basra. Imam Zufar and in one narration Imam Abu Yusuf say it will be decided on the diwan of Kufa. Their proof: the obligation of diyah arises from the crime, and when this crime occurred, his name was in the diwan of Kufa, so they are obligated. Because if the judge had decided on the people of Kufa and after the judgment the killer was transferred to Basra , there the obligation remains on the people of Kufa by consensus. So here it should be the same. Proof of the Ahnaf: And for us, wealth is obligated at the time of judgment because, as we have mentioned, what is obligated is like [equivalent] and by judgment it transfers to wealth. Similarly, the obligation is on the killer and his 'aqila bears it on his behalf. So if that is the case, whoever is his 'aqila at the time of judgment will bear it, unlike after the judgment, because the obligation has been established by judgment, so it does not transfer after that. But the share of the killer is taken from his stipend in Basra because it is taken from the stipend and his stipend is in Basra. Commentary: This is our proof, the gist of which is that the obligation of wealth does not arise from the crime itself, nor does the obligation of like arise from the crime itself. Also, the obligation of like arises on the killer. Then the transfer from like to value and from the killer to the 'aqila takes place due to the judge's judgment. So it is known that the obligation of wealth arises due to judgment. Therefore, at the time of judgment, whoever are his 'aqila, the diyah will be obligated on them. At that time, his 'aqila are the people of Basra, so the diyah is obligated on them. As for the other case on which Imam Zufar analogized this issue: if the killer is still in the diwan of Kufa and the judge has decided the diyah on the people of Kufa, then the killer is transferred to the diwan of Basra, the obligation does not move from where it occurred because that would be a transfer (naql) and transfer is not permissible. Yes, it should be considered that the killer is also an individual of the 'aqila and pays diyah. So the portion collected from the killer will be taken from his stipend in Basra because the diyah is taken from future stipends, and his future stipends will be in Basra, not in Kufa. If after the judgment the 'aqila becomes so few that they are insufficient to pay the diyah, what course should be taken? Unlike when after judgment the 'aqila becomes few: in that case the closest tribes in lineage are added to them, because in transfer (naql) there is abrogation of the first ruling, so it is not permissible at all. And in adding (damm) there is multiplication of those who bear what has been decided upon them, so in it there is confirmation of the first ruling, not its abrogation. Commentary: You have said that transfer is not permissible, so after judgment on the people of Kufa, then judgment on the people of Basra for the diyah obligation will not occur; nor is transfer (naql).
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of the 'aqila (group responsible for paying diyah) when the killer, who is registered in a military diwan (register) with a stipend ('ata'), moves to another city before judgment. The Hanafi position (of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) is that the 'aqila at the time of judgment is liable. Imam Zufar and a narration from Abu Yusuf hold that the 'aqila at the time of the crime is liable. The text begins by stating the Hanafi ruling in the Arabic matn, then gives Zufar's view and his proof. The Hanafi proof, presented under 'Dalil Ahnaf', argues that the obligation of wealth (diyah) arises only at the time of judgment because initially what is due is 'mithl' ( like) which is a liability on the killer. The killer bears it, and his 'aqila bears it on his behalf. The transfer from mithl to wealth and from killer to 'aqila occurs due to judgment. Therefore, the relevant 'aqila is the one at the time of judgment. Zufar's analogy to the case where the transfer occurs after judgment is rejected because after judgment the obligation is established and cannot be transferred. However, if the 'aqila becomes insufficient after judgment, the solution is not to transfer to a new group, but to add the closest relatives in lineage (damm) because transfer would nullify the first judgment, which is impermissible. Adding increases the number of bearers and confirms the original ruling. The text ends by emphasizing this distinction.

Key Terms
ديوان (diwan): A military or administrative register listing the names of those eligible for stipends ('ata'), often used as the basis for 'aqila liability in the Hanafi school.
عطاء ('ata'): A stipend or allowance granted by the state, from which diyah is taken when the killer is not a soldier.
نقل (naql): Transfer of liability from one 'aqila to another, which is impermissible after judgment because it nullifies the first ruling.
ضم (damm): Adding additional relatives or tribes to the existing 'aqila to make up for insufficiency, without transferring the obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which 'aqila is liable for diyah when a killer's diwan is transferred before the judge issues a ruling?
A) The 'aqila at the time of the crime
B) The 'aqila at the time of judgment
C) Both equally
D) Neither; the killer pays alone

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, 'aqila liability for diyah arises at the time of judgment, not at the time of the crime; transfer of liability after judgment is impermissible but addition to the existing 'aqila is allowed.

When Heirs' Permission for a Bequest Becomes Binding
Ruling on when heirs' permission for bequest is binding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the timing condition for heirs' permission to be binding and apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing before-death from after-death permission.

Core Idea
Heirs' permission binds only after death; before death, it is void and revocable.

This lesson examines a critical nuance in Hanafi inheritance law: the timing of heirs' permission for a bequest that exceeds one-third of the estate or benefits an heir. The passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that permission given after the testator's death is final and irrevocable, while permission given during the testator's lifetime carries no legal weight. The difference stems from the nature of the heirs' right: it only becomes an established right after death. Before death, there is no right to waive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage contrasts two situations: heirs' permission after death vs. before death. Identify the ruling for each.
2
Analyze the underlying principle
Understand why pre-death permission fails: the heirs' right is not yet established (thabit), and any dropped right (saqit) is treated as nonexistent.
3
Examine the istinad argument
The text addresses an implied objection about legal attribution (istinad). Explain why attribution cannot revive a nonexistent permission.
Istinad requires the thing to exist at the moment of attribution.
4
Differentiate haqiqah from mujarrad haqq
Real ownership (mulk haqiqi) is established only at death; before death, there is only a mere right. This prevents pre-death permission from being effective through istinad.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Given a similar case (e.g., usurpation analogy), determine whether pre-death permission could be effective by analogy.
The usurpation analogy is rejected because the permission has ceased to exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اجازت موسی کی موت کے بعد ہے تو اجازت درست ہے اور اب ورثہ کو اپنی اجازت سے پھرنے کا حق نہیں ہے اور اگر ورثہ کی اجازت موصی کی زندگی میں ہو تو ابھی اس اجازت کا کوئی اعتبار نہ ہوگا بلکہ ورثہ کو بعد موت موصی اس اجازت سے پھرنے کا اختیار ہوگا کیونکہ موت موصی سے پہلے ورثہ کا حق ثابت ہی نہیں ہوا تو اجازت بھی ان کی معتبر نہ ہوگی لیکن موت کے بعد ان کا حق ثابت ہو گیا تو جب انہوں نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا یعنی اجازت دے دی تو اب حق ساقط ہو گیا اور جو ساقط ہو گیا وہ نہ ہونے کے درجہ میں ہو گیا۔
غایة البیان میں لان الساقط متلاش کا تعلق موصی کی حیات میں اجازت دینے سے کیا ہے یعنی اس وقت میں ورنہ کی اجازت ساقط ہے اور ساقط معدوم کے درجہ میں ہے اور جب وہ معدوم کے درجہ میں ہے تو اس اجازت کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے لہذ اور شہ کو اس کی تردید کا حق ہے۔
سوال مقدر کا جواب
غاية الامرانه يستند عند الاجازة لكن الاستناد يظهر فى حق القائم وهذا قد مضى وتلاشى ترجمہ غایہ الامر یہ ہے کہ حق کا استناد بوقت اجازت ہوگا لیکن استناد تو امر موجود میں ظاہر ہوتا ہے حالانکہ یہ ( قبل الموت کی اجازت ) گزرگئی اور معدوم ہو گئی ہے۔
تشریح یہ حقیقت میں ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔
سوال موت سے پہلے ورثہ نے جو اجازت دی تھی وہ بھی اپنے حق میں دی تھی ، کیونکہ میت کے مال میں ورثہ کا جو حق ہے وہ مرض موت کے وقت سے ہے تو جب بطریق استناد بوقت اجازت ورثہ ان کا حق ثابت ہو گیا تو ان کی اجازت معتبر ہونی چاہئے جیسے غصب میں؟
جواب اگر چہ وارثوں کا حق میت کے ابتدائی مرض ہی سے اس مال کے ساتھ متعلق ہو جاتا ہے لیکن ایک تو ان کو تصرف کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ دوسرے یہ کہ استناد کے لئے اس چیز کی بقاء کی ضرورت ہے جس کو بطریق استناد ثابت کرنے کی کوشش کی جارہی ہے اور وہ اجازت ہے حالانکہ جو اجازت قبل الموت دی گئی تھی اب وہ معدوم ہو چکی ہے لہذا بطریق استناد بھی اس اجازت کا ثبوت نہ ہو سکے گا۔
مذکورہ جواب کی مزید وضاحت
ولان الحقيقة تثبت عند الموت وقبله يثبت مجرد الحق فلو استند من كل وجه ينقلب حقيقة قبله والرضا ببطلان الحق لا يكون رضا ببطلان الحقيقة
ترجمہ اور اس لئے کہ ملک حقیقی موت کے وقت ثابت ہوتی ہے اور موت سے پہلے محض حق ثابت ہوتا ہے پس اگر ہر ہر اعتبار سے استناد ثابت ہو جائے تو حق حقیقت سے بدل جائے گا موت سے پہلے ہی اور بطلان حق سے راضی ہونا بطلان حقیقت سے راضی ہونا نہیں ہے۔
If the permission [of the heirs] is after the death of the testator, the permission is valid and the heirs have no right to revoke their permission. But if the heirs' permission is during the testator's lifetime, then this permission has no weight; rather, the heirs will have the option to revoke this permission after the testator's death, because before the testator's death the right of the heirs has not been established, so their permission is not valid. But after death their right is established, so when they have dropped their right—i.e., given permission—then the right is dropped, and what has dropped is like nonexistent.
In Ghayat al-Bayan: because the dropped [right] is lost, this is connected to giving permission during the testator's lifetime. That is, at that time the permission of the heir is dropped, and what is dropped is in the category of nonexistent. When it is in the category of nonexistent, this permission has no weight. Therefore other heirs have the right to reject it.
Answer to an implied question:
The point is that the right is attributed at the time of permission, but attribution appears in a matter that is existing, while this (permission before death) has passed and become nonexistent.
Explanation: This is actually the answer to an implied question.
Question: The permission given by the heirs before death was given regarding their own right, because the right of the heirs in the property of the deceased is from the time of the death-illness. So, if the right is attributed at the time of permission, the heirs' right is established, so their permission should be valid, like in the case of usurpation?
Answer: Although the heirs' right becomes attached to this property from the beginning of the fatal illness, first, they do not have the authority to dispose of it; second, for attribution, the existence of the thing being attributed is required, which is the permission, while the permission given before death has become nonexistent. Therefore, through attribution, this permission cannot be proven.
Further clarification of the above answer:
And because real ownership is established at death; before death, mere right is established. If attribution were proven from every aspect, it would turn the right into real ownership before death, and being content with the annulment of a right is not being content with the annulment of real ownership.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the timing of heirs' permission for a bequest exceeding one-third. The commentator, following the text of Al-Hidayah, establishes two distinct scenarios. First, if the heirs give permission after the testator's death, this permission is valid and irrevocable. The heirs cannot later revoke it because their right to the estate has already been established, and they have voluntarily dropped it. Second, if permission is given during the testator's lifetime, it is of no legal effect. The heirs may change their minds and refuse after death. The reason is that before death, the heirs have no established right in the estate—only a potential right that becomes actual upon death. The commentator uses the principle that a dropped right (saqit) is like a nonexistent thing. He then addresses an implied question: if we consider that the right is attributed (istinad) back to the time of permission, why isn't pre-death permission valid? The answer is twofold: (1) the heirs have no right of disposal before death, and (2) attribution requires the existence of the thing being attributed, but the permission has vanished by the time of death. Finally, he cites the Arabic text: real ownership (al-haqiqah) is established only at death; before that there is mere right (mujarrad al-haqq). If we attribute ownership back to pre-death, it would turn right into ownership prematurely, which is invalid. Being content with annulment of a right does not imply contentment with annulment of real ownership. This nuanced distinction prevents the pre-death permission from becoming effective through istinad.

Key Terms
اجازة (ijazah): Permission given by heirs for a bequest exceeding one-third or to an heir.
استناد (istinad): Attribution of a legal effect back to the time of a prior act or event.
ملک حقیقی (mulk haqiqi): Real ownership, fully established at the testator's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if heirs give permission for an excessive bequest during the testator's lifetime, what is the status of that permission?
A) It is valid and binding; heirs cannot revoke it after death.
B) It is invalid and has no effect; heirs may revoke it after death.
C) It is suspended pending the testator's death, then becomes binding.
D) It is valid only if the testator confirms it in his will.

Key Takeaway
Heirs' permission for a bequest is only binding if given after the testator's death; pre-death permission is ineffective because the right to the estate is not yet established.

Bequest to Heir with Permission: Ownership Dispute with Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on source of ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the legatee of a permitted bequest to an heir owns the property from the testator, and distinguish this from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Permission from other heirs removes an impediment; ownership still flows from the testator's will.

This passage addresses a dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i over the legal source of ownership in a bequest to an heir that is permitted by other heirs. The core question: from whom does the legatee receive the property? The Hanafi school argues that the cause of ownership is the testator's will, while permission merely clears a legal obstacle. The Shafi'i school attributes ownership to the heirs who gave permission. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
The Hanafi position: the legatee owns from the testator. The Shafi'i position: from the heir who gave permission.
Both agree the bequest is valid with permission; the dispute is about the source of ownership.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
The cause (sabab) of ownership is the will, which comes from the testator. Permission is removal of an impediment (mani')—the heirs' right to object. Attribution is to the cause, not the condition.
Analogy: mortgagee permits mortgagor's sale; ownership still from mortgagor.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Since the heirs remove the impediment, they must have some stake. Shafi'i argues that to remove an impediment, the heir must have possession (qabd) of the property at the time of permission.
This would imply the heirs own the property first and then transfer it to the legatee.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Possession is not a condition for removing an impediment. The impediment is merely the right to object; dropping that right suffices. Hence ownership remains from the testator.
The mortgage analogy reinforces: mortgagee's permission does not require possession.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If ownership is from the testator, the legatee takes free of heirs' claims. If from heirs, they must first own and transfer, which affects liability and timing.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of the disagreement).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و كذلک ان كانت الوصية للوارث واجازت البقيه فحكمه ما ذكرنا وكل ما جاز باجازة الوارث يتملكه المجازله من قبل الموصى عندنا وعند الشافعى من قبل الوارث والصحيح قولنا لان السبب صدر من الموصى والاجازة رفع المانع وليس من شرطة القبض وصار كالمرتهن اذا اجاز بيع الراهن. ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی اگر وصیت وارث کے لئے ہو اور بقیہ ورثہ نے اجازت دے دی ہو تو اس کا حکم وہی ہے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں اور وہ تصرف جو وارث کی اجازت سے جائز ہوا ہو تو مجازلۂ ہمارے نزدیک موصی کی طرف سے اس کا مالک ہوگا اور شافعی کے نزدیک وارث کی جانب سے اور صحیح ہمارا قول ہے اس لئے کہ سب موصی کی طرف سے صادر ہوا ہے اور اجازت تو مانع کو اٹھاد دینا ہے اور اس کی (ازالہ مانع کی شرط قبضہ نہیں ہے اور ایسا ہو گیا جیسے مرتہن جب کہ وہ راہن کی بیچ کی اجازت دیدے۔
تشریح اگر بجائے تہائی سے زیادہ وصیت کرنے کے موصی نے ورثہ کے لئے وصیت کر دی تو بھی یہی حکم ہے یعنی باقی ورثہ کی اجازت موقوف ہے ، اب اس میں سوال یہ ہے کہ موصی لا جو مالک بنا ہے تو موصی کی طرف سے بنا ہے یا وارث کی ، ہمارے نزدیک موصی کی طرف سے مالک بنا ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک وارث کی طرف سے۔
اس پر مصنف نے فرمایا کہ ہمارا قول صحیح ہے اس لئے کہ سبب ملک تو موصی کی جانب سے صادر ہوا ہے کیونکہ وصیت اس نے کی ہے البتہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں اس سبب کے کارگر ہونے کے لئے مانع کو دور کر دینا شرط ہے اور مانع ورثہ کے حق کا اسقاط ہے اور حکم کی اضافت سبب کی جانب ہوئی شرط کی طرف نہیں (الا ان يمنع مانع) سوال امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جب ورثہ کی طرف مانع کا ازالہ پایا گیا ہے تو ضروری ہے کہ ورثہ کا قبضہ بھی ہو حالانکہ ابھی اس مال پر ورثہ کا قبضہ نہیں ہے تو پھر ازالہ مانع اور رفع مانع کیسے درست ہو گیا ؟
جواب حضرت ازالہ مانع کے لئے قبضہ شرما نہیں ہے لہذا یہ اعتراض ہی بے بنیاد ہے اور یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ ملکیت کا اثبات موصی کی طرف سے ہے۔ اور یہ بالکل ایا ہے جیسے را ہن مربوں کو بیچ دے تو یہ بچ مرتہن کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے لیکن جب مرتہن نے بیچ کی اجازت دیدی تو بیچ کا ثبوت را جن کی طرف سے ہوگا نہ کہ مرتین کی۔
And similarly, if the bequest is made to an heir and the other heirs give permission, the ruling is as we have mentioned. Whatever is rendered valid by the permission of the heir, the recipient owns it from the testator according to us (Hanafis), but according to al-Shafi‘i, from the heir. And the correct view is ours, because the cause (sabab) originated from the testator, and permission is merely the removal of an impediment, and possession (qabd) is not a condition for it. This is like the case of the mortgagee (murtahin) when he permits the mortgagor (rahin) to sell.
Explanation: If instead of bequeathing more than one-third, the testator made a bequest to an heir, the same ruling applies: it is suspended upon the permission of the remaining heirs. Now the question is: from whom does the recipient become owner? According to us, he becomes owner from the testator; according to Imam al-Shafi‘i, from the heir. The author said that our statement is correct because the cause of ownership (sabab al-milk) originated from the testator, since he made the will. In both cases, for this cause to become effective, the removal of an impediment is required. The impediment is the dropping of the heirs' right. The ruling is attributed to the cause, not to the condition (unless there is a preventing impediment).
Question: Imam al-Shafi‘i says: when the removal of the impediment is found from the side of the heirs, then possession (qabd) by the heirs is necessary. But the heirs do not have possession of this property yet, so how can the removal of the impediment be valid?
Answer: For the removal of an impediment, possession is not a condition. Therefore this objection is baseless. And it is established that ownership is proven from the testator. This is exactly like the case of a mortgagor selling the mortgaged property; the sale is suspended upon the permission of the mortgagee. But when the mortgagee gives permission for the sale, the sale becomes effective from the side of the mortgagor, not from the mortgagee.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi‘i regarding the legal consequence of a bequest to an heir made with the permission of the other heirs. The Hanafi position (our view) is that the legatee (the heir beneficiary) becomes owner of the bequest from the testator (al-musi), not from the other heirs who gave permission. The ruling is similar to the earlier case of a bequest exceeding one-third. The commentator explains that the cause (sabab) of ownership is the will itself, which comes from the testator. The permission of the other heirs merely removes an impediment (al-mani‘) — namely, the right they have to prevent a bequest to an heir. The removal of an impediment does not constitute a new cause of ownership; it simply allows the original cause to take effect. Therefore, the ownership is attributed to the testator. Imam al-Shafi‘i argues that since the removal of the impediment comes from the heir, the ownership should be attributed to him, which would require the heir to have possession (qabd) of the property before the bequest can be valid. The Hanafi response is that possession is not a condition for removing an impediment. The commentator reinforces this with an analogy from mortgage law: when a mortgagor sells the mortgaged property with the mortgagee's permission, the sale is attributed to the mortgagor, not the mortgagee. The mortgagee merely allows the sale; he does not become the seller. Similarly, the heir granting permission does not become the grantor of ownership. This ruling is from Al-Hidayah and is considered the correct (sahih) position within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
وصية للوارث (wasaya lil-warith): A bequest made to an heir, which is normally invalid due to the hadith 'No bequest to an heir' but becomes valid with permission of other heirs.
سبب (sabab): The cause or legal basis for ownership; here, the testator's will.
مانع (mani'): An impediment that prevents the cause from taking effect; here, the right of other heirs to reject the bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a bequest to an heir with permission of other heirs, according to the Hanafi school, from whom does the recipient become owner?
A) From the testator, because the cause of ownership is the will.
B) From the heirs granting permission, because they removed the impediment.
C) From both the testator and the heirs equally.
D) From the state, because the property becomes unclaimed.

Key Takeaway
In a permitted bequest to an heir, the Hanafi school attributes ownership to the testator because the cause is the will, not the permission.

Bequest to an Heir with Heirs' Permission: Ownership from Testator
Ruling on bequest to heir and ownership attribution dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest to an heir after heirs' permission and explain why ownership is attributed to the testator rather than the heirs.

Core Idea
A bequest to an heir becomes valid with heirs’ permission, but ownership flows from the testator, not the heirs.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a key point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: when a testator bequeaths to a legal heir and the other heirs give permission after death, from whom does the beneficiary actually acquire ownership? The Hanafi position is that the cause (sabab) of ownership is the testator's bequest; the heirs' permission merely removes the impediment. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, including an analogy with mortgage, and explains the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the act is (bequest to an heir) and its general ruling (suspended on permission; valid if permission granted).
The ruling mirrors that of a bequest exceeding one-third.
2
Locate the point of dispute
Identify the specific issue contested between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: from whom does the beneficiary acquire ownership?
Hanafi: from testator. Shafi'i: from heirs.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Examine the qiyas (analogy) with the mortgagee's permission for the mortgagor's sale, and the response to the Shafi'i objection regarding possession.
The illa is that permission removes impediment but does not transfer ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و کذلک ان كانت الوصية للوارث واجازت البقيه فحكمه ما ذكرنا وكل ما جاز باجازة الوارث يتملكه المجاز له من قبل الموصى عندنا وعند الشافعى من قبل الوارث والصحيح قولنا لان السبب صدر من الموصى والاجازة رفع المانع وليس من شرطة القبض وصار كالمرتهن اذا اجاز بيع الراهن. تشریح: اگر بجائے تہائی سے زیادہ وصیت کرنے کے موصی نے ورثہ کے لئے وصیت کر دی تو بھی یہی حکم ہے یعنی باقی ورثہ کی اجازت موقوف ہے ، اب اس میں سوال یہ ہے کہ موصی لا جو مالک بنا ہے تو موصی کی طرف سے بنا ہے یا وارث کی ، ہمارے نزدیک موصی کی طرف سے مالک بنا ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک وارث کی طرف سے۔ اس پر مصنف نے فرمایا کہ ہمارا قول صحیح ہے اس لئے کہ سبب ملک تو موصی کی جانب سے صادر ہوا ہے کیونکہ وصیت اس نے کی ہے البتہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں اس سبب کے کارگر ہونے کے لئے مانع کو دور کر دینا شرط ہے اور مانع ورثہ کے حق کا اسقاط ہے اور حکم کی اضافت سبب کی جانب ہوئی شرط کی طرف نہیں (الا ان يمنع مانع) سوال امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جب ورثہ کی طرف مانع کا ازالہ پایا گیا ہے تو ضروری ہے کہ ورثہ کا قبضہ بھی ہو حالانکہ ابھی اس مال پر ورثہ کا قبضہ نہیں ہے تو پھر ازالہ مانع اور رفع مانع کیسے درست ہو گیا ؟ جواب حضرت ازالہ مانع کے لئے قبضہ شرط نہیں ہے لہذا یہ اعتراض ہی بے بنیاد ہے اور یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ ملکیت کا اثبات موصی کی طرف سے ہے۔ اور یہ بالکل ایسا ہے جیسے راہن مرہون کو بیچ دے تو یہ بیع مرتہن کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے لیکن جب مرتہن نے بیع کی اجازت دیدی تو بیع کا ثبوت راہن کی طرف سے ہوگا نہ کہ مرتہن کی۔
And similarly, if the bequest was to an heir and the rest [of the heirs] gave permission, its ruling is what we mentioned. And every [transaction] that becomes valid by the permission of the heir, the beneficiary owns it from the testator in our view, and according to al-Shafi'i, from the heir. And the correct is our statement because the cause [of ownership] originated from the testator, and permission is removing an impediment, and possession is not a condition of permission. And it becomes like the mortgagee when he allows the sale of the mortgagor. Commentary: If instead of bequeathing more than one-third, the testator bequeathed to an heir, the same ruling applies: it is suspended upon the permission of the remaining heirs. Now the question is: from whom does the beneficiary become owner? From the testator or from the heir? In our view, he becomes owner from the testator, and according to Imam al-Shafi'i, from the heir. On this, the author said that our statement is correct because the cause of ownership originated from the testator, since he made the bequest. However, in both cases, for that cause to be effective, it is necessary to remove the impediment, and the impediment is the right of the heirs. And the attribution of the ruling is to the cause, not to the condition. (Unless an impediment prevents.) Question: Imam al-Shafi'i says: when the removal of the impediment is found from the side of the heirs, then it is necessary that the heirs also take possession, whereas they have not yet taken possession of this property. So how can the removal of the impediment be valid? Answer: Possession is not a condition for removing the impediment. Therefore, this objection is baseless, and it is established that the ownership is established from the testator. And this is exactly like when a mortgagor sells the mortgaged property: the sale is suspended upon the permission of the mortgagee, but when the mortgagee gives permission, the validity of the sale is attributed to the mortgagor, not to the mortgagee.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a testator makes a bequest to an heir (which is normally prohibited without the permission of other heirs) and the other heirs subsequently give their permission. The author states that the ruling is the same as for a bequest exceeding one-third: it is suspended on their permission. Then it addresses a point of difference with Imam al-Shafi'i: our Hanafi position is that the beneficiary acquires ownership from the testator himself, not from the heirs who grant permission. The reason is that the effective cause (sabab) of ownership is the testator's act of bequeathing; the heirs' permission merely removes the impediment (the heir's right as a potential inheritor). Permission is not a new transfer of ownership. The author supports this with an analogy: if a mortgagor sells the mortgaged property, and the mortgagee later permits the sale, the sale is valid and ownership is transferred from the mortgagor, not from the mortgagee. The passage also refutes a possible objection from al-Shafi'i that removal of the impediment requires possession by the heirs; the Hanafi response is that possession is not a condition for removing an impediment. Thus, the beneficiary's ownership is directly from the testator.

Key Terms
الوصية للوارث (al-wasiyya li'l-warith): A bequest made to an heir, which is invalid unless the other heirs permit.
اجازة الورثة (ijazat al-wurathaa): Permission granted by the heirs after the testator's death, making the bequest valid.
سبب (sabab): The cause that brings about ownership; here, the testator's bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when heirs permit a bequest to an heir, from whom does the beneficiary acquire ownership?
A) From the testator
B) From the heirs collectively
C) From the heir who gave permission
D) It depends on the type of bequest

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a bequest to an heir becomes valid with the permission of the other heirs, but the beneficiary's ownership originates from the testator, not from the permitting heirs.

Bequest to a Killer is Invalid: Hanafi Ruling and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on bequest to a killer with proof and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequests to a killer, explain the proof (hadith and legal reasoning), and compare it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the practical difference.

Core Idea
A bequest to a direct killer is invalid — the killer hastened what Allah delayed.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses whether a bequest to someone who kills the testator is valid. The Hanafi school rules it invalid based on a hadith and the principle of punishing the killer for hastening death. The Shafi'i school permits it. We will examine both sides and understand the legal reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its conditions
Identify the ruling: a bequest to a killer is invalid. Note the killer must be a direct (mubashir) killer, whether intentional or accidental.
The text explicitly includes both intentional and accidental killers.
2
Identify the primary proof (dalil)
Locate the hadith 'La wasiyya li qatil' (no bequest for a killer). Consider its transmission (zanni al-thubut) and its clear negation (qat'i al-dalalah).
The negation of genus indicates absolute prohibition.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
Explain why the killer is deprived: he hastened the receipt of the bequest by killing, whereas Shari'ah delays it until death. This is similar to deprivation of inheritance.
The reasoning applies to both cases of bequest and inheritance.
4
Recognize the Shafi'i contrary view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds bequests to killers are valid. The text does not give his proof, but the dispute is highlighted.
The Hanafi response is that the hadith suffices as proof against Shafi'i.
5
Note the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Hanafi law, if a legatee kills the testator, the bequest is void. Under Shafi'i, it remains valid. Also if the testator makes a bequest to a known killer.
The difference applies whether the bequest is made before or after the killing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۶
قاتل کیلئے وصیت کرنا کیسا ہے
قال ولا تجوز للقاتل عامدا كان او خاطئاً بعد ان كان مباشراً لقوله عليه السلام لا وصية للقاتل ولانه استعجل ما اخره الله تعالى فيحرم الوصية كما يحرم الميراث وقال الشافعى تجوز للقاتل وعلى هذا الخلاف اذا أوصى لرجل ثم انه قتل الموصى تبطل الوصية عندنا وعنده لاتبطل والحجة عليه في الفصلين ما قلناه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور قاتل کے لئے وصیت جائز نہیں ہے خواہ عمد اقتل کرے یا خطاء بعد اس کے کہ وہ مباشر ہو نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان لا وصية لو ارٹ کی وجہ سے اور اس لئے کہ قاتل نے جلدی لینا چاہا اس چیز کو جس کو شریعت نے مؤخر کیا ہے تو اس کو وصیت سے محروم کر دیا جائے گا جیسے وہ میراث سے محروم کر دیا جاتا ہے اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قاتل کے لئے وصیت جائز ہے، اور اسی اختلاف پر ہے جب کہ کسی شخص کے لئے وصیت کی ہو پھر اس شخص نے موصی کو قتل کر دیا ہو تو ہمارے نزدیک وصیت باطل ہو جاتی ہے اور شافعی کے نزدیک وصیت باطل نہیں ہوتی ، اور دونوں صورتوں میں شافعی کے خلاف حجت وہی ہے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔
تشریح موانع ارث کا بیان تفصیل سے درس سراجی میں گزر چکا ہے۔
میں صاف حدیث موجود ہے لا وصية للقاتل۔
قتل عمد ا ہو یا خطاء وہ بالغ ارث ہے اسی طرف جواز وصیت سے بھی مانع ہے کیونکہ اس
دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ قاتل موصی کو قتل کر کے مال وصیت جلدی لینا چاہتا ہے حالانکہ شریعت نے یہ فیصلہ کر دیا ہے کہ وہ مال موصی کی
موت کے بعد ملے گا تو ایسے جلد باز کو بالکلیہ محروم کر دیا جاتا ہے جیسے اس نکتہ کے پیش نظر وارث کو میراث سے محروم کیا گیا ہے۔ اور اگر پہلے سے وصیت کر رکھی تھی اور اب موصی لا نے موصی کو قتل کر دیا تو اب بھی قاتل کے لئے وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی مگر یہ ہمارا مسلک ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں وصیت جائز ہے۔
مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے جو حدیث پیش کی ہے یہ دونوں صورتوں میں امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہے۔
Book of Wills. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary on Hidaya, volume 16. How is a bequest for a killer? He said: It is not permissible for a killer, whether intentionally or mistakenly, after he is a direct killer, because of his saying عليه السلام: 'There is no bequest for a killer' and because he hastened what Allah delayed, so the bequest is prohibited just as inheritance is prohibited. Al-Shafi'i said: A bequest for a killer is permissible. And on this difference, if he made a bequest to a man, then that man killed the testator, the bequest is invalid according to us, but according to him it is not invalid. The proof against him in both cases is what we have said. Translation: Quduri stated: And a bequest is not permissible for the killer, whether he commits intentional murder or accidental, after he is a direct killer, because of the command of the Prophet عليه السلام: 'There is no bequest for a killer' and because the killer hastened to take what the Shari'ah has delayed, so he will be deprived of the bequest just as he is deprived of inheritance. And al-Shafi'i said: A bequest for a killer is permissible. And on this same difference, when a person has made a bequest for someone, then that person killed the testator, then according to us the bequest becomes invalid, and according to al-Shafi'i the bequest does not become invalid. In both cases, the proof against al-Shafi'i is what we have stated. Explanation: The discussion of impediments to inheritance has already passed in detail in Dars Siraji. There is a clear hadith: 'There is no bequest for a killer.' Whether the killing is intentional or accidental, he is a mature heir, and this also prevents the permissibility of a bequest because the second reason is that the killer, by killing the testator, wants to take the bequest property hastily, whereas the Shari'ah has decreed that that property will be received after the testator's death. So such a hasty person is completely deprived, just as from this point of view the heir is deprived of inheritance. And if he had already made a bequest and then the killer killed the testator, then also the bequest becomes invalid for the killer. But this is our school, and according to Imam Shafi'i, in both cases the bequest is permissible. The author says: The hadith we have presented is a proof against Imam Shafi'i in both cases.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. It begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: a bequest to a killer is invalid. The killer must be a direct killer (mubashir), whether intentional or accidental. The proof is the hadith 'La wasiyya li qatil' (no bequest for a killer). The reasoning is that the killer tried to hasten the enjoyment of the property that Allah has delayed until death, so he is deprived as a punishment, similar to the deprivation of inheritance. The text then contrasts the Shafi'i position, which permits bequests to killers. Two scenarios are discussed: (1) making a bequest to a killer, and (2) a bequest made to someone who later kills the testator. In both cases, the Hanafi school invalidates the bequest, while Shafi'i upholds it. The commentary explains that the hadith is clear and that the killer's hastiness is the basis for deprivation. It also notes that even if the legatee kills the testator after the bequest, it is invalid. The author affirms the hadith as the decisive proof against Shafi'i.

Key Terms
قاتل (qatil): The killer of the testator, who directly causes death, whether intentionally or accidentally.
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest or will made by a testator to another, effective after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a bequest made to someone who later kills the testator?
A) The bequest becomes invalid.
B) The bequest remains valid.
C) It is valid only if the killer repents.
D) It is valid only if the killer is an heir.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school invalidates a bequest to a direct killer based on the hadith and the principle that the killer hastened what Allah delayed.

Effect of Heirs' Permission on Bequest to a Killer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on heirs' permission for bequest to a killer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequest to a killer after heirs' permission, explain the two positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and evaluate the evidence for each.

Core Idea
The killer's disqualification from bequest is for the heirs' right, not a punishment—so they can waive it.

In this lesson, we explore an intra-Hanafi disagreement: if the testator makes a bequest to his killer, can the heirs' permission make it valid? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say yes, Abu Yusuf says no. Understanding the reasoning behind each position is key to seeing how Hanafi jurists weigh the rights of heirs versus the gravity of unlawful killing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general prohibition
Recognize that a bequest to a killer is normally invalid, and the killer is also deprived of inheritance.
This is a well-established rule.
2
State the two positions within the Hanafi school
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that heirs' permission validates the bequest; Abu Yusuf holds it remains invalid.
3
Follow each side's proof
Abu Hanifa/Muhammad argue the prohibition is for the heirs' right (benefit returns to them). Abu Yusuf argues it is due to the crime itself (jinaya).
The text includes a qiyas analogy to bequest to an heir.
4
Analyze which proof is stronger
The majority refutes Abu Yusuf by noting that accidental killers are included, so it cannot be purely punitive.
This comparison shows the illa is the heirs' right, not punishment.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The mufta bihi position: if heirs permit, the bequest becomes valid. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The practical difference: in Abu Yusuf's view, the bequest remains invalid regardless.

The ruling on the permission of the heirs, statements of jurists and proofs. And if the heirs permit it, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf said: It is not permissible because his crime remains and the prohibition is due to it. And for both of them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the prohibition is due to the right of the heirs, because the benefit of its invalidity returns to them like the benefit of the invalidity of inheritance, and because they would not be pleased with it for the killer just as they would not be pleased with it for any one of them. Translation: And if the heirs gave permission for the bequest, then according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) it is permissible, and Abu Yusuf said: It is not permissible because the killer's crime remains, and the prevention of the bequest is due to the crime. The proof of the two is that the prevention of the bequest is due to the right of the heirs, because the benefit of its invalidity returns to the heirs, like the benefit of the invalidity of the killer's inheritance returns to the heirs, and because the heirs would not be pleased with the bequest for the killer just as they would not be pleased with it for any one of themselves. Explanation: It has passed previously that the killer is deprived of bequest and also of inheritance, but if the testator made a bequest for the killer and the heirs permitted it, what is the ruling? There is a difference among the respected two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Imam Abu Yusuf. Imam Abu Yusuf says: Even if the heirs permit, the bequest will not be permissible. And the respected two say: Now the bequest will be permissible. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that by the permission of the heirs, the crime of the killer does not end, because of which he was deprived of the bequest, and when that crime does not end, the killer's crime remains as before. The proof of the respected two is that the real secret of depriving the killer of inheritance is for the right of the heirs, because the benefit of the invalidity of the bequest goes to the heirs, just as if the killer is deprived of inheritance, its benefit also goes to the heirs. And just as the heirs are not pleased with a bequest for any one of themselves, similarly they will not be pleased for the killer. But if they are pleased with a bequest for any one of the heirs and permit it, then the bequest becomes valid. Similarly, if the heirs permit for the killer, the bequest becomes valid. And the statement of Imam Abu Yusuf that the killer's deprivation from bequest is by way of punishment is not accepted, because in it the intentional and the mistaken are equal, whereas the mistaken is not deserving of punishment.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a bequest to a killer after the heirs have given permission. The ruling is built on the principle that the killer is normally deprived of both inheritance and bequest. The question is whether the heirs' permission can override that deprivation. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) hold that if the heirs permit, the bequest becomes valid. Their reasoning: the prohibition of the bequest exists to protect the heirs' right, because the invalidity benefits them. Since the heirs have the right to object, they also have the right to waive that objection. Just as they can permit a bequest to one of themselves, they can permit it to the killer. Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that the killer's crime (jinaya) remains, and the prohibition is due to that crime, not merely the heirs' right. Since the crime persists, the bequest remains invalid regardless of the heirs' consent. The commentary further refutes Abu Yusuf's view by noting that if the prohibition were purely punitive, then accidental killers would not be included, but the ruling applies to them equally, showing it is not a punishment but a right of the heirs. Therefore, the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is stronger.

Key Terms
ورثہ (waratha): The heirs of the testator who are entitled to the estate.
اجازة (ijazah): Permission granted by the heirs to allow a bequest that would otherwise be invalid.
جنایت (jinaya): The crime of killing committed by the legatee against the testator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what effect do the heirs' permission have on a bequest to the testator's killer?
A) It makes the bequest valid.
B) It has no effect.
C) It is valid only if the killer repents.
D) It is valid only if the testator wrote a new will.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a bequest to a killer is not a fixed punishment; it is invalid to protect heirs' rights, so heirs' permission can validate it.

Bequest to an Heir is Invalid
Ruling on bequest to an heir with proof and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a bequest to an heir is invalid, identify the hadith proof, and explain why the timing of death determines heirship status.

Core Idea
A bequest to an heir is invalid because the heir already has a fixed right; it would disrupt the inheritance.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a foundational rule of Islamic inheritance: you cannot make a will in favor of someone who is already an heir. The ruling is based on a clear prophetic hadith and is designed to protect the fixed shares that Allah has allotted. We will examine the proof, the critical timing of heirship, and how similar transactions like gifts from a sick person are treated.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the specific ruling: a bequest (wasiyya) to an heir is not permissible (la tajuza). Determine the hukm level: batil (invalid).
The ruling is clear and unconditional in the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the primary proof
Find the hadith cited: 'Verily Allah has given every right-holder his right. Beware: There is no bequest for an heir.' Understand how this explicit negation (la) establishes prohibition.
The hadith is ahad (single narration) with zanni thubut but qat'i dalala according to Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the timing condition
Note that heirship is assessed at the time of the testator's death, not at the time of writing the will. The bequest is a tamlik mudaf (conditional transfer) attached to death.
This principle distinguishes bequests from gifts: the bequest takes effect only after death.
4
Distinguish related transactions
Compare a gift (hiba) from a sick person to an heir: it is treated like a bequest (wasiyya hukman) and limited to one-third. Contrast with an acknowledgment (iqrar) to an heir, which is valid because it is immediate.
The key difference: hiba from a marid is conditional on death; iqrar is binding in life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا تجوز لوارثه لقوله عليه السلام ان الله تعالى اعطى كل ذي حق حقه الا لا وصية للوارث ولانه يتاذى البعض بايثار البعض ففى تجويزه قطعية الرحم ولانه حيف بالحديث الذى رويناه ويعتبر كونه وارثا اوغير وارث وقت الموت لا وقت الوصية لانه تملیک مضاف الى ما بعد الموت وحكمه يثبت بعد الموت والهبة من المريض للوارث فى هذا نظير الوصية لانها وصية حكما حتى تنقذ من الثلث واقرار المريض للوارث على عكسه لانه تصرف في الحال فيعتبر ذلك وقت الاقرار
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور موصی کے وارث کے لئے وصیت جائز نہیں ہے نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فرمان کی وجہ سے اللہ تعالیٰ نے ہر حق والے کو اس کا حق دید یا آگاہ ہو جاؤ کہ وارث کیلئے وصیت نہیں ہے اور اس لئے کہ بعض کو تکلیف ہوگی بعض کو ترجیح دینے کی وجہ سے تو اس کے جائز قرار دینے میں قطع رحمی ہے اور اس لئے کہ یہ وارث کے لئے وصیت کرنا ) حیف و ظلم ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں اور اس کے وارث ہونے یا غیر وارث ہونے کا اعتبار موت کے وقت ہوگا نہ کہ وصیت کے وقت اس لئے کہ وصیت ایسی تملیک ہے جو مابعد الموت کی جانب مضاف ہے اور وصیت کا حکم موت کے بعد ثابت ہوتا ہے اور مریض کی جانب سے وارث کے لئے ہبہ کرنا اس سلسلہ میں ( کہ اس کے وارث ہونے کا بوقت موت اعتبار ہے) وصیت کے مثل ہے اس لئے کہ ہبہ حکم موت کے اعتبار سے وصیت ہے
He said: And it is not permissible for his heir, because of his saying عليه السلام: Verily Allah has given every right-holder his right. Be aware: There is no bequest for an heir. And because some are harmed by giving preference to others, so in permitting it there is cutting of family ties. And because it is wrongdoing according to the hadith we have narrated. And his being an heir or non-heir is considered at the time of death, not at the time of the bequest, because it is a transfer (tamlik) annexed to after death, and its ruling is established after death. And the gift (hiba) from the sick person to his heir in this regard is similar to a bequest because it is a bequest by ruling until it is executed from the one-third. And the acknowledgment (iqrar) of the sick person to the heir is contrary to that, because it is a transaction in the present, so it is considered at the time of acknowledgment. Translation: Quduri said: And a bequest for the heir of the testator is not permissible because of the command of the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم: 'Allah has given every right-holder his right. Be aware: There is no bequest for an heir.' And because some are harmed by preferring others, so in making it permissible there is cutting of family ties. And because it is wrongdoing according to the hadith we have narrated. And his being an heir or non-heir is considered at the time of death, not at the time of the bequest, because a bequest is a transfer annexed to after death, and its ruling is established after death. And a gift from a sick person to his heir in this sequence is similar to a bequest because it is a bequest by ruling, executed from one-third. And the acknowledgment of a sick person to his heir is contrary to that because it is a transaction in the present, so it is considered at the time of acknowledgment.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a bequest to an heir is invalid. The primary proof is the hadith: 'Indeed Allah has given every right-holder his right. Beware, there is no bequest for an heir.' This indicates that since the heir already has a fixed inheritance share, adding a bequest would disturb the distribution and harm other heirs, potentially cutting family ties. The text also clarifies the crucial timing: the determination of whether a person is an heir is made at the time of the testator's death, not at the time the bequest was written. This is because a bequest is a transfer (tamlik) that is contingent upon death (mudaf ila ma ba'd al-mawt). Therefore, if at the time of death the legatee is an heir, the bequest fails. The text then distinguishes two similar transactions: a gift (hiba) from a sick person (marid) to an heir is treated like a bequest (it is considered a bequest in effect and limited to one-third of the estate). Conversely, an acknowledgment (iqrar) by a sick person to an heir is treated differently because it takes effect immediately during life, so heirship is assessed at the time of acknowledgment, not at death.

Key Terms
وارث (warith): An heir who is entitled to a share of the deceased's estate according to Shari'ah.
تملیک مضاف (tamlik mudaf): A transfer of ownership that is conditional upon a future event, here death.
ہبہ (hiba): A gift from a sick person to an heir is treated like a bequest by ruling (hukman).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the status of being an heir determined for the purpose of a bequest?
A) At the time the bequest is made.
B) At the time of the testator's death.
C) At the time of the testator's illness.
D) At the time of the legatee's death.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to an heir is invalid in Hanafi law because the heir already has a fixed share; the determination of heirship is at the time of death.
